801 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Edwards


No. 1-92-0851


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


259 Ill. App. 3d 151; 630 N.E.2d 1266; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 278; 197 Ill. Dec. 142



March 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 19, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD NEVILLE JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which sentenced defendant to concurrent 10-year terms on two armed robbery counts and imposed a 10-year sentence on an aggravated criminal sexual assault conviction, which was to run consecutive to the sentences for armed robbery pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man robbed the victims at gunpoint and raped the female victim. The trial court stated that it was required by statute to give defendant a consecutive sentence because he committed a Class X felony and an aggravated criminal sexual assault. On appeal, defendant challenged the consecutive nature of his sentence. The court vacated the imposition of a consecutive sentence and remanded the case for resentencing. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a) (1989) did not require mandatory consecutive sentences in a case where the crimes were not part of a single objective in a single transaction. The court could not initially make the determination of whether there was a substantial change in the nature of the criminal objective from the armed robbery to the aggravated criminal sexual assault. The trial court was best suited to make such a determination, which was based upon factual considerations. The trial court purported to act pursuant to a provision that it incorrectly interpreted as mandatory when it was in fact discretionary. The court remanded the case to allow the trial court to exercise its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's imposition of a consecutive sentence on the charge of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The court remanded the case for resentencing.

 

802 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Brewer v. Peters


Nos. 5-92-0205, 5-92-0382 (CONSOLIDATED)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


262 Ill. App. 3d 610; 633 N.E.2d 17; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 656; 198 Ill. Dec. 555



March 2, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County. No. 92-MR-2, No. 92-MR-26. Hon. James R. Williamson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 5-92-0205 (No. 92-MR-2), Affirmed. No. 5-92-0382 (No. 92-MR-26), Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates appealed orders of the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois), which dismissed their petitions for writs of mandamus and habeas corpus filed against defendant director of corrections. The inmates alleged that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-6-3(3) (1991) (now Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(3) (1992)), which prohibited an award of good-conduct time to inmates convicted of certain offenses, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were convicted of criminal sexual assault. Section 3-6-3(3) prohibited the director of corrections from awarding good-conduct time to inmates convicted of certain crimes including criminal sexual assault. The trial court dismissed the inmates' petitions for writs of mandamus and habeas corpus. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) the statute did not violate the equal protection or due process clauses of the United States and Illinois constitutions because the classification of offenses were rationally related to a legitimate government need of alleviating prison overcrowding while reducing the risk of public harm from the early release of offenders; (2) mandamus could not be granted because there was no clear duty on the part of the director of corrections to act; (3) the amendment to the statute was not an ex post factor law because it did not criminalize an act that was not an offense when committed, increase punishment for a previously committed offense, or alter rules of evidence to make conviction of a prior act easier; and (4) the trial court had no duty to appoint counsel in a civil action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's orders dismissing the inmates' petitions for writs of mandamus and habeas corpus.

 

803 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Patrasso


No. 1-92-3182


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


271 Ill. App. 3d 1087; 649 N.E.2d 428; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 213; 208 Ill. Dec. 372



February 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 3, 1995. Released for Publication May 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Ronald Banks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant on two counts of attempted murder and two counts of aggravated battery and denied defendant's request for post conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and aggravated battery after he shot two victims at close range. Due to the trial court's findings that the crime was particularly brutal, defendant's sentence was extended as allowed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (1983). After unsuccessfully appealing his convictions and sentence, defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was also denied by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were meritless, particularly where no prejudice was demonstrated. As to the extended sentence handed down, the court found the crimes at issue were of the type for which extended sentencing was proper. Certain claims by defendant, including his claim that the trial court erred in imposing an extended term sentence without notifying him of an intention to do so, were res judicata since defendant raised and the court addressed these same issues on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the sentence imposed by the trial court.

 

804 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Calvert


No. 5-92-0501


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


258 Ill. App. 3d 504; 629 N.E.2d 1154; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 172; 196 Ill. Dec. 310



February 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. No. 91-CF-77. Honorable Joseph L. Fribley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (Illinois), which convicted him after a jury trial of harassment of a witness in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 32-4a (1991). The jury acquitted defendant of charge aggravated assault arising from the same incident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a deputy sheriff, confronted a police dispatcher who had testified against him in an earlier proceeding. On appeal, the court held that evidence that defendant came to the dispatcher's office for a confrontation after verifying that she was on duty, and evidence of his shouting, threats, gestures, a disparity in size, and the fear and upset he caused, were more than sufficient to sustain the conviction by a jury that had the opportunity to listen to the evidence and to observe and assess the witnesses. The court held that the First Amendment did not protect all types of speech and that the harassment statute was not overbroad because it protected a defined class from specific behavior and it was justified by a legitimate need of society to protect witnesses. The court held the statute's wording was sufficiently clear to put a person of average intelligence on notice of the proscribed conduct, so it was not void for vagueness. The court found that there could not be a legitimate expectation of privacy in a shouting match in a municipal building and that the Eavesdropping Act was not violated by the inadvertent recording of the incident on police equipment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of defendant, a deputy sheriff, for harassing a witness, a police dispatcher, in a confrontation in a municipal building after the dispatcher had testified against him in an earlier proceeding.

 

805 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hull (In re General Order of March 15, 1993)


1-93-1348


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


258 Ill. App. 3d 13; 629 N.E.2d 673; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 97; 196 Ill. Dec. 128



February 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ARTHUR ROSENBLUM, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney appealed from an order of a judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that barred the attorney from appearing in his courtroom on any case.


OVERVIEW: The attorney contended that the circuit court's order was based upon § 6 of an act, codified at 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/6 (1992), and that the act impermissibly encroached upon the exclusive prerogative of the state's supreme court to regulate the legal profession. The state argued that the judge had inherent power to control his courtroom and to ensure that attorneys appearing before him exhibit proper respect for the authority of the court and that the attorney lacked standing to contest the constitutionality of § 205/6. The court vacated the circuit court's order because the act was an unconstitutional encroachment upon the supreme court's exclusive authority to punish or to disbar an attorney. The court found that the circuit court did not have inherent power to limit the practice of the attorney in his court and its authority to do so could only have come from the act; thus, the attorney had standing to challenge the act's constitutionality. The court concluded that the supreme court's preemption of all authority having to do with attorney discipline rendered the act unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the circuit court's order that barred the attorney from practicing before a judge of that court.

 

806 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Myles


No. 1-91-1477


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


257 Ill. App. 3d 872; 629 N.E.2d 648; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 124; 196 Ill. Dec. 103



January 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 18, 1994. As Corrected May 24, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael B. Getty Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, rejected defendant's self-defense claim, found him guilty of first degree murder, and sentenced him to 35 years in the state penitentiary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed an off-duty police officer. Defendant admitted that he shot the officer but alleged that he acted in self-defense. In a bench trial, the trial court rejected defendant's self-defense claim and found him guilty of first degree murder. The court then sentenced defendant to 35 years. On appeal, defendant argued 1) the state failed to disprove his claim of self-defense; 2) the trial court committed reversible error in convicting defendant of first degree murder in light of mitigating evidence; 3) the trial court abused its discretion in allowing the state to reopen its case in order to establish corpus delicti; 4) the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing defendant to 35 years; and 5) the Illinois homicide statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed both the conviction and the sentence, holding that 1) the state presented more than sufficient evidence to rebut self-defense; 2) there was nothing inconsistent with a finding that defendant "over-reacted" and a finding of first-degree murder; 3) the state proved corpus delicti before its case was reopened; 4) the sentence was not excessive, and 5) the murder statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first degree murder and his 35-year sentence were affirmed.

 

807 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. DePalma


No. 2-92-0179


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


256 Ill. App. 3d 206; 627 N.E.2d 1236; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 88; 194 Ill. Dec. 594


November 19, 1993, Submitted  
January 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 3, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 92-CF-14. Honorable John J. Nelligan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that convicted him of possessing a vehicle with knowledge that the vehicle's identification number (VIN) had been removed, a violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-103(a)(4), (b) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found sleeping in his car by a police officer who discovered that the car, which defendant had recently purchased, was missing its VIN plates. Defendant explained that the car was stolen from its previous owner, and a check revealed that the car had been recovered and the State did not dispute that defendant was the lawful owner of the car. Defendant contended that § 4-103(a)(4) was overly broad because it criminalized innocent conduct, and in conjunction with § 4-103(b), which made the offense a class 2 felony, violated the constitutional guarantees of due process and proportionate penalties. The court held that the statute was constitutional but only if the knowledge requirement was construed to mean "criminal knowledge." Thus, because the evidence in the record was insufficient to show that defendant possessed this requisite criminal intent, his conviction could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

Jahn v. Troy Fire Protection Dist.


No. 3-93-0119


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


255 Ill. App. 3d 933; 627 N.E.2d 1216; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 91; 194 Ill. Dec. 574


October 21, 1993, Submitted  
January 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 90-L-16773. Honorable Herman H. Haase Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fire protection district was granted a permissive interlocutory appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), which denied their motions to dismiss appellee state employee's claims for injuries based on the argument that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Tort Immunity Act) granted them immunity.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured by an accident caused by firemen from the district while they were on duty. The district argued that the Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 10/5-106 (1992), and the Fire Fighter Liability Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 75/1 (1992), were in direct conflict. The district argued that § 10/5-106 provided immunity for public employees responding to emergency calls, but that § 75/1 imposed liability upon fire protection districts thereby discriminating against the districts. The court held that the district had standing to bring the cause of action because they were being discriminated against. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court and dismissed the third count of the amended complaint. The court held that where two statutes conflicted the later enacted statute was said to take precedence over the older statute and that the dismissed count was based on a statute that had been repealed, therefore, dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, dismissed the third count of the employee's amended complaint, and remanded the cause for further action.

 

809 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilson


No. 1-91-3399


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


257 Ill. App. 3d 826; 629 N.E.2d 582; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 52; 196 Ill. Dec. 37



January 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JOHN E. MORRISSEY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of armed robbery and sentenced him to natural life imprisonment under the Illinois Habitual Criminal Act (Act), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: At his trial for robbery, defendant objected to the introduction of evidence relating to the circumstances of his arrest. That evidence consisted of testimony that defendant had held a gun on a woman and had shot at police who were attempting to arrest him. The evidence was admitted, and defendant was convicted and sentenced to natural life imprisonment under the Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1 (1992). The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The trial judge's refusal to exclude the evidence relating to defendant's arrest did not deprive defendant of a fair trial and was not an abuse of discretion. Even though it included evidence regarding other crimes, the evidence was admissible to show identity, to place defendant with a gun in his hand in close proximity and time to the offense charged, and to show absence of mistake as well as the circumstances of his arrest. The probative effect of the evidence outweighed its prejudicial effect and was subject to a limiting instruction. The Act did not violate federal or state constitutional due process rights, was not an ex post facto law, and did not place defendant in double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of armed robbery and sentencing him to natural life imprisonment under the Act was affirmed.

Kromeich v. City of Chicago


No. 1-92-0688


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


258 Ill. App. 3d 606; 630 N.E.2d 913; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 14; 196 Ill. Dec. 748



January 12, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 3, 1994. Released for Publication April 19, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994. As Corrected August 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Glynn Elliott, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied recovery in claimant's replevin action to return nine firearms seized by police officers of defendant city pursuant to Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 8-20.


OVERVIEW: Investigating an anonymous tip of unregistered guns, city police officers went to claimant's temporary residence, conducted a consent search, and seized various unregistered weapons. Claimant appealed when the circuit court determined that the weapons were contraband per se and entered judgment for the city in claimant's replevin action. The court held that Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 8-20-040 was not unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the ordinance did not involve constitutionally protected rights, was reasonably clear in its application to claimant, and that the ordinance's language was unambiguous and self-explanatory. Contrary to the claimant's assertion, the court further ruled that the ordinance did not delegate to the police superintendent the council's inherent function of determining what the law should have been and to whom it should have been applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that denied recovery in claimant's replevin action for the return of unregistered firearms.

 

811 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dominguez


No. 2-92-0429


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


255 Ill. App. 3d 995; 626 N.E.2d 775; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 2; 193 Ill. Dec. 465


December 16, 1993, Submitted  
January 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-1722. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated battery. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) sentenced him to an extended term of 10 years' imprisonment. The trial court found two of the factors justifying an extended-term sentence to be applicable. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his codefendants severely beat a fellow gang member when he indicated a desire to leave the gang. The gang rules required that any member who desired to leave had to undergo a beating. The victim was beaten into a coma and suffered permanent brain damage. The trial court found that defendant committed the offense in a brutal and heinous manner indicative of wanton cruelty pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(2) (1992) and that defendant committed the offense as part of a gang activity pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(6) (1992). The court modified the sentence to grant defendant credit for time served and then affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 5-5-3.2(b)(2) was unconstitutionally vague and overly broad. The court held that non-capital cases were analyzed under the Due Process Clause, and that a vagueness challenge under that clause could be overcome when the defendant's conduct clearly fell within the statutory definition. Here, defendant's conduct was clearly heinous and brutal. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in weighing the aggravating and mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment to give defendant credit for time served and then the court affirmed the judgment as modified. The court thereafter remanded the cause.

 

812 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 5-92-0831


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


255 Ill. App. 3d 482; 625 N.E.2d 1213; 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 4; 193 Ill. Dec. 92



January 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wayne County. No. 91-MC-2. Honorable Donald E. Garrison, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Wayne County (Illinois) that affirmed a decision by defendant Zoning Board of Appeals to rescind a permit issued to her that would have allowed her to place a mobile home on a lot.


OVERVIEW: The owner possessed two contiguous lots, and the city approved her application for a permit to place a mobile home on one of those lots. When defendant citizens filed a complaint with the board and asked for a recission of the permit, the owner filed a request with the city to combine her two lots to satisfy the acreage requirements for zoning purposes. The board rescinded the permit, and the trial court entered judgment against the owner. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in finding that the owner was not permitted to "tack" her lots because the lots were already improved with an existing structure; thus, the combining of such lots for zoning purposes freed no open space for use by another structure as required by Fairfield, Ill., Municipal Zoning Code §§ 28.040.030, 28.12.030 (1988). The trial court did not exceed its authority by considering the lot width even though that issue had not been specifically raised by defendants. The owner waived the issue of constitutionality and failed to raise the issue of detrimental reliance at the initial hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that upheld a decision by the board to rescind a permit issued to the owner that would have allowed her to place a mobile home on a lot.

In re Marriage of T.H.


No. 5-92-0422


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


255 Ill. App. 3d 247; 626 N.E.2d 403; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 2033; 193 Ill. Dec. 370



December 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. Nos. 90-D-675, 91-J-411, 91-F-61. Honorable Robert Hennessey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which terminated his parental rights with respect to his two minor children and denied his motion to stay the proceedings to terminate his parental rights pending disposition of a petition filed by petitioners, brother and sister-in-law, to adopt the children with appellant's consent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father was convicted of the murder of decedent mother with whom appellant had two children. The trial court appointed a guardian ad litem, who filed a petition pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 802-13 (1989) to terminate father's parental rights with respect to the children. It was alleged that appellant was an unfit person within the meaning of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501 (1989). Appellant's brother and sister-in-law filed a petition to adopt the two children that had appellant's final and irrevocable consent to the adoption attached. Subsequently, decedent's sister filed a petition to adopt the children. The guardian ad litem filed a motion for summary judgment. Appellant filed a petition to stay the proceedings. Appellant's motion to stay was denied, and the guardian's motion for summary judgment was granted. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that appellant's parental rights were terminated based on a number of factors, including his murder of the mother of his children in an exceptionally brutal and heinous fashion, which murder was proved through evidence of his conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied appellant father's motion to stay proceedings on the petition to terminate his parental rights and granting summary judgment terminating his parental rights to his two children. The court held that appellant's parental rights were terminated based on a number of factors, including his murder of the mother of his children in an exceptionally brutal and heinous fashion.

 

814 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Diversified Realty Group v. Davis


No. 1-92-2861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


257 Ill. App. 3d 417; 628 N.E.2d 1081; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 2101; 195 Ill. Dec. 617



December 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 9, 1994. As Corrected March 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: In the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Michael W. Stuttley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) that granted defendant tenant's motion for summary judgment, denied plaintiff's cross-motion for summary judgment, and denied plaintiff's petition for rehearing. Plaintiff had filed an action for possession of the premises claiming that defendant had breached the terms of her lease agreement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord served defendant tenant with a notice of termination for an alleged breach of defendant's lease after defendant's son had been arrested for alleged possession of drug paraphernalia found in defendant's federally subsidized apartment. The charges against defendant's son were eventually dropped because the items might have belonged to a stepson guest. Defendant was not home at the time of the search and arrest. Plaintiff filed the action for possession of the premises after defendant failed to vacate the premises as instructed. The lower court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, denied plaintiff's cross-motion for summary judgment, and denied plaintiff's petition for a rehearing. The court affirmed the lower court. The court held that under the terms of defendant's lease, plaintiff was not permitted to evict her without a showing of material non-compliance and a showing that the termination was for good cause. Defendant could not be convicted when the facts showed that defendant was without knowledge or fault concerning the alleged criminal conduct of her stepson guest. The court did not address defendant's constitutional claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant tenant. Defendant could not be evicted by plaintiff landlord for an alleged violation of the terms of her lease agreement when defendant was not at fault for and had no knowledge of her guest's alleged criminal conduct.

People v. Kluppelberg


1-90-1114


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


257 Ill. App. 3d 516; 628 N.E.2d 908; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1944; 195 Ill. Dec. 444



December 28, 1993, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Loretta Hall Morgan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County found defendant guilty of murder and arson and sentenced him to natural life in prison for murder with concurrent terms of 14 years for the 3 counts of arson. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a new trial because evidence was presented at the post-trial motion hearing that cast doubt on a witness' veracity. The court found that the trial court was well within its discretion in refusing to grant a new trial. Defendant also contended that defense counsel was ineffective in failing to investigate these matters. The court found that defendant's counsel's performance did not fall below the objective standard of reasonableness and that defendant was not prejudiced. The court determined that witness statements that were admitted into evidence did not violate the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine. Furthermore, the court found no error in any of the trial court's evidentiary determinations. The court concluded that defendant received a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

In re General Order of October 11, 1990


No. 1-90-3675


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


256 Ill. App. 3d 693; 628 N.E.2d 786; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1918; 195 Ill. Dec. 322



December 22, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Arthur Hamilton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public defender challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion to vacate or stay a general order concerning procedures for the treatment of sick or injured minors.


OVERVIEW: The public defender argued that the juvenile judge was without authority to issue an order that exceeded its rulemaking power. The court reversed the judgment that denied the public defender's motion. The court set aside and vacated the general order as an improper exercise of legislative power by the judiciary. The court addressed the issue despite the absence of an actual case involving a minor. Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970) provided that the legislative, executive, and judicial branches were separate and that no branch could exercise powers properly belonging to another. The court held that the general order created a law, and therefore the circuit court improperly exercised legislative power. The court found that Illinois law provided sufficient mechanisms to provide all urgent medical needs of minors without the general order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied the public defender's motion to vacate or stay a general order. The court set aside and vacated the general order and held that the circuit court exceeded its power, which was limited to issuing orders concerning administrative matters of the juvenile court.

 

818 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ratzke


No. 2-91-1440


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


253 Ill. App. 3d 1054; 625 N.E.2d 1004; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1883; 192 Ill. Dec. 849


November 23, 1993, Submitted  
December 21, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 26, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-951. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) after his conviction for first-degree murder. The trial court found that the murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty and the aggravating factor in § 9-1(b)(6) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b)(6) (1989), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-1(b)(6) (1992), was present.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend carjacked the victim at gunpoint, drove the victim to a location where, after stepping out of the car, the victim was shot and then struck by the car when the victim tried to run away. While lying in the road, the victim was struck by another vehicle and died. The jury determined that defendant was not eligible for the death penalty and he was sentenced by the court to a natural-life term in prison based on a finding that the § 9-1(b)(6) aggravating factor was present. The court affirmed and held that (1) statutory accountability principles that incorporated the "common-design" rule made a defendant responsible for a wide range of consequences for criminal acts; (2) defendant's conduct was comparable to conduct in other cases where extended-term or natural-life sentences were upheld; (3) there was no showing that the victim impact statements improperly influenced the sentence; and (4) the trial court did consider defendant's show of remorse and the evidence of defendant's emotional or mental condition but determined that it deserved little weight in the sentence and the evidence did not preclude a finding of exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's sentence of a natural-life prison term against defendant who had been convicted of first-degree murder, based on a finding that a certain statutory factor was present.

 

819 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Union Bank v. Blackstone Sunbury-Nevada Grain Co.


NO. 4-92-0985


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


254 Ill. App. 3d 206; 627 N.E.2d 385; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1867; 194 Ill. Dec. 269


October 19, 1993, Oral Argument Held  
December 16, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 28, 1994. Petition for Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication February 10, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court. County of Livingston. No. 91MR68. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee bank filed an action in the Circuit Court, County of Livingston (Illinois) seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against appellants, State of Illinois Department of Agriculture, Bureau of Warehouses (department) and a corporation. After a bench trial, the trial court found for the bank. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bank loaned money to the corporation to operate a grain elevator. The department suspended the corporation's licenses and assumed control of the corporation. The bank asserted a lien over the corporation's accounts receivable. But the department claimed a superior lien under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 40.23 (1991). The bank elected not to pursue its administrative remedies under Ill. Admin. Code tit. 8, §§ 1,10-1.500 (1991). The trial court ruled that the bank's lien had priority. The court held that a party aggrieved by administrative action had to exhaust its administrative remedies before seeking judicial review. Although the department failed to raise in the trial court the issue of exhaustion of administrative remedies, the issue was not waived. Waiver was not a limitation on the court's jurisdiction. Exhaustion was not required where a statute was attacked on its face. But the bank challenged only the department's interpretation and application of the law, not the constitutionality of the law on its face. Even clear indications that the department would rule adversely to the bank did not render exhaustion of administrative remedies futile.


OUTCOME: The court, in the bank's action for declaratory and injunctive relief, reversed the trial court's order that the bank's lien was superior to that of the department.

 

820 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Gorgees v. Daley


No. 1-91-1374


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


256 Ill. App. 3d 143; 628 N.E.2d 721; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1875; 195 Ill. Dec. 257



December 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edward C. Hofert, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant owner appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant Liquor Appeal Commission of the City of Chicago (commission), which affirmed the Mayor's License Commission's decision, which denied him a liquor license. The restaurant owner had brought his action against the commission and defendant mayor pursuant to Ill. Code Civ. P., 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-101.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant owner opened his business, and then sought a liquor license but was ultimately denied by the commission. The restaurant owner sought judicial review, and the trial court affirmed the decision of the commission. The restaurant owner appealed, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision of the trial court. The court held that the restaurant owner did not prove the two prerequisites necessary to invoke the doctrine of equitable estoppel. There was no evidence that the restaurant owner relied upon the city's actions to his detriment. The restaurant owner did not demonstrate that, in the absence of estoppel, he would suffer a substantial loss. The court held that the trial court erred when it did not address the restaurant owner's argument that 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-11 was unconstitutional. The court found that 5/6-11 was not unreasonable in requiring that a school be 100 feet from an establishment that served liquor where the population of the city was more than 500,000 persons. The legislature could have reasonably concluded that there was a greater likelihood of school children coming into contact with intoxicated individuals or alcohol.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the decision of the trial court, which affirmed the commission's decision, which had denied the restaurant owner a liquor license. The court reversed in part the order of the trial court, which failed to address the constitutionality of a statute.

Midland Enters. v. City of Elmhurst


No. 2-91-0300


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


624 N.E.2d 913; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1835; 191 Ill. Dec. 725


March 3, 1992, Submitted  
December 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 88-CH-150. Honorable Carl F. J. Henninger, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state division of water resources (DWR) appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois), which denied statutory injunctive relief. The DWR sought a mandatory injunction against plaintiff corporation to remove two berms and a lift station that it constructed adjacent to its properties along a creek.


OVERVIEW: The corporation built a shopping center along a creek. The corporation constructed a berm at the shopping center without a permit. The corporation later built a hotel and applied for a permit to continue the berm. The corporation brought the instant action when its occupancy permit for the hotel was denied and the DWR counterclaimed for an injunction to compel the corporation to remove both berms, for the shopping center and for the hotel. The court first held that DWR had statutory power to make administrative decisions to designate floodplain and issue permits under the section 18f of the Rivers Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 65f (1987). Exhaustion of administrative remedies was required in accordance with the Administrative Review Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 19, para. 75a (1987). The court affirmed the trial court's denial of an injunction as it pertained to the shopping center berm because removing the berm could be disastrous for the shopping center and because the berm was constructed years earlier. However, the court reversed the denial of an injunction as it pertained to the hotel berm because DWR had full administrative authority to regulate floodplains.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction relating to the hotel berm and reversed the injunction relating to the shopping center berm. Regarding the details of the permit application, the court held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to review the permit conditions because the corporation failed to seek review from DWR pursuant to the Administrative Review Law within the designated 35-day period.

People v. Culpepper


NO. 4-92-0935


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


254 Ill. App. 3d 215; 625 N.E.2d 868; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1815; 192 Ill. Dec. 713



December 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 26, 1994. As Corrected January 28, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court. County of Edgar. No. 92TR1246. Honorable H. Dean Andrews, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver filed a petition pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2 para. 2-118.1 (1991) and sought recission of her license suspension. The Circuit Court of Edgar County (Illinois) granted recission of the driver's suspension. Plaintiff state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The driver was charged with driving under the influence and she was sent a notice that her driver's license had been suspended pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(2). The driver alleged that she was traveling along a road and swerved into a culvert to avoid a car in her lane. She was knocked unconscious but claimed that she had consumed two drinks. At the hospital, she was given medicines and had blood drawn, before being taken to the intensive-care ward, at the request of the responding officer because he detected alcohol. The court determined that the driver had the burden of proving that the suspension should be rescinded because she was the one who suffered the suspension. The court held that the circuit court's ruling which denied the state's motion for a finding and that the state made a prima facie case was not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence because there was a concern with the validity of the blood test. The court gave great deference to the circuit court's ruling because it had the benefit to determine the credibility of the witnesses and if the prima facie case was made, the proof of the validity of the blood test clearly failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the recission of the driver's license suspension.

People v. Rushton


Nos. 2-92-0852, 2-92-0978 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


254 Ill. App. 3d 156; 626 N.E.2d 1378; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1799; 193 Ill. Dec. 827


November 4, 1993, Submitted  
December 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 10, 1994. Released for Publication February 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-2364. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) convicted defendant for reckless homicide under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3 (1992) and sentenced him to five years imprisonment pursuant to the enhancement provision of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3(e) (1992).


OVERVIEW: While traveling northbound, the defendant's vehicle collided head-on with an automobile travelling southbound. The defendant had no recollection of the accident and was uncooperative at the hospital. There was evidence of a report of defendant's blood alcohol level and testimony that he smelled of alcohol, but the trial court failed to make a requisite finding of intoxication beyond a reasonable doubt. On appeal, the court found that under the instructions given, it was possible for the jury to have concluded that the defendant had recklessly driven his vehicle across the center line and into the oncoming lane of traffic even if it was not convinced that he had been under the influence of alcohol. Although the verdict necessarily incorporated a finding of reckless driving, it did not necessarily establish that the defendant was proven beyond a reasonable doubt to have been under the influence. Absent such a determination, the court had to conclude that the trial court committed reversible error in sentencing defendant pursuant to the enhanced penalty provision of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3(e) (1992), rather than under the standard penalty range of two to five years' imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for reckless homicide but vacated his five-year sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing as a Class 3 felony.

People v. McPhee


1-91-2908


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


256 Ill. App. 3d 102; 628 N.E.2d 523; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1751; 195 Ill. Dec. 59



November 29, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook. Honorable Shelvin Singer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that found him guilty of possession with the intent to deliver more than 15 and less than 100 grams of a controlled substance containing cocaine and sentenced him to prison. Defendant argued that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to effective assistance was denied, his motion to suppress should have been granted, resentencing was necessary, and improper closing remarks.


OVERVIEW: A narcotics detection dog alerted the detective to an envelope addressed to defendant, and after further investigation, the substance within the envelope tested positive for cocaine. The trial court denied defendant's pretrial motions to suppress, which claimed that the detective did not have probable cause or reasonable suspicion to seize the envelope. Defendant was subsequently found guilty of possession with the intent to deliver more than 15 and less than 100 grams of a controlled substance containing cocaine and sentenced to prison. The court found that the failure to file a pretrial motion to quash defendant's arrest rose to the level of ineffective assistance of counsel because warrant was limited to the envelope and the police searched defendant's house. The court also found that the motion to suppress should have been granted because the detective admitted that there was nothing unusual about the envelope that supported a reasonable, articulable suspicion that the envelope contained contraband. The testimony of defendant's minor daughter, who witnessed defendant's arrest should have been admitted. The court reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that the detective did not have sufficient facts to support a reasonable, articulable suspicion that the envelope at issue contained contraband. The court also held that defendant had a constitutional right to present testimony from his minor daughter, who witnessed defendant's arrest. The court did not address defendant's contention regarding improper remarks during closing argument.

People v. Belton


No. 1-91-2916


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) defendant was convicted of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault, one count of home invasion, and one count of armed robbery. The trial court imposed two 20-year sentences of imprisonment for aggravated criminal sexual assault, to be served consecutively, and a concurrent 20-year term of imprisonment for home invasion was imposed, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was chased into an apartment building by the victim's father and neighbors, and subsequently arrested by police. In affirming the denial of his motion to quash his arrest, the court held that there was probable cause to arrest defendant based upon the fact that a crime had been committed, and a victim had positively identified defendant. The court affirmed defendant's mandatory consecutive sentences, noting that he had asked the court to rule on the propriety of such sentences based upon the outcome of another pending appeal, and had waived any other argument regarding the issue by relying solely on the outcome of that decision and not advancing any further arguments or citation to authority for the trial court to consider. The court stated that a reviewing court was not simply a depository into which the appealing party could dump the burden of argument and research. In addition, the court stated that a constitutional challenge to the mandatory consecutive sentences applied in the case would necessarily have failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to quash his arrest, affirmed his convictions, and affirmed the mandatory consecutive sentences imposed by the trial court.

People v. Toliver


No. 2-91-1195


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 1092; 623 N.E.2d 880; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1675; 191 Ill. Dec. 290


October 25, 1993, Submitted  
November 10, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-1182. Honorable Peter M. Trobe, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count of home invasion and three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault based on bodily harm, and sentenced him to concurrent terms of imprisonment on the home invasion and one aggravated assault counts, and to concurrent terms of imprisonment on the other two aggravated assault counts, to run consecutively to other two sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into a home and sexually assaulted the female occupant three times. He was convicted of one count of home invasion and three counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault premised on bodily harm, and was sentenced to concurrent prison terms on the home invasion and one aggravated assault count, and to concurrent prison terms on the other two aggravated assault counts, to run consecutively to other two sentences. Defendant appealed, claiming that the mandatory imposition of consecutive sentences under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) (1992) violated constitutional equal protection and due process requirements. The court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the sentences and remanded for resentencing. The challenged statute, which was applicable to defendant's commission of three sexual assaults, did not offend principles of equal protection and due process because its classifications were not arbitrary and it bore a rational relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose. However, the trial court imposed a combination of concurrent and consecutive sentences that appeared to be inconsistent with the statute, and gave no explanation for its action in the record.


OUTCOME: The convictions on all counts were affirmed, the sentences were vacated, and the cause was remanded to the trial court with directions to impose de novo new sentences consistent with the court's opinion, and to make a clear record of the reasons for its findings and determinations in imposing the sentences.

People v. Morales


Nos. 2-92-0098 & 2-92-0154 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 1001; 623 N.E.2d 864; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1669; 191 Ill. Dec. 274

November 9, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-1722. Honorable William D. Block, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), in which they were convicted of aggravated battery, causing great bodily harm. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(a) (1991), now codified, as amended, at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4(a). One of the two defendants also appealed from the trial court's imposition of the maximum extended term of 10 years.


OVERVIEW: At a joint bench trial defendants, two gang members, were convicted of aggravated battery causing great bodily harm. The victim was also a former gang member who was made to undergo a three-minute "violation," or beating, in order to be released from gang membership. The first issue raised by defendants on appeal is whether the state's evidence failed to prove either defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt under the theory of accountability. The court affirmed both defendants' convictions and found no error in the record. The court held that the state's evidence was sufficient to prove defendants guilty beyond a reasonable doubt under the theory of accountability. Although the testimony varied as to the details of the procedure, it was not disputed that the gang members intended to "violate" those members wishing to leave the gang. There is no question that the victim was beaten and sustained great bodily harm. It was also undisputed that both defendants were present during the commission of the beating. The court upheld the sentences and stated that a challenge to proportionality of extended sentences only applied to death penalty cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences for aggravated battery causing great bodily harm, and upheld the judgments of the circuit court, having found no error.

People v. Turnage


No. 2-91-0861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 485; 622 N.E.2d 871; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1615; 190 Ill. Dec. 841


August 31, 1993, Submitted  
October 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 1993. Supplemental Concurring Opinion Dated January 4, 1994. Supplemental Concurring Opinion Withdrawn December 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 91-CF-434. Honorable Melvin E. Dunn, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which quashed defendant's arrest and suppressed the evidence seized pursuant to that arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. The day after defendant was released on bail, the trial court, relying on the grand jury's finding of probable cause, issued a second warrant for his arrest on the same charge. Defendant was rearrested, and a search of his car turned up evidence which formed the basis of the charges herein. The trial court quashed the arrest and suppressed the evidence. The state appealed. The court affirmed the order. No statute authorized the trial court, which already had jurisdiction over defendant, to issue a warrant for his arrest merely because he was indicted in the same court for the same offense. Thus, the arrest warrant was invalid. The trial court erred in holding that the "good-faith" doctrine was inapplicable to the warrant because the warrant was based upon a grand jury's determination of probable cause. Regardless, the good-faith exception did not apply. The procurement and execution of the first warrant was historical facts which the officers knew or should have known at the time the second warrant was issued. Thus, the officers had no reasonable grounds to believe that the warrant was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order quashing defendant's arrest and suppressing the evidence seized pursuant to that arrest.

People v. Franzen

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied his petition for post conviction relief after he was convicted of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for criminal sexual assault was affirmed by the court on direct appeal. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1992), alleging numerous violations of his constitutional rights. Moreover, the court concluded that defendant's other claims were also without merit.

People v. Gassman


No. 2-91-1136


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 681; 622 N.E.2d 845; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1608; 190 Ill. Dec. 815


September 29, 1993, Submitted  
October 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CF-2422. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicted defendant of several crimes, including driving with any amount of a drug in his blood or urine resulting from the unlawful use or consumption of cannabis or a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501(a)(5) (1990), 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(a)(5) (1992). Defendant appealed and contended that § 11-501(a)(5) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested, he admitted that he had been smoking marijuana and he underwent a blood and urine test, which revealed a small amount of cannabis. Defendant contended that § 11-501(a)(5) was unconstitutional because it failed to specify a requisite mental state as an element of the offense, violated due process and equal protection guarantees, and was vague. The court held that (1) defendant had standing to challenge § 11-501(a)(5); (2) the trial court was not required to determine defendant's state of mind at the time of the offense because § 11-501(a)(5) imposed strict liability and defendant's intent was immaterial to the question of guilt; (3) the provision was not void for vagueness because it clearly prohibited individuals from driving with any amount of a controlled substance unlawfully in their systems and punished only those who had already knowingly ingested illegal substances; and (4) the provision did not violate due process or equal protection guarantees because it was rationally related to the State's legitimate interest in protecting the public from drivers whose driving ability was impaired by the consumption of controlled substances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Farm Credit Bank v. Schwarm


No. 5-93-0054


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 205; 622 N.E.2d 97; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1609; 190 Ill. Dec. 687



October 18, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. No. 92-CH-7. Honorable William D. Kelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Fayette County (Illinois), which evicted him from his farm and granted possession of it to plaintiff creditor, a farm credit bank.


OVERVIEW: The notice informing the debtor of the mortgage foreclosure hearing contained a typographical error as to the year. The debtor filed a pleading entitled an answer in abatement, in which he contended that the creditor was a foreign corporation that lacked the capacity to bring the action. The trial court ordered the answer in abatement stricken and entered a judgment of foreclosure. The debtor's motions to vacate or modify the judgment of foreclosure were denied. The court affirmed, finding that defendant appeared in court on the proper date and was not prejudiced by the typographical error. Moreover, the creditor, as a federally chartered corporation, was not a foreign corporation under Illinois law and was not required to obtain a certificate of authority from the state to transact business or sue in Illinois. The court held that the answer in abatement was properly stricken because it was an unverified document. The court held that prospective application of a new procedural rule was permissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the trial court granting judgment for the creditor, striking the debtor's answer in abatement, and denying the debtor's motion to vacate.

 

833 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garland


No. 1-91-2810


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


254 Ill. App. 3d 827; 627 N.E.2d 377; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1593; 194 Ill. Dec. 261



October 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 3, 1993. Released for Publication February 16, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied April 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LORETTA HALL MORGAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of multiple counts of armed robbery and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of having committed two counts of armed robbery at a Wendy's restaurant while with two accomplices. After the trial court denied a post-trial motion for a new trial that defense counsel had filed, the trial court was presented with a pro se motion from defendant entitled "Petition for Compulsory Process," which the trial court refused to consider. On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court improperly omitted the issue of mental state from the jury instructions. The court, in affirming the trial court's judgment, rejected this contention, holding that because armed robbery was a general intent crime, a particular mental state was not a necessary element of the crime. For general intent crimes, a mental state of intent, knowledge, or recklessness was necessarily implied by the circumstances of the crime. Further, the court ruled that even if the trial court's failure to consider defendant's post-trial petition as an ineffective assistance of counsel claim constituted error, it was harmless error because it related to failure to call a witness, a matter of trial strategy which did not support an ineffective assistance claim.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment of conviction to reflect the fact that one of the charges of armed robbery was nolle prossed and, as so modified, affirmed the judgment.

Northern Ill. Home Builders Ass'n v. County of Du Page


No. 2-92-0963


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 494; 621 N.E.2d 1012; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1546; 190 Ill. Dec. 559


September 21, 1993, Submitted  
October 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 89-MR-0313. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, builders association, builders, and developers, sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which rendered judgment in favor of defendants, county and county official, in plaintiffs' action to have the state legislation enabling the county to establish impact fees, and the ordinance passed pursuant thereto, declared unconstitutional and to have the county refund impact fees already assessed.


OVERVIEW: The county passed an impact fee ordinance pursuant to former Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 5-608(a) (1987) and later amended it to comply with the Road Improvement Impact Fee Law, 605 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-901 et seq. (1992). The court found that (1) the impact fees were not takings in violation of the Fifth Amendment because the formula used by the county imposed fees only on the road improvement costs generated by the new development and the new developments received a direct and material benefit from the road improvements; (2) the impact fees did not violate the Uniformity Clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), because there was a real and substantial difference between those new developments that generated additional traffic and the existing developments that did not; (3) the enabling legislation was not local legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970) because there was a reasonable basis for limiting operation of the legislation to communities of a certain size; and (4) the appeals section of the county ordinance did violate due process because it imposed a penalty for pursuing an appeal, however, that section was severable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court with respect to the constitutionality of the appeals section of the county's impact fee ordinance and affirmed the decision of the trial court in all other respects.

People v. James


1-90-0033


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


255 Ill. App. 3d 516; 626 N.E.2d 1337; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1502; 193 Ill. Dec. 786



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Mary Jane Theis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated arson and sentenced him to 10 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted, in absentia, of aggravated arson. He was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment. The court reversed because the jury was asked to determine the defendant's fate and provided with verdict forms that did not allow them to find him not guilty of any arson related offenses. There was a reasonable probability that the error had the effect of removing from the jury's consideration the elements of arson, conveying the message that it was the jury's duty only to determine whether the aggravating factor of the greater offense was present, thus directing a verdict of guilty on the charge. The error undermined the reliability of the verdict and was not harmless. Finally, during sentencing, the trial judge improperly considered in aggravation that defendant's conduct threatened harm to others when that fact was implicit in the offense for which he was charged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that convicted the defendant of aggravated arson and remanded the case for a new trial.

People v. Benson


NO. 4-93-0069


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 144; 621 N.E.2d 981; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1501; 190 Ill. Dec. 528


August 18, 1993, Argued  
September 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 26, 1993. As Corrected October 28, 1993. Released for Publication November 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 91CF869. Honorable Ronald C. Dozier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted him of one count of criminal sexual battery, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, sentenced to seven years in prison, and ordered to pay restitution. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the spectators at the trial lacked the direct interest contemplated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-11. The court noted that defendant made no offer to distinguish particular family members from neighbors and collateral relatives among the spectators. The court found that the record sufficiently supported the trial court's decision to clear the courtroom while the child victim testified. The court noted that defendant failed to identify any immediate family when asked by the trial court. The court held that the Waller criteria did not apply to § 115-11. The court found no prohibition against including in the restitution order expenses for prospective psychological counseling of the sexual abuse victim. The court held that the restitution order was not speculative because it set both a ceiling on the amount of additional restitution and a time frame in which therapy could be completed.

Williams v. Nagel


NO. 4-92-0949


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 176; 620 N.E.2d 1376; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1528; 190 Ill. Dec. 115


July 20, 1993, Oral Argument Held  
September 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication and Rehearing Denied November 1, 1993.As Corrected October 26, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 92L645. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) granted defendants, the management and owners of the complex, the city and two police officers, summary judgment in the action of plaintiff individuals for damages for common law, statutory and constitutional violations. The individuals appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individuals, were barred from entering a housing complex. The individuals contended that the management and owners of the complex, the city and two police officers, violated their common law, statutory and constitutional rights. The lower court granted summary judgment to defendants. The individuals contended that they were invited onto the premises by certain tenants and had common law and statutory rights. The court determined that the individuals did not have common law or statutory rights to enter the complex because the tenants were not plaintiffs in the proceeding and that the lease agreement with tenants provided management the right to bar individuals from the property. The individuals alleged that the police's practice of recommending who was to be placed on the no trespass list created a close nexus between the actions of the police and the management of the complex to make the action of the management that of the city. The court found that the conduct of the management of the complex could not have been treated as that of the city or the police to establish the necessary state action for a constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment.

People v. Rivera


No. 1-91-0407


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


255 Ill. App. 3d 1015; 627 N.E.2d 294; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1506; 194 Ill. Dec. 178



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 20, 1993. Released for Publication February 16, 1994. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 6, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Mary Maxwell Thomas Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of first-degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 1992, 5/9-1 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a Hispanic man, stabbed an unarmed African-American man to death during a fight in which racial epitaphs were used and gang members were present. Defendant claimed that the victim initiated the fight by demanding a bicycle and threatening him. After the trial court denied defendant's request for a jury instruction on the mitigating factors establishing second-degree murder, defendant was convicted on a first-degree murder charge. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) the evidence presented at trial supported the first-degree murder conviction because it did not show that the victim was the aggressor, the danger of harm was imminent, unlawful force was threatened by the victim, or that defendant used the kind of force necessary to avert danger; (2) because the evidence was insufficient to reduce the conviction to second-degree murder or to affirmatively raise the issue of self-defense, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on those issues, and the burden did not shift to the state to disprove the existence of justification; (3) the trial court did not err in excluding irrelevant testimony concerning the victim's gang membership.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on a charge of first-degree murder.

People v. Warwick


No. 2-91-1423


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 65; 621 N.E.2d 282; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1482; 190 Ill. Dec. 413



September 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-CF-1585. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the 10-year sentence given by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) after he pleaded guilty to one charge of reckless homicide committed while under the influence of alcohol, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-3(e) (1991), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3(e) (1992). He claimed that the statute violated due process and equal protection because it was irrational and improperly extended a term without aggravating factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant illegally drove his car into an intersection while under the influence of alcohol, struck a car and killed a passenger in that car. He pleaded guilty to reckless homicide, a Class 3 felony, but the charge was enhanced to a Class 2 felony and the 10-year sentence rendered was four years under the maximum for that felony. On appeal, the court found that he had to demonstrate clearly the alleged constitutional violation. The court found that the Equal Protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, did not require equal treatment of differently situated classes of persons, and that where no fundamental right was at stake, the legislature could differentiate between similarly situated persons if there was a rational reason for doing so. The court ruled that it was rational to impose a more harsh penalty for the crime because of the state's police interest in deterring driving while under the influence of alcohol, and that a double enhancement of a penalty was permissible and was given effect where it was clear that the legislature intended such a result. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which sentenced defendant to 10 years for reckless homicide committed while under the influence of alcohol.

People v. Truss


No. 1-90-1426


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


254 Ill. App. 3d 767; 626 N.E.2d 1175; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1471; 193 Ill. Dec. 624



September 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on denial of rehearing September 24, 1993. Released for Publication February 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE RALPH REYNA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, after a jury trial, entered a conviction of first degree murder and sentenced defendant to 40 years' imprisonment. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by giving the jury two issues instructions on first degree murder and by excluding evidence regarding his state of mind.


OVERVIEW: A witness testified that after hearing a loud commotion in his house, he went inside and saw defendant, who was living with his mother, holding a knife in his right hand. The witness saw the deceased sitting in a chair with a small bloodstain on the left side of his chest. A jury convicted defendant of first degree murder. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court's jury instructions properly conveyed the relationship between first degree murder and the lesser offense of second degree murder by apprising the jury that once it found that the state had proved the elements of first degree murder, it was required to determine whether a mitigating factor had been proved to reduce the offense to second degree murder. Defendant was afforded ample opportunity to establish his state of mind at the time of the stabbing. Although the prosecutor's erroneous statement of the law of self-defense was improper, the statement was not prejudicial to defendant in light of the overwhelming evidence against defendant, including defendant's own testimony admitting that he stabbed the deceased and a witnesses' testimony that the deceased did not push or threaten defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and his sentence of imprisonment.
