People v. One 1986 White Mazda Pickup Truck


No. 2-92-0666


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


251 Ill. App. 3d 79; 621 N.E.2d 250; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1470; 190 Ill. Dec. 381


August 24, 1993, Submitted  
September 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 27, 1993. Petiton for Leave to Appeal Allowed February 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 91-MR-465. Honorable James F. Quetsch, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed the denial from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), of the State's request for forfeiture of defendant's pickup truck pursuant to § 505(a)(3) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1505(a)(3) (1991) (now 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/505(a)(3) (1992))).


OVERVIEW: The issue of first impression was whether the mere existence of a controlled substance on the person of a vehicle occupant subjected the vehicle to forfeiture. Defendant was stopped in his truck due to a warrant which had issued for his failure to appear on a traffic violation. The police officer searched defendant. Defendant had a clear plastic straw in his right interior coat pocket and a plastic bag containing cocaine in his underwear. The State argued that the trial court erred in denying the complaint for forfeiture of defendant's truck because it "facilitated" defendant's possession of the cocaine within the meaning of the forfeiture statute. The court held that where the use of the vehicle was entirely incidental to the possession of the controlled substance, it did not make the possession "easier or less difficult" as required by the key word "facilitate" in the forfeiture statute. Defendant did not use the vehicle in any manner to make or try to make possession easier. Rather, the controlled substance was already secreted on his person, and the use of the vehicle did not in any manner "facilitate" this violation of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that the pickup truck was not subject to forfeiture.

Larkin v. Hartigan


NO. 4-93-0052


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 91L22. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which dismissed his action for declaratory and injunctive relief filed against defendants, Attorney General of the State of Illinois and Secretary of State of the State of Illinois. The driver contended that the Illinois Vehicle Code authorization of a program for proof of insurance was unconstitutional because it violated due process.


OVERVIEW: The secretary sent the driver a letter stating that his license plates would be suspended if he did not provide insurance information within 30 days, sent in erroneous information, or indicated that he carried no coverage. The driver had coverage, but sent a letter stating it was unclear if he was insured. The secretary suspended his plates but indicated that suspension would be lifted if he paid a fee and sent in proof of coverage. U.S. Const. amend. XIV was not violated because a pre-suspension hearing was available under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-118(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the driver's action.

People v. Tirado


NO. 1-92-2101


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


254 Ill. App. 3d 497; 626 N.E.2d 1114; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1423; 193 Ill. Dec. 563



September 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Francis J. Mahon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of attempting to lure a child into his car without the consent of her parent for other than a lawful purpose in violation of the child abduction statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1991). The trial court sentenced defendant to three years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: An eight-year old girl reported to police that a man had followed her home from school. She described the man's appearance, car, and clothing. In the meantime, defendant was stopped for a traffic violation. He was brought to the police station, where the girl identified him. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court rejected defendant's assertion that the trial judge improperly responded to a jury inquiry as to whether defendant could speak English because the record did not reflect that such an interchange took place. A jury instruction properly created a permissive presumption by stating that the attempted luring "may be considered" evidence of other than a lawful purpose. The child abduction statute created only a permissive inference and did not improperly place on defendant the burden of proving lawful purpose. The trial judge did not violate defendant's rights by stating that he was surprised at how low the statutory maximum sentence was.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted child abduction.

Sparks & Wiewel Constr. Co. v. Martin


NOS. 4-92-0235, 4-92-0236 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


250 Ill. App. 3d 955; 620 N.E.2d 533; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1378; 189 Ill. Dec. 565


May 19, 1993, Oral Argument  
September 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 19, 1993. As Corrected October 22, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 91MR26. Honorable Sue E. Myerscough, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted summary judgment to plaintiffs, various corporations and partnerships (companies), against defendants, the Department of Labor (Department) and others. The circuit court granted attorney fees to the companies under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 1014.1(b) of the Administrative Procedure Act. At issue was the Prevailing Wage Act (Wage Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 39s-1 et seq. (1991).


OVERVIEW: The Department hired a general contractor, which hired a quarrying company, which hired one of the companies to perform trucking. The drivers were employed by the companies. The Department determined that the drivers were entitled to prevailing wages under the Wage Act. The trial court, however, found that the companies were exempt from the provisions of the Wage Act and that the Department's interpretation to the contrary was improper rulemaking. The companies sought attorney fees. The court found that the drivers were engaged in transportation by sellers and suppliers of materials and, as such, they were expressly excluded from coverage of the Wage Act. The fact that the drivers dumped the material where it would be used was not dispositive. Only employees of contractors or subcontractors were covered by the Wage Act. The drivers were engaged in the transportation of the materials and were, therefore, properly excluded from coverage. The court further found that the Department did not engage in rulemaking, but merely interpreted the statutory language of the Wage Act. There was no improper rulemaking under the Administrative Procedure Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order finding the companies exempt from the provisions of the Wage Act. The court reversed the circuit court's order determining that the Department engaged in improper rulemaking. The award of attorney fees was also reversed.

People v. Smith

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which convicted him, by a bench trial, of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial of burglary. He appealed from his conviction, arguing that the trial judge erred by denying him the right to present closing argument at trial, that his appointed counsel abdicated her responsibility at trial, and that the trial judge erred when he did not obtain a proper waiver of defendant's right to counsel. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that defendant was not denied an opportunity to argue his case to the trial court. The court also held that defense counsel's forbearance from cross-examining a witness did not deny defendant his right to effective assistance of counsel. Although defendant did not waive his right to counsel at his sentencing, the court found that defendant's ineffective waiver was harmless because he knew of his right to have counsel represent him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary.

People v. Staton


No. 2-91-1107


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


248 Ill. App. 3d 799; 619 N.E.2d 777; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1257; 189 Ill. Dec. 76


July 21, 1993, Submitted  
August 17, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 16, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County. Nos. 90-TR-8920, 90-TR-8921, 90-TR-8922, 90-TR-8923, 90-TR-8924, 90-CF-99. Honorable Richard E. DeMoss, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court of Stephenson County, Illinois, for driving under the influence of alcohol, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501 (1992), driving while his driver's license was revoked under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/6-303 (1992), disobeying a stop sign under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-1204(b) (1992), and two snowmobile offenses under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 40/5-2(A), 40/5-3 (1992).


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw a snowmobile without its lights on, travelling through an alley in the early morning hours. The officer followed the snowmobile and stopped it. Defendant was driving the snowmobile. The officer ran defendant's license and discovered it was revoked. The officer determined that defendant was intoxicated and charged him with driving under the influence, driving while his driver's license was revoked, disobeying a stop sign, illegal operation of a snowmobile, and operating a snowmobile without a valid license. He was convicted of all the charges. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions for the illegal operation of a snowmobile and operation of a snowmobile without a license and reversed the other three convictions. The court held that the definition of vehicle in the general provisions of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-101 et seq., did not apply to snowmobiles. In fact snowmobiles were expressly excluded from the definition of vehicle under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-217 (1992). The court held that the definition of "vehicle" had to be given its plain and ordinary meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for illegal operation of a snowmobile and operation of a snowmobile without a license and reversed his convictions and sentences for the offenses of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor, stop sign violation, and driving while license revoked.

People v. d'Avis


No. 1-92-3176


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 649; 621 N.E.2d 206; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1209; 190 Ill. Dec. 337



August 6, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 9, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ABISHI C. CUNNINGHAM, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County, which convicted the defendant of misdemeanor battery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3(a)(2) (1991), and sentenced the defendant to one year probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant performed a rectal exam on a patient. The patient alleged that defendant asked if the patient was "enjoying" the exam and that the patient saw defendant masturbate during the procedure. The trial court convicted defendant of misdemeanor battery in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3(a)(2) (1991), and sentenced defendant to one year probation. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for misdemeanor battery and the trial court's sentencing of defendant to one year of probation.

People ex rel. Harris v. Parrish Oil Prod.


No. 5-92-0021


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


249 Ill. App. 3d 664; 622 N.E.2d 810; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1199; 190 Ill. Dec. 780



August 5, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied September 14, 1993. As Corrected September 24, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jasper County. Nos. 90-TX-1(2) and 90-TX-1(3). The Honorable Edward C. Eberspacher III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax collector challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Jasper County (Illinois), which held a tax regulation relating to the taxation of fractional interest ownership in oil-well leases unconstitutional and vacated the tax sales performed pursuant to the regulation.


OVERVIEW: The tax collector billed defendant taxpayers as the operators of the wells for the property tax on the entire seven-eighths working interest rather than just the fractional undivided share that each owned. The taxpayers paid only the amount attributable to their individual fractional ownership interests, and the tax collector thereafter sold the entire working interest in each lease at a tax sale to satisfy the property tax due from the entire working interest. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that the owners of the working interest obviously had a property interest, yet the regulation itself contained insufficient procedural safeguards to ensure that the owner had adequate notice and opportunity for a hearing prior to being deprived of property pursuant to a delinquent-tax sale. The court determined that individual notice to all holders of a working interest was more burdensome, but those burdens did not outweigh an individual's guarantee of due process under the law. The court concluded that the regulation was facially invalid as applied and deprived the owners of the undivided working interest of the leases without due process and equal protection of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding a tax regulation relating to the taxation of fractional interest ownership in oil-well leases unconstitutional and vacating the tax sales performed pursuant to the regulation was affirmed.

 

849 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wesley


1-90-3210


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 245; 620 N.E.2d 1335; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1150; 190 Ill. Dec. 74



July 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 2, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE CHARLES E. PORCELLINO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Cook County (Illinois) that entered judgment against defendant upon a jury's verdict, which adjudged defendant guilty of one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault to the anus. Defendant also challenged the trial court's imposition of a 14-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault to the anus after he forcibly raped a woman in the anus. The trial court entered judgment and imposed a 14-year sentence. Defendant challenged the guilt finding and sentence. The court affirmed. The court held: (1) defendant's venire was not unconstitutionally composed because the jury selection comported with the due process principles of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 78, para. 9.2 (1991) and African-Americans were not systematically excluded because the selection process followed Cook (Ill.) Cir. Ct., R. 0.4; (2) the trial court judge properly exercised its discretion in evaluating impartiality; (3) the verdicts were not legally inconsistent because the jurors could have found evidence to show lack of consent to the rectal act, but insufficient evidence as to lack of consent of the vaginal intercourse; (4) the lesser included instruction of battery was not appropriate in a sexual assault case; and (5) the evidence substantiated that defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's evidentiary objections, and did not abuse its discretion in imposing a 14-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that entered judgment against defendant upon a jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault to the anus, and affirmed the trial court's imposition of a 14-year sentence.

 

850 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Memory Gardens Cemetery v. Village of Arlington Heights


No. 1-92-1227


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 553; 621 N.E.2d 107; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1118; 190 Ill. Dec. 238



July 27, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 9, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Monica Reynolds, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Village of Arlington Heights, its building commissioner, and zoning board of appeals denied plaintiff cemetery's request for a permit to build a mausoleum. The cemetery filed a declaratory judgment action and alleged that a special use permit was not required, or that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendants' motion for judgment in their favor. The cemetery appealed.


OVERVIEW: The construction of the ordinance was a question of law, which the court reviewed de novo. The court also sought the plain meaning of the ordinance's wording. The cemetery argued that when the Village wished a particular use to be deemed separate and distinct, the Village gave it a separate listing in the ordinance's index or defined it. However, the ordinance's use table contained the words cemeteries, crematories, or mausoleums on a single line, and there was no definition for these terms. Under the ordinance, special use permits were needed for cemeteries, crematories, or mausoleums. The use of the disjunctive indicated the intent to draw a distinction among the words used. Thus, the Village intended that the two words be considered separate uses. Also, among the purposes of the ordinance was regulation of the intensity of land use and prevention of overcrowding. In this light, a definition of "cemetery" did not include mausoleums. The latter were above ground structures, which afforded more intense use of the same land. Accordingly, the court held a mausoleum was a use separate and distinct from that of a cemetery, and the cemetery was required to obtain a special use permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Petition to Form New Park Dist.


No. 2-91-1443


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


247 Ill. App. 3d 702; 617 N.E.2d 464; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1094; 187 Ill. Dec. 256


October 23, 1992, Submitted  
July 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 91-MC-5. Honorable William D. Block, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioners sought review of a grant of summary judgment to appellee objectors in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) on appellants' petition to form a new park district on the ground that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction over the petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that the property included in the petition that made the petition defective was included inadvertently and that the trial court should have allowed them to amend the petition to bring it into conformity with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 105, para. 2-2 (1989). Appellees responded that the inclusion of the improper parcels rendered the petition void ab initio and the trial court, therefore, lacked jurisdiction to consider its amendment. The court reversed the trial court's order. The court found that the trial court could and should have entertained appellants' motion to amend the petition because the petition was sufficient to confer jurisdiction on the court for purposes of subsequent amendment. The court held that the Code of Civil Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 1-101 et seq. (1989), which applied to procedural matters that were not regulated by the Park District Code, provided for amendment to the petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the order of the trial court granting appellees' motion for summary judgment, vacated the portion of the order denying appellants' motion to amend, and remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Cano v. Village of Dolton


1-92-0003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 130; 620 N.E.2d 1200; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1088; 189 Ill. Dec. 883



July 20, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Order of the Illinois Human Rights Commission



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner job applicant filed a complaint with the Illinois Department of Human Rights for age discrimination against respondent village pursuant to the Illinois Human Rights Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 2-101 (1991). The Illinois Human Rights Commission granted a summary decision in favor of respondent. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner job applicant applied for a job with respondent village, which, he claimed, refused to hire him because of his age, which was 40. The court affirmed the Illinois Human Rights Commission's grant of a summary decision in favor of respondent. Under the Illinois Human Rights Act (HRA), the Human Rights Commission could render a summary decision in favor of either a complainant or a respondent if the pleadings and affidavits, if any, showed that there was no genuine issue as to any material fact and that the moving party was entitled to a recommended order as a matter of law. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 8-106.1 (1991). Petitioner did not supply any competent evidence that counteracted the affidavit of respondent that it told petitioner two days before his fortieth birthday that they would not hire him, thus petitioner was not yet protected by the HRA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary decision in favor of respondent village.

 

853 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


NO. 5-92-0409


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


246 Ill. App. 3d 647; 616 N.E.2d 737; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1095; 186 Ill. Dec. 547



July 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 88-CF-353. Honorable Kimberly Dahlen, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of, and sentence for, home invasion, residential burglary, theft under $ 300, and two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois). Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in denying his motion for continuance to allow DNA testing, the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt his guilt of aggravated criminal sexual assault, and other errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant waived any error in the denial of his motion for continuance when he failed to file a post-trial motion. Also, the motion for a continuance was untimely. Defendant filed the motion three days before trial, which would have required a delay of up to six months in a case already more than three years old. Defendant had already filed other motions, including one for continuance, and obtained rulings on them some three months earlier. If defendant believed DNA testing would exonerate him, he should have made the proper motion earlier. The evidence was sufficient to establish guilt of criminal sexual assault by causing bodily harm to the victim in transmitting a sexual disease. The victim testified that she did not have gonorrhea before the assault, but was infected with the disease afterward. Tests conducted on defendant after the assault revealed he was infected with the same strain of gonorrhea. Conviction for two aggravated sexual assaults was warranted when defendant committed multiple rapes on the victim during one criminal episode. Defendant's sentence was not excessive when his actions at the time of the offenses and afterward revealed little rehabilitative potential.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

854 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 1-91-0350


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 80; 621 N.E.2d 62; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1066; 190 Ill. Dec. 193



July 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1993. As Corrected September 22, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard E. Neville, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of possession with intent to deliver more than 900 grams of a substance containing cocaine in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(2) (1987). He was sentenced to the minimum term of 15 years' imprisonment. On appeal, defendant maintained that the statute under which he was sentenced was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the provision under which he was sentenced was unconstitutional because it violated the due process and proportionate penalties provisions of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 11 (1970). The State argued that there were no constitutional infirmities in the statute, which was reasonably related to legislative concerns about the harmful consequences of the distribution of large quantities of cocaine. The court found no reason for reversal. The mandatory minimum sentences imposed for drug trafficking crimes were not clearly irrational or wholly disproportionate to the offense committed. The imposition of greater sentences and mandatory minimum terms for the possession and delivery of cocaine reflected the seriousness of the offense, and was reasonably designed to remedy the evils of drug trafficking and its attendant social repercussions. Accordingly, the court found no reason to depart from the presumptive validity of the legislative enactment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the sentence imposed by the circuit court were affirmed.

Tim Thompson, Inc. v. Village of Hinsdale


No. 2-92-1166


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


247 Ill. App. 3d 863; 617 N.E.2d 1227; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1068; 187 Ill. Dec. 506


June 22, 1993, Submitted  
July 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 17, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-MR-651. Honorable S. Keith Lewis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, corporation and trustee(claimants), filed a complaint against defendant village seeking to enjoin the enforcement of a zoning ordinance and a declaration of its invalidity. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) granted summary judgment to the village on four counts and dismissed two counts. The claimants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The zoning ordinance changed the classification of a residential subdivision, modifying the minimum lot size required for development. The claimants had agreed to purchase lots in the subdivision prior to the zoning ordinance change. After the change, the village advised the claimants that development of one lot was not permitted and that a variation was required prior to the development of a second lot. The claimants argued that the denial of their application for a map amendment to rezone was arbitrary and capricious and that the subject lots were suitable for development. The court set forth the factors used to determine whether a zoning ordinance was valid and held that there was an issue of material fact precluding summary judgment. The claimants also sought an injunction to enjoin the village from enforcing the zoning ordinance. The court found that the claimants had constructive notice of the proposed zoning changes at the time the claimants made expenditures and that summary judgment against the claimants on that issue was proper. Nor did the rezoning violate 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-13-1 by depriving the claimants of using the lots for a lawful purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment as to the claimants request for an injunction but reversed the grant of summary judgment denying the claimants request for a map amendment to rezone.

Reuter v. Korb


No. 2-92-0811


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


248 Ill. App. 3d 142; 616 N.E.2d 1363; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1070; 186 Ill. Dec. 731


June 10, 1993, Submitted  
July 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication August 20, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 89-L-1027. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff guardians of victim sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) which granted defendant driver's motion for a directed verdict, and granted the driver's motion to bar the guardians' expert witness' testimony, because any proof was likely to pertain to the same evidence already proffered to the court at the time it considered the driver's motion in limine to bar the testimony.


OVERVIEW: The guardians of the victim brought an action against the driver for injuries to the victim by the alleged negligence of the driver in operating his automobile. The driver's answer included affirmative defenses alleging that the victim was more than 50 percent of the proximate cause of the injury. The trial court granted the driver's motion in limine barring the guardians' expert witnesses, a pharmacist and an accident reconstructionist. The court granted the driver's motion for a directed verdict, finding that no negligence on the driver's part had been shown. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the overwhelming evidence had shown that the proximate cause of the victim's injuries were his own conduct, and any such inference from the driver's failure to see the victim in the roadway was not sufficient to overcome the directed verdict. The court held that the trial court had abused its discretion in granting the driver's motion in limine to bar evidence of the expert pharmacist because evidence to show that the drinking resulted in intoxication had been lacking, however the expert reconstructionist's opinion would not have aided in the resolution of the dispute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that no negligence on the driver's part had been shown and that the evidence overwhelmingly indicated that the victim's own conduct constituted the proximate cause of the accident. The court found that the trial court had abused its discretion in barring the expert testimony of the pharmacist because the record lacked evidence showing that the drinking resulted in intoxication.

People v. Young


No. 1-90-2357


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


248 Ill. App. 3d 491; 618 N.E.2d 1026; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 982; 188 Ill. Dec. 456



June 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993. Rehearing Denied September 7, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas Maloney, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder and her sentence of 35 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to 35 years in prison for the stabbing death of a woman during a fight. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court held that defendant's motion to quash the arrest and to suppress her confession was properly denied because under the totality of the circumstances, the warrantless arrest was proper. The information regarding defendant as to her physical description and the location of her residence from two eyewitnesses provided probable cause. Improper comments by the trial court did not require reversal of the conviction because defendant failed to show they were a substantial factor in the conviction. Defendant waived her objection to limits put on defense counsel's questioning of various witnesses by failing to raise the issues with adequate specificity in her motion for new trial. Defendant was not entitled to a second degree murder instruction based on serious provocation because the evidence indicated that defendant was the instigator of the physical fight and the victim was an unarmed and unwilling participant defending herself. The victim's verbal comments were insufficient to show provocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder and her prison sentence of 35 years.

People v. Hooker


No. 1-91-3241


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


249 Ill. App. 3d 394; 618 N.E.2d 1074; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 989; 188 Ill. Dec. 504



June 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Christy S. Berkos, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first-degree murder alleging, inter alia, that he either acted in self-defense or should have been guilty of only second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and appealed the conviction asserting, inter alia, that he acted in self-defense or, alternatively, even if his belief that his life was in imminent danger was unreasonable, a conviction for second degree murder would have been appropriate. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that a rational trier of fact could have found that the essential elements of first-degree murder were established beyond a reasonable doubt and that the state sufficiently refuted the assertion of self-defense. The court found that both testimonial and physical evidence suggested that defendant fired multiple shots while the victim was retreating and that the bullets missing from defendant's gun corresponded with the number of wounds sustained by the victim in the back of the head, neck, and leg. The court also found that defendant's offense should not have been reduced because the evidence sufficiently established that defendant, and only defendant, had a gun, which he fired repeatedly at the victim as he sought to retreat and defendant did not contest the sentence imposed by the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder.

Department of Pub. Aid ex rel. Evans v. Lively


NO. 5-91-0359


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


246 Ill. App. 3d 216; 615 N.E.2d 1381; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1031; 186 Ill. Dec. 324



June 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellee's Petition for Rehearing Granted June 2, 1993 and Appellant's Motion for Extension of Time Denied June 30, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 1030.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 90-F-129. Honorable David W. Watt, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Public Aid, acting on behalf of the mother (mother), appealed from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which granted respondent putative father's motion to dismiss and denied petitioner's motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: This action was brought by the mother to establish the putative father's paternity of a child but was dismissed by the trial court based on the statute of limitations that existed prior to adoption of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2501 et seq. (1989). The mother appealed and the court reversed, holding that because the prior statute of limitations had been held to be unconstitutional, it conferred no rights and the putative father had acquired no vested rights by the expiration of the limitations period provided by prior law. Because no vested rights had been acquired under the prior statute, retroactive application of the new statute of limitations did not violate the putative father's due process rights by reviving a previously barred cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders below which had dismissed the case and remanded the case to the lower court for further proceedings.

FDIC v. O'Malley


1-90-1718


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


249 Ill. App. 3d 340; 618 N.E.2d 818; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 942; 188 Ill. Dec. 248



June 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 10, 1993. Released for Publication September 3, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. The Honorable Thomas E. Hoffman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee corporation made a demand to appellant guarantor for payment under a guaranty. When the guarantor refused to pay, the corporation filed an action to recover the amounts due under the guaranty. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment in favor of the corporation pursuant to 12 U.S.C.S. § 1823(e). The guarantor appealed. The corporation filed a cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: A corporation filed an action against a guarantor to recover the amount due under a guaranty. The trial court issued judgment for the corporation under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1823(e). The guarantor appealed and asserted that the trial court erred when it found that the guaranty was an asset of an insolvent bank, found that the guarantor was not released under § 1823(e), refused to find that the guarantor was discharged, refused to grant a setoff or a partial release, and denied him a new trial. The corporation cross-appealed and asserted that the amount of its award of interest was improperly reduced. The court held that the trial court's findings were proper because the alleged release did not comply with § 1823(e), the guaranty was a bank asset because it was not extinguished prior to the corporation's takeover of the bank, the guarantor was not discharged because the guaranty was unaffected by extensions of credit to the co-guarantor, guaranty did not provide for a setoff or partial release, the trial court's calculations of interest due under the guaranty were incorrect, and a new trial was not warranted because Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 63(C), 113 Ill. 2d R. 63(C)(1)(c) was not violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the corporation was affirmed. The award of interest to the corporation was reversed and remanded for correction of the amount of the award.

People v. King


No. 1-88-0798, 1-89-2086; Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


248 Ill. App. 3d 253; 618 N.E.2d 709; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 905; 188 Ill. Dec. 139



June 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Will E. Gierach, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of two judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him for aggravated criminal sexual assault and home invasion for two separate incidents. On appeal, he raised several arguments including that he was denied a fair trial in each instance, and that the jury was not correctly instructed on the state's burden of proof in the second trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and home invasion in two separate circumstances, and sought review of both convictions in a consolidated appeal. On appeal, he contended inter alia that he was denied a fair trial in each instance, and that the jury was not correctly instructed on the state's burden of proof. The court held that: (1) defendant's confession was voluntary under the Illinois Juvenile Act, as a youth officer was present and spoke with defendant prior to the confession; (2) admission of evidence concerning defendant's sexual assault of one victim in his trial for the attack on second victim, did not deprive defendant of a fair trial, as that evidence served to delineate defendant's modus operandi; and, (3) in view of the multiple instructions given to the jury at trial the jury was adequately informed on state's burden of proof even though the trial court did not give a certain instruction requested by defendant. The matter was remanded for resentencing on defendant's conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault. The trial court's judgment was thus affirmed on the convictions, and reversed and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that convicted defendant for two instances of home invasion and aggravated criminal sexual assault was affirmed. Defendant was not denied a fair trial when state introduced evidence of his one aggravated sexual assault and home invasion offense, as that evidence went to delineate defendant's modus operandi for the second offense. The was reversed in part and remanded for resentencing.

Management Ass'n v. Board of Regents


No. 1-92-0476


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


248 Ill. App. 3d 599; 618 N.E.2d 694; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 908; 188 Ill. Dec. 124



June 18, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff not-for-profit corporation appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant independent contractors' and the state university's motion to dismiss the corporation's action for damages, an injunction and other relief pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 110, par. 2-619. The dispositive issue was whether the court of claims had exclusive subject matter jurisdiction over the litigation.


OVERVIEW: The not-for-profit corporation, an educational and training service provider, contracted with the independent contractors to serve as instructors. A dispute arose when the contractors left the corporation's service and went to work for the state university. The trial court granted the contractors' and the university's motion to dismiss the corporation's action for damages, an injunction and other relief. The issue was whether the trial court had subject matter over the corporation's claims. The court affirmed because the court of claims had exclusive subject matter jurisdiction over the action. The court of claims also had exclusive jurisdiction over the issuance of injunctive relief because its jurisdiction was not limited to monetary claims. In addition, the court of claims had jurisdiction to grant such equitable relief as an accounting and a constructive trust. In addition, § 8(d) of the Court of Claims Act gave the court of claims jurisdiction over claims against the university that sounded in tort. Finally, the court of claims had jurisdiction over claims against the university under the Illinois Trade Secrets Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 140, par. 351 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted the independent contractor's and the state university's motion to dismiss the not-for-profit corporation's action for damages, an injunction and other relief.

Pick v. Pucinski


No. 1-91-0384


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


247 Ill. App. 3d 1068; 618 N.E.2d 657; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 882; 188 Ill. Dec. 87



June 16, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Thomas J. O'Brien, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, the clerk of the circuit court and the county treasurer. The citizen had brought an action against defendants after he was required to pay a filing fee pursuant to the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.2(11)(b) (1989), after his case was remanded to the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The citizen appealed a case against an insurer and the court remanded the matter back to the circuit court. On remand, the circuit court required that the citizen pay a filing fee. The citizen paid the fee under protest and filed an action against defendants for a declaratory judgment, an accounting, and injunctive relief. The circuit court granted summary judgment to defendants and the citizen appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the circuit court. The court held that there was a reasonable basis for the Act's authorization of the collection of additional filing fees upon remand of a cause from a reviewing court and such fees were being imposed for purposes relating to the operation and maintenance of the circuit court. The imposition of a refiling fee upon remand was ostensibly for a court related purpose. The court found that there were some additional services that were performed that were in addition to the services that were normally required at the initial filing of a case. The court held that under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307(a), the citizen could not raise the circuit court's denial of injunctive relief for the first time on appeal. 134 Ill. 2d R. 307(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants against the citizen.

People v. Ramirez


1-90-3528


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


248 Ill. App. 3d 938; 618 N.E.2d 638; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 880; 188 Ill. Dec. 68



June 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN D. BRADY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state arrested and charged defendant by information for possession of more than 15 but less than 100 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied his motion to quash his arrest and to suppress evidence obtained incident to his arrest and convicted defendant. Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was stopped for a traffic violation, he failed to produce his driver's license. His vehicle was searched and drugs were found. Defendant was arrested and prosecuted. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence obtained as a result of his arrest arguing the fact that he actually had a valid license made his arrest unwarranted. The trial court denied the motion and defendant was convicted. Defendant argued for reversal of his conviction on the basis that he was found guilty on the strength alone of the evidence discovered as the product of what he described as an illegal seizure. According to defendant, the Fourth Amendment prohibited all seizures, even those which followed the commission of offenses, which were not reasonable. The conviction was affirmed based upon the holding that defendant was seized for what the officer had probable cause to believe was the commission of what was determined to be a misdemeanor, the driving of a motor vehicle without being licensed. The court reasoned the seizure was effected in response to the commission of an act, which the legislature had chosen to define as a crime, and thus, was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of drug related offenses was affirmed.

 

865 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Kaszubowski v. Board of Educ.


No. 1-91-3494


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


248 Ill. App. 3d 451; 618 N.E.2d 609; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 858; 188 Ill. Dec. 39



June 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 3, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE THOMAS J. O'BRIEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their claims to recover money damages and injunctive relief against defendant Interim Board of Education of the City of Chicago (board) based on contract rights allegedly created by operation of law pursuant to the Illinois School Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 34-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The employees lost their jobs as subdistrict superintendents because of the adoption of the School Reform Act (act) and filed suit against the board for damages. The trial court found in favor of the board and held that the mere reference to performance contracts in the act did not suggest a legislative intent to create vested contractual rights. The court reversed. The court found that the act was not ambiguous and it provided that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 34-8.3(g) was an intention to employ the employees until their terms expired. The court held that since the language of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 34-8.3(g) clearly and unambiguously granted the employees a contract by operation of law, the subsequent actions of the board which resulted in the employees' termination or reassignment violated those contractual rights. The court held that following the rules of statutory construction and utilizing the plain meaning of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 34-8.3(g), the legislature intended to create a contract with the employees effective until the date of termination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with directions.

People v. Smith

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which convicted him for residential burglary, criminal sexual assault, theft (under $ 300), and aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for appointment of an expert witness, the state failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of aggravated criminal sexual assault, and, because there was only one sexual assault and criminal sexual assault was a lesser-included offense, one of his convictions had to be reversed. The court vacated the conviction for criminal sexual assault, but otherwise affirmed. The court determined, however, that there was only one sexual assault and, criminal sexual assault being a lesser-included offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault, the conviction for criminal sexual assault had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The conviction for criminal sexual assault was vacated and the remaining convictions were affirmed.

People v. Fryer


No. 1-89-1774


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


247 Ill. App. 3d 1051; 618 N.E.2d 377; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 766; 187 Ill. Dec. 786



May 28, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 9, 1993. Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Shelvin Singer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault, criminal sexual assault, and unlawful restraint. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict and that there were numerous alleged procedural errors that deprived him of his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault, criminal sexual assault, and unlawful restraint, alleged multiple errors on appeal. The court affirmed the conviction because, in part, the state did not need medical evidence to prove sexual penetration and did not need to allege or instruct the jury as to defendant's intent, because sexual assault was a general, not specific, intent crime. Neither did the state need to show resistance on the part of the victim if it was useless under the circumstances. The court also held that aggravated sexual assault could be established by harm to the victim immediately after and not just before the sexual act. In addition, the codefendant's plea agreement that prevented his testimony on behalf of defendant did not violate defendant's right to compulsory process because the codefendant, who still faced criminal prosecution, had a right not to testify and because there was no showing that the testimony was both material and favorable for defendant. The court also held that state's objection to certain black veniremen were did not violate defendant's right to equal protection because they were for legitimate, "race neutral" reasons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault, criminal sexual assault, and unlawful restraint because the evidence was sufficient and because the alleged procedural errors were without merit, were not preserved for appellate review, were not prejudicial, were not an abuse of the trial court's discretion, or were not a violation of defendant's constitutional rights.

Carbondale Convention Ctr., Inc. v. City of Carbondale


No. 5--92--0143


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District

Rev. Stat. ch. 116, para. 201 (1989).

The press filed a petition to intervene, asking that the gag order be vacated and that the settlement agreement be produced. The circuit court granted the petition to intervene but, upon the motions of the convention center and the city, dismissed the petition. Land & Lakes Co. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 3-92-0496


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


245 Ill. App. 3d 631; 616 N.E.2d 349; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 756



May 27, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication and Rehearing Denied June 30, 1993. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Order of the Illinois Pollution Control Board



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landfill owners sought review of the decision of respondent Illinois Pollution Control Board (board), which affirmed respondent village's decision to deny approval of the landfill owner's site plan to expand the landfill.


OVERVIEW: The landfill owners submitted a site plan to the village for approval of expansion. The county intervened and, at the hearing on the application, testified that it was likely that a neighboring landfill would soon reopen. At a meeting of the village board, the village board denied the application, but granted the landfill owners' motion to take judicial notice that the county also had filed a suit to keep the neighboring landfill closed. The landfill owners appealed to the board, which reversed the village's decision. Subsequently, the board granted the village's request to reconsider and remanded the case to the village. The village denied the landfill owners' application again, and the board affirmed the denial. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case to the village with instructions to hold a new hearing. The court held that landfill owners were denied a fair hearing because the county failed to disclose that it was taking legal action to prevent the reopening of a neighboring landfill while simultaneously contending that the expansion of the landfill owners' landfill was not needed because the neighboring landfill was likely to reopen.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the board's affirmation of the village's decision to deny the landfill owners approval to expand their landfill and remanded the case to the village for a new approval hearing.

In re Marriage of Vanek


No. 1-91-2351


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


247 Ill. App. 3d 377; 617 N.E.2d 329; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 739; 187 Ill. Dec. 121



May 26, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Mitchell Leikin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ex-wife challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the ex-wife's petition to modify a judgment of dissolution of marriage, awarded to the ex-wife and respondent ex-husband on October 21, 1981, as untimely. The ex-wife's petition, filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1401 (1989), specifically requested an equitable distribution of the ex-husband's military pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the dissolution of the parties' marriage, federal law precluded the division of military pensions in dissolution proceedings held pursuant to state law. Effective February 1, 1983, Congress enacted the Uniform Services Former Spouses Protection Act (Act), which allowed states to divide military pensions in dissolution proceedings for pay periods beginning after June 25, 1981. In conjunction with the Act, Illinois enacted Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 510.1 (1987), which provided a legal avenue for parties to reopen marriage judgments rendered in the era when division of the military pensions was precluded. The Illinois law extended the normal two-year statute of limitations governing the modification of judgments until January 1, 1989. The ex-wife filed her petition on January 31, 1991. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that: (1) where the ex-wife filed her petition more than two years from the date her judgment became final, the trial court properly dismissed the petition for failure to comply with the two-year statute of limitations; and (2) although the ex-wife's rights to the pension were revived by the Act and extended by § 510.1, she failed to timely act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the ex-wife's petition to modify a judgment of dissolution of marriage where the petition was not timely filed.

 

871 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Truss


No. 1-90-1426


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 677



May 14, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE RALPH REYNA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of first-degree murder and sentencing him to a term of 40 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in the stabbing death of the victim, and was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court committed reversible error when it gave two first-degree murder instructions, neither of which mentioned the jury's duty to consider mitigation, before giving the second-degree murder instruction. Because the second-degree murder instruction followed the first-degree murder instructions, there was no way of knowing whether the jury considered the mitigation issue or whether it ceased deliberating because it determined that the state proved the elements of first-degree murder beyond a reasonable doubt. The second-degree murder instruction should have preceded the first-degree murder instruction. Further, the error was not harmless because there was sufficient evidence presented from which the jury could have reasonably concluded that defendant believed he was justified in using force. Additionally, the court held that the trial court erred when it excluded evidence regarding defendant's state of mind at the time he stabbed the victim, and when it gave a jury instruction on mutual combat.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and remanded the cause for a new trial.

Clark v. Board of Fire & Police Comm'rs


No. 3--92--0637


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District

May 14, 1993, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), which upheld the decision of appellee board of fire and police commissioners (board) terminating his employment as a police officer because of charges of criminal conduct.


OVERVIEW: The board terminated the police officer's employment after finding that he had engaged in criminal conduct, including bribery and failing to make arrests, while acting as a police officer. The police officer appealed and the trial court upheld the board's determination. The police officer sought review of the trial court's decision, objecting to participation by two of the board members, claiming that the department rules were invalid because they were based on an unconstitutional delegation of police authority, and that the board's decision was arbitrary and capricious. PEOPLE v. CONRAIL CORP.


No. 5--92--0539


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


245 Ill. App. 3d 167; 613 N.E.2d 784; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 682; 184 Ill. Dec. 467



May 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 92-CH-237. Honorable James M. Radcliffe, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, railroad and company, filed an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), that denied their motions to dissolve or vacate an ex parte temporary restraining order (TRO) and entered a preliminary injunction against them. The state filed a complaint alleging violations of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2 para. 1042, 1043(a) (1991).


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that the railroad and the company had violated the Act by their transfer and storage of waste at the railyard and that their failure to comply with the Act resulted in substantial danger to the public health of the area. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order and found that (1) the trial court had not abused its broad discretionary power by entering the TRO because a reasonable potential for harming the environment existed as a result of the railroad and company's actions; (2) that § 11-101 did not apply to injunctive actions under the Act; and (3) the parties waived any complaint to the trial court's procedures by not raising the issue at the TRO hearing. The court further held that the activities complained of fell within the ambit of the Act and the terms of the preliminary injunction were not overly broad. The trial court's actions were not preempted by the Commerce Clause because they did not conflict with the Commerce Clause or any other federal law. Last, the court found that the injunction had no aspect of local protectionism, was related to legitimate environmental concerns, and did not violate interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and denied the railroad and the company's motions to dissolve or vacate an ex parte TRO and entered a preliminary injunction.

Chicago v. Kideys

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Morton Zwick, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgagee sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found the mortgagee personally liable for appellee court appointed receiver's fees and expenses.


OVERVIEW: The city had filed an action against appellant property owner and the mortgagee to enforce violations of the city's building code. The property owner was absent from the state, and the mortgagee filed for and was granted a protective order wherein the mortgagee was given immediate possession of the property. The circuit court appointed a receiver upon the mortgagee's request, and the mortgagee purchased receiver's certificates issued by the circuit court. The court ruled that § 11-31-2 allowed the receiver to recover its fees and expenses from rent monies, through a receiver's lien, or by request of additional receiver certificates.

Finally, a rational jury could have clearly found the elements of the crime established beyond a reasonable doubt.

People v. James


No. 1-92-0146


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


246 Ill. App. 3d 939; 617 N.E.2d 115; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 592; 186 Ill. Dec. 876



April 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JOSEPH J. URSO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of aggravated assault, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-2(a)(13) (1991) and two counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.2-A(2) (1991). Defendant also appealed his sentence of two years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was asked to leave a building and responded by firing three shots in the direction of three people. The trial court convicted defendant of two counts of aggravated assault and two counts of the offense of aggravated discharge of a firearm. The court affirmed and held that the offense of aggravated discharge of a firearm was not a lesser included offense of the charge of aggravated assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-2(a)(13) (1991), because the elements of the offenses differed. The aggravated assault statute required that the victim be aware of defendant's conduct, while the aggravated discharge of a firearm statute had no such requirement. The court ruled that the imposition of longer sentences for aggravated firearm violations did not create an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentencing scheme because there were valid reasons for imposing greater penalties on those that discharged firearms as compared to those who engaged in aggravated assault. Additionally, the court held that the statute required that defendant knowingly discharge a firearm in the direction of another and that innocent conduct was not unconstitutionally punished by the firearm statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of aggravated assault and two counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm and the two year sentence of imprisonment.

People v. Allen


No. 1-88-0189


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


249 Ill. App. 3d 1001; 620 N.E.2d 1105; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 565; 189 Ill. Dec. 788



April 22, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 27, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE RICHARD E. NEVILLE, PRESIDING.
People v. Allen, 1991 Ill. App. LEXIS 1885 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 7, 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of four counts of murder and arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of murder and arson. The charges stemmed from a fire in an apartment building that killed four people. Defendant was questioned and taken from his home to the police station, but not formally charged. After questioning at the police station, defendant confessed to setting the fire. Defendant's appeal of his convictions raised several issues. Among them, defendant claimed that his confession should have been suppressed because his arrest was illegal. The court found, contrary to the trial court, that despite not being formally charged, defendant was arrested when he was taken from his apartment because, under the circumstances, a reasonable person would have believed that he was not free to leave. However, because the police acquired probable cause after the arrest but before defendant's statement was given, the intervening acquisition of probable cause meant that defendant's statement of confession need not be suppressed. Accordingly, defendant's convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions of defendant on multiple counts of murder and arson, and ruled that denial of defendant's suppression motion was proper.

People v. Brooks


1-90-3313


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


246 Ill. App. 3d 777; 619 N.E.2d 1271; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 550; 189 Ill. Dec. 222



April 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 20, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE CHARLES E. PORCELLINO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-16(d) (1987), and which imposed a three-year sentence on defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a child care service worker attending to the everyday needs of abused or neglected children in a facility housing the children. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse of one of the children under his care after addressing each of defendant's claimed errors on the merits. For example, the court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in admitting testimony, which insinuated that defendant "was a person of bad character." Instead, the court held that the state was not attempting to portray defendant as a repeat child molester since the thrust of the state's argument was that defendant was an opportunist, taking advantage of children, when no one else was around. Furthermore, in pertinent part, the court rejected defendant's argument that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because of the failure of his counsel to preserve numerous issues for review. Rather, the court determined that each of the claimed errors was either without merit or insufficiently prejudicial to warrant reversal. Thus, the failure to preserve the issues was inconsequential.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of aggravated criminal sexual abuse.

 

880 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Haywood v. Superior Bank F S B


No. 1-92-0556


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


244 Ill. App. 3d 326; 614 N.E.2d 461; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 534; 185 Ill. Dec. 327



April 16, 1993, Decided  
April 16, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 10, 1993. Released for Publication June 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993. As Corrected April 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Albert Green, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individual and group of tenants, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied their request for class certification in their action to recover interest on security deposits from defendant landlords. Plaintiff individual also appealed the trial court's denial of his claim and the ruling that he lacked standing as class representative.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, individual and group of tenants, appealed the trial court's judgment denying their request for class certification for their action against defendant landlords for not paying interest on security deposits as required by the Security Deposit Interest Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 89, para. 121, 122. Plaintiff individual also appealed the denial of his individual claim and that he lacked standing as class representative. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment. The court held that the tenant class certification was appropriate because the common issue of defendants' uniform statutory violation predominated. Further, defendants failed to established that plaintiff individual had entered into an accord and satisfaction with defendants that precluded his standing as a class representative. Plaintiff was unaware when he cashed a check that he was entitled to interest and damages, and he could not have intended to compromise a claim which he did not know existed. There was no language on the check indicating that cashing it would have extinguished defendants' responsibility to pay damages due to their failure to pay annual security deposit interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment denying class certification to plaintiff group of tenants and ruling that plaintiff individual lacked standing as class representative. Class certification was appropriate because the common issue of defendant landlords' uniform statutory violation predominated. Further, defendants failed to prove that plaintiff individual had entered into an accord and satisfaction.

 

881 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Golden


No. 1-92-0456


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


244 Ill. App. 3d 908; 614 N.E.2d 444; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 537; 185 Ill. Dec. 310



April 16, 1993, Decided  
April 16, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which after a bench trial found him not guilty on a first degree murder charge, under Article 7 of the Illinois Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1989), but convicted and sentenced him to second degree murder, allegedly in violation of his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree murder, but convicted of second degree murder. Defendant sought review and the court affirmed the findings. The court held that the state carried its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of each element of first degree murder. But although defendant's belief that it was necessary to use deadly force to defend himself was unreasonable, it nevertheless was a mitigating factor sufficient to reduce his culpability to second degree. The court held that defendant's due process rights were not violated because the trial court correctly applied the law in finding him guilty of second degree murder. The court held that it was not unconstitutional for the legislature to require a defendant to prove a mitigating factor that would reduce a crime from first degree to second degree murder because mitigating factors were affirmative defenses and did not bear upon the ultimate burden of proof. The court held that imposition of sentence was a matter within the sound discretion of the trial court and that defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the trial court.
