People v. Griffin


1-90-2101


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


247 Ill. App. 3d 1; 616 N.E.2d 1242; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 506; 186 Ill. Dec. 610



April 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 7, 1993. Released for Publication August 20, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOHN WASILEWSKI, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his post-trial motion after his conviction of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentence of two concurrent terms of seven years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that insufficient evidence supported his conviction for criminal sexual assault based on accomplice liability, that his trial was unfair based on the prosecutor's comments and defects in the jury's charge, and that he was entitled to a remand for resentencing. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment except that it vacated one conviction for criminal sexual assault. The court held that accomplice liability was proved because a rational trier of fact could have found that defendant facilitated in the commission aggravated criminal sexual assault. Defendant was present at the scene and drove the car in which the assault was committed. Nor did defendant report the incident. Moreover, defendant waived his objection to the prosecutor's comments by omitting it from his post-trial motion. The error was, however, was harmless in light of the overwhelming evidence of guilt. The jury was properly charged because unanimity was required only as to guilt and any error resulting from the inclusion of accountability language did not affect the outcome of defendant's trial. Nevertheless, the court vacated one of defendant's convictions, which was improperly entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction for one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault, vacated the other count for the same offense, and affirmed his sentence of seven years' imprisonment.

Niziolek v. Chicago Transit Auth.


1-91-2368


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


251 Ill. App. 3d 537; 620 N.E.2d 1097; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 509; 189 Ill. Dec. 780



April 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 27, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Odas Nicholson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injury victim sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed the personal injury action he had filed against defendants, Chicago Transit Authority (CTA) and its employee. The trial court held that plaintiff failed to give proper written notice as required by the § 41 of the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act (Transit Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 341 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a personal injury action against the CTA and its employee seeking to recover damages for injuries he allegedly sustained when his automobile was struck from behind by a CTA bus. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted CTA's motion to dismiss. Pursuant to para. 341, plaintiff was required to file notice with the secretary of the board and the CTA's general counsel within six months of the incident. The court rejected plaintiff's "substantial compliance" argument, holding that he had the burden of strictly complying with para. 341. The court also found that plaintiff did not raise a material question of fact on the issue of whether the CTA was estopped from asserting his failure to give proper written notice as a bar to his claim. Therefore, the trial judge was correct in disposing of plaintiff's complaint as a matter of law. Plaintiff was not denied equal protection of the law because the differing notice and limitations periods of the Transit Act and the Tort Immunity Act bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state purpose. The Transit Act's limitation provisions also applied to the employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the personal injury action that plaintiff had filed against the CTA and its employee.

People v. Windsor


No. 3--92--0613


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District

April 7, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Fulton County, Illinois. No. 91-CF-91. Honorable Charles H. Wilhelm, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Fulton County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful commercialization of fish.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sitting in the co-defendant's truck when the co-defendant approached with an agent for the Department of Conservation. Defendant did not speak to the agent and exited the truck toward the end of the agent's conversation with the co-defendant. The co-defendant had dressed bluegill and bass in the truck that were filleted and ready for frying. Defendant was charged and convicted of unlawful commercialization of fish. 515 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5 -- 25. On review, the court found that defendant did not receive any money in the transaction and took no part in the conversation. Defendant admitted, however, that he picked up the co-defendant and took him to the meeting place for the express purpose of selling fish. The court concluded that defendant's admission established beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's action furthered the unlawful sale of fish. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that convicted defendant of unlawful commercialization of fish was affirmed.

People v. Galvan


No. 1-90-2094


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


244 Ill. App. 3d 298; 614 N.E.2d 391; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 442; 185 Ill. Dec. 257



March 31, 1993, Decided  
March 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1993. Released for Publication June 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Shelvin Singer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that entered a jury conviction for aggravated arson and for the murder of two persons who died in a house fire and that sentenced him to natural life imprisonment without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told an individual that he had started a fire by throwing an ignited bottle of gasoline at a house, and that individual made a statement to the police. Defendant was arrested and confessed to the crime, and a jury convicted him of aggravated arson and murder. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in finding that the individual who had made the statement against defendant was reliable because he was an identified person with no criminal background and no motivation to lie. Defendant also failed to show that the individual had been coerced into making his statement. The trial court allowed defendant to sufficiently cross-examine a detective about his experience. Defendant was not denied a fair trial by the prosecutor's comments during closing argument because he was not substantially prejudiced. The trial court properly refused to admit evidence of others who had threatened to burn the same house because defendant failed to identify those people or offer any evidence of motive or location of those people at the time of the crime. The court concluded that Illinois' felony sentence statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that convicted defendant of aggravated arson and of the murder of two persons who died in a house fire and that sentenced him to natural life imprisonment without parole.

People v. Weninger


No. 3--92--0346


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


243 Ill. App. 3d 719; 611 N.E.2d 77; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 474; 183 Ill. Dec. 224


November 18, 1992, Submitted  
March 30, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Released for Publication May 4, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County. No. 91 CF 638. The Hon. John Donald O'Shea, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) that convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised two issues: 1) whether the evidence presented was sufficient to prove him guilty of the offenses beyond a reasonable doubt; and (2) whether the trial court erred in allowing the victim to testify by means of closed circuit television, out of the presence of defendant, pursuant to § 106B-1 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 106B-1 (1991). In affirming, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to find defendant guilty of the offenses beyond a reasonable doubt based on the Collins standard of review, which provided that the test was whether, after viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court further held that the portion of § 106B-1 at issue only required testimony sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the child would have suffered severe emotional distress that was likely to cause the child to suffer severe adverse effects. The court concluded that defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and of criminal sexual assault.

People v. Major

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division

March 26, 1993, Decided

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE HOWARD T. SAVAGE, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, entered judgment of his conviction for first degree murder, and which sentenced defendant to 30 years in the state department of corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the circuit court of first degree murder following a bench trial, and sentenced to 30 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed. Upon review, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that defendant's claim that the circuit court's admission of rebuttal testimony that the victim did not own or ever carry a gun was erroneous was waived because the claim was not raised in defendant's post-trial motion; further, the court held that, even if not waived, the admission of the testimony was not reversible error, and any error which may have occurred was harmless. The court held that defendant also waived his claim of error concerning the length of his sentence; however, again, the court held that even if the issue had not been waived, there was no reversible error, and the circuit court was within its discretion in deciding that, in light of all of the evidence, including that offered in mitigation, a 30 year sentence was appropriate. The court also rejected defendant's contention that the Illinois homicide statute violated due process because the statute had been previously considered, and had been consistently held constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first degree murder conviction and his sentence of 30 years in the state department of corrections.

People v. Holman


1-90-1466


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


250 Ill. App. 3d 503; 620 N.E.2d 1222; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 392; 189 Ill. Dec. 905



March 23, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1993. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing July 27, 1993. Released for Publication October 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOSEPH J. URSO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his post-conviction petition alleging he was denied effective assistance of counsel, his arrest should have been quashed, his statements should have been suppress, and the sentencing statute was unconstitutional. Defendant was previously convicted and sentenced for murder, rape, residential burglary, robbery, and home invasion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was previously convicted and sentenced for murder and other crimes. After exhausting his appeals for the convictions, defendant filed a post-conviction petition, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the petition. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel due to the failure to argue that the findings of fact as to the motion to suppress were erroneous because the trial court's finding of voluntariness as to defendant's statements was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel due to the failure to argue lack of probable cause for arrest because the statement by defendant's accomplice implicating defendant attenuated any taint surrounding the arrest. Defendant was not denied his rights to equal protection and due process because the factors in mitigation and aggravation in § 5-8-1(a)(1) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-2(a)(1) (1989), provided the necessary guidance for the trial court to decide whether a particular defendant should be sentenced to life imprisonment or to an extended term.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's post-conviction petition because defendant was not denied ineffective assistance of counsel or his rights to due process or equal protection. The provision of the Unified Code of Corrections under which defendant was sentenced was found to be constitutional both on its fact and as applied.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied the village's motion to dismiss and granted summary judgment to plaintiffs, trustee and landowner, in the trustee's action seeking a declaration that two village ordinances purporting to regulate an unincorporated parcel of property were void with respect to the property.


OVERVIEW: The trustee, in an effort to commercially develop its parcel of residential-zoned unincorporated property, filed a petition with the county for rezoning of the property. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the village's motion to dismiss the trustee's complaint for a declaration that two village ordinances were void and granting summary judgment to the trustee.

People v. Carter


No. 1--91--0188


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


245 Ill. App. 3d 7; 614 N.E.2d 167; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 354; 185 Ill. Dec. 33



March 19, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Released for Publication June 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE LEO E. HOLT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which rejected his theories of justified use of force and second degree murder and found him guilty of first degree murder under the Illinois murder statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1, 9- 2 (1987), which defendant alleged was unconstitutional because it violated principles of due process, equal protection, and separation of powers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified that he shot the decedent in self-defense because the decedent had a gun. While being questioned, defendant told the police that he did not know who shot the decedent and that he did not mention that the decedent had a gun. Defendant was convicted and his conviction was upheld. The court agreed with the trial court that defendant's failure to inform the police of critical details belied his self-defense claim. Similarly, a defense witness's failure to tell police that defendant shot the deceased to protect himself further weakened the claim. Defendant was advised of his right to remain silent and his right to speak to an attorney before questioning. Waiving those rights, defendant failed to tell police at the first opportunity that the deceased was the aggressor and that he shot the deceased only to protect himself. The court held that a reasonable person would have informed police of these critical circumstances. Although the trial court erred in finding that the State presented testimony of two eyewitnesses when there was only one, it was not reversible error. The court found the statute to be constitutional, declining to diverge from established precedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Dempsey


No. 5--91--0033


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


242 Ill. App. 3d 568; 610 N.E.2d 208; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 358; 182 Ill. Dec. 784



March 19, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 90-CF-147. Honorable Snyder Howell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) from his convictions and sentences for the offenses of aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal transmission of the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV).


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court did not err in finding the child victim competent to testify, and no prejudice resulted from the failure to hold a pretrial competency hearing. The jury chose to believe the victim's trial testimony, and its conclusion was not unreasonable. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a new trial based on the victim's recanting testimony. Evidence of child sexual abuse syndrome was admissible under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115(7.2) (1989), and where the subject of the victim's recantation was first raised in the cross-examination of the victim during the state's case in chief, there was no error in the admission during the state's case in chief of evidence of the syndrome. Defendant's conduct fell within the proscription of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12(16.2)(a)(1) (1989), that statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, and defendant had no standing to raise the constitutionality of the statute as it could apply to others. The convictions were not based upon the same physical act, and both could stand. The sentencing judge was so prejudiced by fear of HIV that he let improper factors influence him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for aggravated criminal sexual assault and criminal transmission of HIV were affirmed, defendant's sentences were vacated, and the cause was remanded for resentencing with directions that it be assigned to a different judge on remand.

People ex rel. Hansen v. Phelan


1-92-2915, 1-92-2931 (Cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


255 Ill. App. 3d 113; 628 N.E.2d 160; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 328; 194 Ill. Dec. 663



March 16, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed June 3, 1993. As Corrected February 4, 1994. Released for Publication March 11, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS J. O'BRIEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, four members of the county board of commissioners, initiated an action against defendants to enjoin implementation of defendant president's executive order that directed the restoration of elective abortion services at a local hospital. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied plaintiffs' petition for a preliminary injunction and dissolved the temporary restraining order that it had previously entered. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: From 1973 to 1980, elective abortions were regularly performed at a local public hospital. In 1980, the former president of the board issued a directive to the hospital's medical director ordering the immediate cessation of elective abortion services there, except those necessary to save the life of the woman. In 1992, the new defendant president issued an executive order that revoked the former president's directive. Plaintiffs contested defendant president's authority to restore elective abortion services at the hospital. The court affirmed the denial of plaintiffs' petition for a preliminary injunction, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that plaintiffs failed to establish a likelihood of success on the merits. First, the board did not have a policy that prohibited defendant president from resuming the performance of elective abortions at the hospital. Second, defendant president had the delegated authority to order the resumption of such services. Plaintiffs' only recourse was to seek to override defendant president's effective veto of the former president's directive by garnering a four-fifths vote of the board members, including themselves.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Nitz


No. 5--89--0784


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


242 Ill. App. 3d 209; 610 N.E.2d 1289; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 314; 183 Ill. Dec. 45



March 9, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 29, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Massac County; No. 89-CF-55, the Hon. Donald Lowery, Judge, presiding.
People v. Nitz, 143 Ill. 2d 82, 572 N.E.2d 895, 1991 Ill. LEXIS 23, 157 Ill. Dec. 431 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Massac County (Illinois). The trial court entered judgment on a jury verdict convicting her of first-degree murder, and the trial court sentenced her to natural life in prison.


OVERVIEW: The headless body of a homosexual man was found in his car trunk near a camping area. An eyewitness testified she saw defendant's husband hit a man on the back of the head with a baseball bat, that defendant and her husband put the man in the trunk of his car, that defendant's husband drove away in defendant's car, and that defendant followed her husband in the victim's car. Other witnesses testified regarding the extreme hatred that defendant's husband had for homosexuals. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. The court affirmed. The indictments adequately informed defendant that she was charged with murder, and the prosecution's evidence indicated she had participated in the murder as a silent partner. Defendant admitted that she joined her husband on a spending spree with the victim's credit cards following the victim's death. Defendant had not shown any prejudice from the state's failure to prove the instrumentality of death; defendant had not relied on the state's theory of the method of murder to prepare her defense. The trial court properly sentenced her to natural life in prison rather than an extended term after considering facts in mitigation and aggravation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for first-degree murder.

People v. Nelson


No. 1-91-1199


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for murder and home invasion by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and home invasion and sentenced to 25 years imprisonment. Defendant contended he was denied a fair trial when the trial court relied on speculation and extra-evidentiary conclusions regarding the effects of PCP on the decedent. The court concluded there was a sufficient basis from which the trial court could properly infer that decedent was helpless at the time of his death. The court determined it could reasonably be inferred that decedent was unable to defend himself because he had consumed narcotics and alcohol. Defendant contended the evidence could have supported second degree murder. The court deemed this argument unpersuasive. The court held defendant was not denied a fair trial. Defendant argued he was denied his constitutional right to confrontation and cross-examination of witnesses against him. The court held that defendant was not denied his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and home invasion.

People v. Lance


No. 1--91--2804


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


243 Ill. App. 3d 380; 612 N.E.2d 53; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 259; 183 Ill. Dec. 796



February 26, 1993, Decided  
February 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 28, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DENNIS PORTER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence of delivery of a controlled substance from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming that sections 401(a)(2)(A) and 102(h) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1401(a)(2)(A), 1102(h) (1989), upon which his conviction was predicated violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of unlawful delivery of more than 15 grams of cocaine. Defendant appealed. He admitted that he arranged and participated in a planned sale of cocaine, but contended that the statutes impermissibly failed to differentiate between an attempted delivery of a controlled substance and the completed act. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. The court determined that a rational basis existed for the legislature's decision to treat those persons caught in the act of dealing drugs the same as those persons who were caught in the act of dealing drugs but did not consummate the act. The court found that the difference between these two groups to be one without a distinction and that their equal treatment was rationally related to the legislative purpose of deterring drug trafficking and abuse. The court concluded that defendant's rights to equal protection or due process were not violated by the legislature defining the offense of delivery of a controlled substance to include an attempted delivery and penalizing both equally.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of unlawful delivery of more than 15 grams of cocaine.

 

898 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Novak


No. 1--91--0539


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


242 Ill. App. 3d 836; 611 N.E.2d 1203; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 210; 183 Ill. Dec. 555



February 23, 1993, Decided  
February 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Released for Publication April 28, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed June 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Paul T. Foxgrover, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38 para. 12-14(b)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(b)(1) (1989). The court affirmed his conviction. The court held that the trial court's response to the jury's note that it was hung was appropriate. An instruction to continue deliberations must be simple, neutral, and not coercive. The test of a proper instruction was whether it imposed such confusion and pressure on the jury to reach a verdict that the accuracy and integrity of the verdict became uncertain. The legislature could enact statutes governing judicial procedure without violating the separation of powers. The court's refusal to dismiss prospective jurors for cause did not prejudice defendant because he did not demonstrate that defendant was forced to accept another objectionable juror after exhausting his peremptory challenges. Evidence of defendant's similar offenses with other children was admissible to establish defendant's modus operandi. Defendant was not entitled to his requested lesser-included offense instruction because aggravated criminal sexual abuse was not a lesser-included offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because a statute could govern judicial procedure. The trial court's instruction that the jury continue deliberating and that it was still quite early was a simple, neutral, and noncoercive instruction. Evidence of similar offenses was admissible to show defendant's modus operandi. The aggravated criminal sexual abuse was not a lesser-included offense of aggravated criminal sexual assault.

 

899 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Board of Trustees of Addison Fire Protection Dist. No. 1 Pension Fund v. Stamp


No. 2--92--0406


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


241 Ill. App. 3d 873; 608 N.E.2d 1274; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 217; 181 Ill. Dec. 800


January 20, 1993, Submitted  
February 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CH0749. The Hon. John W. Darrah, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Director of the Department of Insurance (Director) appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) granting summary judgment and a permanent injunction in favor of plaintiff pension board. The board had sought to enjoin the Director from threatening or demanding that the pension board exclude those service credits to fire fighters mandated by a previous declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: The issues were whether a prior declaratory judgment precluded the Director from questioning the pension board's actions; whether the Director exceeded his authority in questioning the pension board's actions; and whether the injunction was improper because the dispute was not ripe, because the pension board failed to exhaust administrative remedies, and because the pension board failed to establish the necessary elements for an injunction. The court held that res judicata and collateral estoppel did not apply to preclude the Director from questioning the actions of the pension board. The Director did not order the pension board to change a policy, but sought to reverse the adjudicatory decisions themselves. Because the administrative action was beyond the authority delegated to the Director by the Pension Code, it was void. The pension board's statutory challenge was ripe for judicial review. The trial court did not fail to observe the exhaustion doctrine when it heard the request for an injunction. The pension board established a threat of irreparable harm and the lack of an adequate remedy at law, and the trial court properly issued a permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Kochan v. Owens-Corning Fiberglass Corp.


No. 5--91--0191


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


242 Ill. App. 3d 781; 610 N.E.2d 683; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 241; 182 Ill. Dec. 814; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,751



February 23, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 6, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 86-L-1650. No. 86-L-1651. No. 86-L-1653. No. 87-L-870. No. 87-L-498. Honorable Gordon E. Maag, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, affirmed as modified in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, asbestosis patients and others, brought an action against defendant manufacturer seeking recovery for personal injury resulting from their exposure to asbestos-containing products. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) rendered judgment in favor of the asbestosis patients, and the manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the manufacturer argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by precluding it from introducing evidence that the asbestosis patients were exposed to asbestos-containing products manufactured by other companies not present at trial, and by denying its motion for change of venue. The court held: (1) evidence of exposures of the asbestosis patients to other manufacturer's products was not relevant in determining whether exposure to manufacturer's product was a substantial factor in causing their injury; (2) the manufacturer was not entitled to a change of venue under Ill. Code Civ. P., 2-1001(a)(2), Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1001(a)(2) because the trial judge's ruling on the motion for clarification and for sanctions was a ruling on a substantive issue; (3) the evidence showed that the manufacturer was aware of the hazards of asbestos, chose not to disclose the information, and failed to place warning labels on the product at the time it knew of the hazards of the product; and (4) the manufacturer's conduct amounted to an utter indifference to or conscious disregard for the safety of others. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to warrant punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the asbestosis patients in part, conditionally affirmed the judgment in part, and remanded with directions.

People v. Bowen


No. 4--92--0206


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


241 Ill. App. 3d 608; 609 N.E.2d 346; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 185; 182 Ill. Dec. 43


September 15, 1992, Oral Argument Held  
February 18, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 26, 1993. As Corrected May 6, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 91CF1254. The Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) convicted and sentenced defendant for two counts of criminal sexual assault and one count of unlawful restraint in violation of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 12 - 13(a)(1), 10 - 3(a) (1991). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim asserted that, while lying on top of her, defendant inserted his fingers and penis into her vagina. Defendant admitted having sexual intercourse with the victim, but he claimed that it was consensual. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for two counts of criminal sexual assault and one count of unlawful restraint. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for criminal sexual assault, holding that the victim's testimony was sufficient evidence to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. As such, defendant's ineffective assistance claim failed because the result would not have been different "but for" the alleged errors. However, the court vacated defendant's unlawful restraint conviction because the act of lying on top of the victim was part of the conduct for which defendant was convicted of sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for criminal sexual assault, but vacated his conviction for unlawful restraint.

Roth v. Saint Elizabeth's Hosp.


No. 5--92--0227


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


241 Ill. App. 3d 407; 607 N.E.2d 1356; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 161; 180 Ill. Dec. 843



February 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 91-MR-271. The Hon. James M. Radcliffe, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner administratrix brought an action against respondent hospital to discover the identity of persons who may be responsible in damages under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224, 134 Ill. 2d R. 224. The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) held a doctor and his lawyers in contempt for failure to respond to the administratrix's request for production of medical records and incarcerated them. The doctor and lawyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court's order of incarceration was entered in an attempt to coerce the doctor and his lawyers to accede to the administratrix's demands for information in an action brought under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224, 134 Ill. 2d R. 224. The court concluded that the circuit court was wrong in entering an order of contempt. The order's immediate implementation, lack of obstreperous conduct to support it, and wrong legal analysis required reversal. The circuit court decided to jail the doctor without regard to his patients. None of the jailed parties exhibited any disrespect during the proceeding. The court found that (1) rule 224 did not allow discovery as extensive as that sought and ordered, (2) the committee comments were contrary to the circuit court's construction, (3) the cases construing the rule did not support the circuit court's interpretation, (4) contrary to the circuit judge's thought, the supreme court's denial of the doctor's earlier petition for a supervisory order did not act as an approval of his management of the proceedings; and (5) the case's factual circumstances make it clear that the use of rule 224 was both unnecessary and unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment of contempt and dismissed the rule 224 petition.

People v. Jones


1-91-0038, 1-91-0070 (Cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


264 Ill. App. 3d 556; 636 N.E.2d 604; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 107; 201 Ill. Dec. 172



February 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 1, 1994. Released for Publication August 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JOAN M. CORBOY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendants guilty of two counts each of criminal sexual assault, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-13 (1989), and sentenced each of them to five years' incarceration. Defendants sought review of their convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with sexual assault. Prior to trial, the state filed a motion in limine under the rape shield statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-7 (1989), seeking to exclude any evidence regarding the victim's sexual reputation or her prior sexual activity with anyone other than defendants. In response, one of the defendants claimed that he had watched the victim perform consensual sexual acts on a third-party on a prior occasion and that such evidence was admissible. The trial court granted the motion and subsequently found defendants guilty. Defendants appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in granting the motion in limine and that their sentences were excessive when compared to the reduced sentenced received by a third co-defendant, who pleaded guilty to lesser charges.. The court affirmed, holding (1) the evidence defendants sought to introduce was inadmissible because "voyeurism" did not fall within the rape shield law's definition of admissible "past sexual conduct," (2) the rape shield law did not violate defendants' right of confrontation, and (3) defendants' sentences were not excessive because they and the co-defendant were not similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences.

People v. Berquist


Nos. 2-91-0970 through 2-91-0989 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

January 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 1, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 91-CM-497 through 91-CM-515, 91-CM-517. Honorable Richard A. Lucas and Honorable James W. Jerz, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted them of criminal trespass to real property under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 21-3(a) (1991), after they refused to leave the abortion facility where they were protesting.


OVERVIEW: Defendants arrived at an abortion facility carrying picket signs, went past the reception desk, sat on the floor of a hallway leading to the operating rooms while reading Bibles and reciting prayers, or sat on the front steps and blocked the entrance. Defendants were arrested after being informed that they were trespassing and refusing to leave the premises. The trial court granted the state's motion in limine, which barred defendants from presenting any evidence in support of the defense of necessity. The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting the motion in limine and their convictions. The court held that the defense of necessity was not a valid defense to the criminal trespass of a facility that performed abortions. The facility only performed abortions during the first trimester, which was constitutionally protected. The defense of necessity was not available to trespasses that interfered with constitutional rights. Defendants were not entitled to an instruction on necessity because the trial court found that the affirmative defense was unavailable as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for criminal trespass to real property.

Warbucks Inv. Ltd. Partnership v. Rosewell


No. 1--91--1586


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of the 1990 amendment to § 245 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 726 (1991). Appellee, Collector of Cook County (Collector), also sought review of the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The company contended that the Act as amended was unconstitutional. The Collector contended that the company's intervention was improper. The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment allowing the company's intervention and vacated the trial court's findings regarding the constitutionality of the Act, as the constitutional challenges addressed in the trial court's order were only raised by the company's pleadings. The court noted that although the intervention statute was remedial and should be liberally construed, the company neglected to set forth its specific interest in the matter and how it would be affected by the amendment to the Act. The court held that the absence of specific facts in the company's complaint that established its identity and showed how it would be affected by the amendment at issue was fatal to its petition to intervene, and it held that the trial judge should have denied the company's petition to intervene.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment allowing the company's intervention and vacated the trial court's findings regarding the constitutionality of the Act.

People v. Leach


Nos. 2-90-0998 & 2-90-1407 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


245 Ill. App. 3d 644; 612 N.E.2d 825; 1993 Ill. App. LEXIS 14; 183 Ill. Dec. 898



January 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Unpublished Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published January 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CF-1245. Honorable Perry R. Thompson, Judge, Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CF-2011. Honorable John J. Nelligan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 2-90-0998, Affirmed.

No. 2-90-1407, Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the state challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motions to quash his arrest and suppress evidence with respect to two separate indictments.


OVERVIEW: At a hearing pursuant to one indictment, the trial court held that defendant's warrantless arrest violated the Fourth Amendment, and granted his motions to quash the arrest and suppress all evidence. In the second matter, defendant's motion for an order applying collateral estoppel to his motions to quash and suppress was granted. On appeal, defendant argued that the court lacked jurisdiction to address the appeal as to the second matter because the state's notice of appeal was not timely filed. The court dismissed the appeal, concluding that the trial court's order in the second matter, though nominally an order granting collateral estoppel, was in substance and effect a suppression order which granted defendant all the relief he sought in his earlier motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. Thus, the order was immediately appealable. The fact that the trial judge continued the cause for status was not material. Although the order stated only that the defendant's motion for collateral estoppel was granted, that statement, by the very nature of collateral estoppel, incorporated the factual findings and implicit legal conclusions of the earlier suppression order.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal with respect to one case and affirmed the trial court's judgment granting defendant's motion to quash his arrest and suppress evidence in the second case.

Hoem v. Zia


No. 4-92-0048


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


239 Ill. App. 3d 601; 606 N.E.2d 818; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2178; 179 Ill. Dec. 986



December 31, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 4, 1993. As Corrected February 2, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed June 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 90L65. Honorable John K. Grenias, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executor filed an action for medical malpractice against defendants, doctors, hospital, and clinic, after the doctors failed to diagnose the heart condition that killed the deceased. The Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) rendered judgment in favor of the doctors, hospital, and clinic pursuant to a jury verdict. The executor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The executor assigned various points of error. The court found that the trial court erred in allowing one of the doctors to testify to about what the decedent said to the doctor in order to explain the doctor's notes because the admission of such testimony violated the Dead Man's Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-201 (1991), and because testimony by the executor's expert regarding the doctor's notes did not open the door to the deceased's conversation. The court also found that the trial court erred in preventing an expert called by the executor in rebuttal from testifying to the standard of care for pulmonologists on the grounds that she could have presented the witness in the case in chief; where the rebuttal evidence was otherwise proper, it was not barred merely because it could have been brought in the case in chief. The court also found that the trial court did not err in allowing the doctor the deceased was scheduled to see the day after he died to testify as an expert for the defendants because the doctor never saw the deceased, had not reviewed the deceased's medical records, and no doctor-patient relationship existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision in favor of the doctors, hospital, and clinic and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Terneus


No. 4-92-0383


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


239 Ill. App. 3d 669; 607 N.E.2d 568; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2127; 180 Ill. Dec. 499



December 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 24, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 92CF38, 91CF703. Honorable Jerry L. Patton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which accepted his guilty plea for aggravated sexual assault, sentenced him to 11 years in prison, and then ordered him to pay the cost of the proceedings. Defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court denied him procedural due process by entering a money judgment for costs without notice following his guilty plea. He further argued that the judgment improperly modified the plea agreement reached with the state. The court disagreed and affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 180-3 (1991) stated that when any person was convicted of an offense under any statute, or at common law, the court had to enter judgment that the offender pay the costs of the prosecution. The court held that defendant's notice of the requirement that the trial court impose costs on his conviction was premised upon the doctrine of law that one was presumed to know the law and ignorance of it was no excuse. The court held that the trial court was not responsible for advising defendant of the civil or collateral consequences of his guilty plea. The court held that the trial judge did not modify the plea agreement merely by inserting the condition that defendant pay the court costs because the trial judge was not only authorized, but was required to have defendant pay the court costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea after he was ordered to pay the costs of the proceedings.

Patrick Media Group, Inc. v. Ad-Ex, Inc.


No. 1-91-0298


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 487; 608 N.E.2d 427; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2122; 181 Ill. Dec. 354



December 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Anthony J. Scotillo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff billboard corporation against defendant competitor seeking to enjoin defendant from maintaining advertising signs, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint and certified a question to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant, a competitor of plaintiff, seeking to enjoin defendant from maintaining advertising signs on grounds that the signs violated applicable provisions of the Municipal Code of the City of Chicago, a home rule unit. Defendant moved to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the language of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 24, para. 11-13-1, rendered Ill. Rev. Stat. 1991, ch. 24, para. 11-13-15 inapplicable to alleged violations of a City of Chicago ordinance, and plaintiff therefore lacked standing to bring the action. The trial judge denied defendant's motion and certified the issue on appeal. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Section 11-13-1 was applicable, in the main, to home rule and non-home rule municipalities. The court found that plaintiff had standing to maintain the action. The court did not believe that the 1971 amendment restricted the power of home rule communities, rather it enhanced their right to decide their own destiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint and remanded for further consideration.

Smith v. Normal


No. 4--92--0430


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


238 Ill. App. 3d 944; 605 N.E.2d 727; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2060; 178 Ill. Dec. 933



December 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 20, 1993. As Corrected January 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 92MR4. Honorable William T. Caisley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which upheld appellees', a town, its Zoning Board of Appeals, and its building commissioner, ruling against the homeowner requiring him to change the lawful nonconforming use of his property from a rooming house to a single-family residence.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner owned a seven-bedroom house, which was located in an area zoned for single-family residences, in the town and rented the house to students. The rent generated an income of approximately $ 16,000 a year. He also rented the house during the summer for approximately $ 1,000 to $ 1,200. The Zoning Board of Appeals sustained the determination made by the building commissioner that the town's zoning code required the homeowner to change the lawful nonconforming use of his property from a rooming house to a single-family residence. The lower court upheld the board's ruling and the homeowner sought further review, arguing that the board's interpretation of the zoning code was contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence and that the applicable nonconforming-use provisions of the code were void for vagueness. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that prohibiting certain types of repair or extensive repair on structures devoted to a nonconforming use was a reasonable method for eliminating such nonconforming uses over time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding appellees' zoning ruling against a homeowner.

 

912 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sonntag


No. 2--91--0887


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


238 Ill. App. 3d 854; 605 N.E.2d 1064; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2046; 179 Ill. Dec. 50


November 19, 1992, Submitted  
December 18, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 29, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. Nos. 90-CF-488, 90-CF-490, 90-CF-492. Hon. Susan F. Hutchinson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance and criminal drug conspiracy. He argued that the trial court erred in entering convictions of the inchoate offenses and substance ones, and that §§ 401(a)(7), 401(b)(7) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1401(a)(7), (b)(7) (1989), violated equal protection and due process.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that defendant waived the issue of improper sentencing when he failed to raise it either in his motion to vacate the guilty plea or in his motion to reconsider his sentence. However, under the plain error doctrine, the trial court vacated defendant's convictions and sentences for criminal drug conspiracy. The court affirmed the other conviction. The reversal of one conviction did not require that defendant be resentenced on the remaining conviction, as long as the trial court considered the offenses separately and sentenced defendant separately on each offense. Defendant had standing to challenge both sections of the statute since they equated grams of LSD with objects containing LSD. There was a rational basis for the State's choice of penalties for LSD distribution in that it intended to punish severely large-volume drug traffickers at any level. The equal protection clause did not deny the States the power to classify in their exercise of their police power and it gave broad latitude in classifying. Defendant did not dispute the number of objects containing LSD, indicating that the police had no difficulty in applying it, and the statute was not vague.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for criminal drug conspiracy and affirmed his conviction for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance.

Garcia v. Chicago


No. 1-91-3156


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 199; 608 N.E.2d 239; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2049; 181 Ill. Dec. 166



December 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE IRVING R. NORMAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found in favor of plaintiff cyclist in an action for injuries sustained by the cyclist while she rode her bicycle on a city sidewalk. The challenged decision found that of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 9-52-020(b) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The 27-year-old cyclist was injured while riding her bicycle on a city sidewalk. The city defended the action and raised the application of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 9-52-020(b), which prohibited bicycle riding on the sidewalks by persons over 12 years of age, in conjunction with § 3-102(a) of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 3-102(a) (1989). The trial court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause and the case proceeded to trial, with no mention of the ordinance made to the jury. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the cyclist and the city appealed. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and found that the city's objectives in passing the ordinance were legitimate and that the ordinance was rationally related to those objectives. The court held that the ordinance was constitutional and that the cyclist was not an intended and permitted user under § 3-102(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the cyclist. The court ruled that the ordinance was constitutional.

Buell v. Oakland Fire Protection Dist. Bd.


No. 4--92--0380


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


237 Ill. App. 3d 940; 605 N.E.2d 618; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2043; 178 Ill. Dec. 824



December 17, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Coles County; the Hon. Paul C. Komada, Judge, presiding. No. 89L98.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, ambulance service and its employee, challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois) denying their motion for leave to file an affirmative defense of immunity under the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Tort Immunity Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 5-106 (1991), against defendant joint tortfeasor's counterclaim for contribution in a personal injury action filed against them.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a passenger in an ambulance driven by the employee, was injured when the ambulance collided with a vehicle driven by the joint tortfeasor. The passenger filed an action for damages against the joint tortfeasor, the ambulance service, and the employee, and the joint tortfeasor filed a counterclaim against the ambulance service and the employee for contribution. After their motion for summary judgment raising § 5-106 was denied, the ambulance service and the employee filed a motion for leave to file an affirmative defense under § 5-106, which the trial court also denied. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that § 5-106 was an affirmative defense in an action for contribution. The court found that the Tort Immunity Act, which was enacted after the Joint Tortfeasor's Contribution Act, did not limit application of § 5-106 to direct actions and prevailed over the joint tortfeasor's right to contribution under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 302(a). The court found that application of § 5-106 of the Tort Immunity Act to the joint tortfeasor's claim for contribution did not violate due process or equal protection guarantees or special legislative proscription.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the ambulance service and the employee's motion for leave to file an affirmative defense of immunity against the tortfeasor's claim for contribution. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Cummings v. Beaton & Assocs.


1-91-2131 & 1-91-2492 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


249 Ill. App. 3d 287; 618 N.E.2d 292; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2052; 187 Ill. Dec. 701



December 17, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied March 31, 1993. Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. HONORABLE Alan J. Greiman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fast-food company challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff corporate officers in their breach of contract action. The officers filed a cross-appeal relating to their interest award and to the denial of their claim for attorney fees. The officers also challenged a ruling that dismissed defendants, detective agencies and individuals, from the case.


OVERVIEW: The officers claimed that the fast-food company violated a written settlement agreement in a subsequent bankruptcy court proceeding by encouraging its rejection in favor of a different settlement. The fast-food company argued that its conduct was justified by its "duty" to disclose the parties' earlier settlement negotiations to the bankruptcy court. The court affirmed the trial court's award of summary judgment in favor of the officers. The court held that the fast-food company breached the agreement where nothing on its face was ambiguous regarding the parties' intention to settle the officers' claims. The court found that the breach of contract could not be justified by references to ethics and public policy. The court rejected the fast-food company's argument that its breach was excused because the bankruptcy court's approval of the settlement agreement would not have been forthcoming in any event. The court held that the officers were not entitled to attorney fees based on the fast-food company's bad faith. The court concluded that the detective agencies and individuals were included in the scope of the settlement agreement and thus were properly dismissed from the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in all respects, including the determination of liability on the part of the fast-food company, the amount of damages, the amount of prejudgment interest, and the refusal to award attorney fees to the officers. The court also affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed the detective agencies and individuals from the case.

Phelan v. County Officers Electoral Bd.


1-92-2880, 1-92-2906 Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 368; 608 N.E.2d 215; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2027; 181 Ill. Dec. 142



December 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Francis Barth, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Republican judicial candidates, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that affirmed the decision of appellee Electoral Board to allow the names of appellee, Democratic judicial candidates, to be placed on the general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: In two elections, a Republican candidate was elected as the Republican nominee to run for office in the general election. No Democratic candidate ran and none was nominated by petition. Following the primary, the Democratic party nominated appellees as candidates by party resolution. Objections were filed to the Democratic nominees' placement on the general election ballot. They claimed that the nomination was unconstitutional because Ill. Const. art. VI, § 12(a) required candidates for judicial office to be nominated at primary elections or by petition. The court found that appellee Electoral Board had jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of a statute. It held that the trial court had original jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of a statute. The framers believed that the primary election of judicial candidates would be conducted in the same manner as primary elections for governor, implicitly including the right of political parties to fill vacancies in nomination for judicial office by resolution. Interpreting the constitutional provision to forbid a political party from filling vacancies in nomination would be a restrictive interpretation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Lockwood


NO. 1-90-3522


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 137; 608 N.E.2d 132; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 2002; 181 Ill. Dec. 59



December 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied June 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William J. Hibbler, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of aggravated arson and sentenced him to 12 years imprisonment following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of aggravated arson and sentenced him to 12 years imprisonment following a jury trial, he appealed. The court affirmed. Viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the jury's verdict. The evidence was sufficient to satisfy the definition of a burning. The court agreed with the trial court's finding that no rational basis existed upon which the jury could find defendant guilty of any of the lesser offenses instead of the greater offense of aggravated arson. The evidence establishing the presence of people in the building precluded the giving of an instruction on simple arson. The record was devoid of evidence tending to show that defendant acted recklessly. The trial court correctly refused to instruct the jury on a statute addressing criminal damage to property. Defendant failed to establish a constitutional infirmity in the aggravated arson statute as written or in its application to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated arson and sentence to 12 years imprisonment.

Almgren v. Rush-Presbyterian-St. Luke's Medical Ctr.


No. 1-89-3263


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 585; 608 N.E.2d 92; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1991; 181 Ill. Dec. 19



December 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Appeal as a Matter of Right Allowed March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dean J. Sodaro, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a malpractice action against defendant hospital based in part on the acts of a psychiatric resident who treated the patient at the hospital and issued a pass authorizing the patient to leave the hospital. The patient brought an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) permitting the hospital's attorneys to have private discussions with the psychiatric resident.


OVERVIEW: The patient was severely injured after leaving the hospital on the pass issued by the psychiatric resident. On appeal, the court held that the interlocutory order permitting the hospital to conduct an ex parte interview with the resident was reviewable under the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Confidentiality Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 801 et seq. (1991), and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307(a)(1), 134 Ill. 2d R. 307(a)(1), which did not conflict with each other, because the patient's privilege could not be effectively restored on review from the final judgment after trial and she could not be obtain immediate review by being found in contempt of the order. The court further held that the order was improper because § 10 of the Act established the hospital's undisputed right to discovery of information from the resident through appropriate court-supervised discovery channels, but provided no support for a special right to a private interview with the resident. The trial court could only decline to review the information in camera if it provided some other means of protecting the patient's right to limit disclosure of potentially damaging matters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order permitting the hospital to conduct a private interview with the psychiatric resident and remanded for court-supervised formal discovery.

Memorial Child Care v. Department of Revenue


No. 4--92--0309


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


238 Ill. App. 3d 985; 604 N.E.2d 530; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1934; 178 Ill. Dec. 274



November 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 1992. As Corrected January 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 91MR113. Honorable C. Joseph Cavanagh, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state department of revenue appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which reversed the decision of the department and granted tax-exempt status to three tracts of land owned by plaintiff hospital.


OVERVIEW: The hospital was granted a property tax exemption as a charitable organization pursuant to the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.7 (1989). The hospital operated a not-for-profit child care center on a contiguous parcel of property. The department found that the primary use of the child care's property was neither charitable nor educational and denied the hospital's application for tax exemption. The child care center was not profitable and provided a service to the employees of the hospital. The hospital contended that the child care center was reasonably necessary to fulfill the charitable objections of the hospital. The court held that property of charitable institutions qualified for a charitable exemption if the use of the property was exclusively charitable or reasonably necessary for accomplishing the goals of a charitable organization. The record in the instant case indicated that the area had a shortage of child care facilities and that the employees had difficulty finding child care that fit the hospital scheduling requirements. The child care center enabled the hospital to retain quality employees to better serve the needs of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the hospital qualified for a property tax exemption for its affiliate child care center.

Aken v. Board of Control of Lake County Area Vocational Center


No. 2--92--0056


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


237 Ill. App. 3d 97; 604 N.E.2d 524; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1921; 178 Ill. Dec. 268


November 10, 1992, Submitted  
November 25, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Jack Hoogasian, Judge, presiding. No. 91-MR-349.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint for a declaratory judgment of their tenure rights under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 24-11 (1991), and for an injunction prohibiting defendant Board of Control of Lake County Area Vocational Center from refusing to provide information concerning available positions.


OVERVIEW: The teachers, who were employees of a cooperative vocational education program under the Board's control, were dismissed due to a reduction in force, even though they had tenure. The teachers contended that they, like special education teachers, had "super-tenure" rights under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 24-11 (1991) in the school districts participating in the joint education program. The court rejected the argument that the statute granted the same tenure protections to teachers in all types of joint educational agreements. All joint agreements were not subsets of special education joint agreements. Special education joint agreements were species of joint agreements. The statute provided for "super-tenure" only for special education teachers. The legislature intended to treat special education teachers differently from other joint program teachers. The distinction between special education teachers and other classes of teachers in relation to tenure rights did not violate equal protection guarantees because the classification rationally advanced the objective of attracting and retaining professionals with highly particularized training and experience.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

Doe v. Calumet City


No. 1-90-1121


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


240 Ill. App. 3d 911; 609 N.E.2d 689; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1893; 182 Ill. Dec. 155



November 23, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DEAN SODARO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motions filed by defendant municipalities and police officers to dismiss the mother's claims of negligence, gender-based discrimination, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The mother alleged that the police officers failed to protect her and her minor children after an assailant entered her apartment and raped one of the children.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought the claims individually and on behalf of her children. The mother alleged that the police officers refused to break down the apartment door even after she informed them that the assailant was inside with her children. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed the mother's claims. The court found that (1) the mother failed to establish that a special duty was owed by the municipalities and police officers based on facts showing that her children were injured while they were under the direct and immediate control of the police officers. (2) The mother's claim of gender-based discrimination was not supported by any established municipal policy nor by the questions asked by one police officer, who may have been attempting to determine if there was a domestic dispute in order to decide how to proceed. (3) The police officers' actions in initially not entering the apartment and in removing the mother from the area did not establish the claim of intentional infliction of emotional distress because the police officers were likely acting to protect the mother and not with an intent to inflict her with emotional distress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the motions to dismiss the mother's claims.

That condition alone was reversed and the matter was remanded for reconsideration of probation conditions.

People v. De Oca


No. 1--91--1165


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


238 Ill. App. 3d 362; 606 N.E.2d 332; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1808; 179 Ill. Dec. 500



November 12, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Paul T. Foxgrover, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of the charge of second degree murder, after he admitted that he shot the victim, but claimed he acted in self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction in the trial court of the charge of second degree murder, and asserted that the trial court in finding that appellant was the initial aggressor, that the state disproved appellant's assertion of self-defense beyond a reasonable doubt, that the burden was improperly placed on appellant to prove his innocence, that the trial court omitted from evidence appellant's statements to the police, and that the Illinois murder statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and noted that the evidence of events that preceded the shooting was contradictory. The court held that it was the trial court's duty to resolve contradictions in the evidence, and that the trial court did not err when it determined that appellant was the aggressor at the time of the shooting. The court held that one element of appellant's assertion of self-defense was negated by the trial court's determination that appellant was the aggressor. The court held that the trial court's expression of disbelief of appellant's version of events did not shift the burden of proof on appellant to prove his innocence, and that his prior statements to police were properly excluded from evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the trial court properly resolved the conflict in the evidence, and found that appellant was the aggressor at the time of the shooting.
