People v. Marsan


No. 1--89--1168


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


238 Ill. App. 3d 470; 606 N.E.2d 344; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1803; 179 Ill. Dec. 512



November 12, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Howard T. Savage, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced defendant for possession with intent to deliver 900 grams or more of a controlled substance (cocaine), pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401.1(3) (1987).


OVERVIEW: After defendant's arrest, police retrieved a gun and a brown paper bag containing what proved to be cocaine behind soft drink machines where defendant had been seen squatting. Initially, the court granted a sentencing rehearing after defendant argued, in part, that this was his first criminal offense, and that he had a good work history and study record. Upon reconsideration of the issue, the court held that the trial court properly sentenced defendant for possession with intent to deliver 900 grams or more of a controlled substance. In pertinent part, the court noted that it was undisputed that defendant's sentence was at the low end of the statutory range of sentencing for the offense. Thus, given the seriousness of the offense, the nature and circumstances of the case, and defendant's criminal history, the court could not say that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing defendant. Lastly, the court held that defendant's argument that he was a first-time offender was irrelevant under the statutory scheme, and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401.1(3) (1987), was not unconstitutional because of the need to eliminate the threat to society from drugs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for possession with intent to deliver 900 grams or more of a controlled substance.

People v. Morris


No. 2--90--1404


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


237 Ill. App. 3d 140; 603 N.E.2d 1196; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1795; 177 Ill. Dec. 822



November 10, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Released for Publication December 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. David F. Smith, Judge, presiding. No. 90-CF-185.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, modified in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(1)(1989) and attempted murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4(a)(1989). Defendant also challenged the imposition of a 20-year term of incarceration for murder, followed by a 10-year consecutive sentence for attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed her boyfriend and attempted to kill the woman that he was caught having sex with. On appeal, defendant argued that (1) the trial judge tendered incorrect instructions on a special verdict of guilty but mentally ill, (2) the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing her to consecutive terms of imprisonment, and (3) the statutory scheme for first-degree and second-degree murder was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, modified, and vacated the judgment in part, and remanded the case. The court modified the judgment to reflect a guilty but mentally ill verdict to remove any prejudice that resulted from defense counsel's failure to tender proper instructions and ruled that a new sentencing hearing was needed. The court further determined that the consecutive sentences were proper because there was evidence to support the trial court's finding that the attempted murder of the woman was motivated by a criminal objective that differed from the motivation to murder the man. However, the court did comment on what sentence should be imposed upon remand. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the statutes were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed in part, modified in part, vacated in part, and remanded. The judgments that defendant was guilty of murder and of attempted murder were vacated. The judgments that defendant was guilty of murder but mentally ill and of attempted murder but mentally ill were entered. In addition, the case was remanded for resentencing on both of the modified convictions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff's request for declaratory relief directing that defendant's application for adjustment of claim, which was pending before the industrial commission, be dismissed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's prior application for adjustment of claim for a heart attack was dismissed for want of prosecution, defendant refiled a substantively identical application for adjustment of claim with the industrial commission. People v. Labosette


No. 4-91-0729


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


236 Ill. App. 3d 846; 602 N.E.2d 966; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1775; 177 Ill. Dec. 71



November 5, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 5, 1992. As Corrected January 22, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Morgan County; the Hon. J. David Bone, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed his first-degree murder conviction and 50 year prison sentence imposed on him by the Circuit Court of Morgan County (Illinois). Defendant argued that his trial lawyer ineffectively conceded his guilt and that the sentencing judge relied upon an unconstitutionally vague aggravating factor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with having deliberately shot and killed another man, and the prosecutor sought the death penalty. At trial, defendant's attorney conceded that defendant had shot the decedent, but argued that the circumstances were such that defendant's crime was second-degree murder rather than first-degree murder. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder nonetheless, and sentenced to 50 years of confinement owing to the cold, calculated, and premeditated manner in which he killed. The court, in affirming, held that trial counsel had not improperly conceded defendant's guilt of second-degree murder, inasmuch as that was a reasonable strategy given the number of eyewitnesses to defendant's act. It also held that the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravating factor was not impermissibly vague, and thus the trial judge could rely upon it in determining the proper sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction and 50 year prison sentence were affirmed.

Kleiboeker v. Industrial Com.


No. 5-90-0724WC


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District, Industrial Commission Division


236 Ill. App. 3d 1020; 602 N.E.2d 912; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1746; 177 Ill. Dec. 17



October 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County; the Hon. David Sauer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois), which granted judgment in favor of appellee employee and awarded him medical expenses, attorney fees, and additional compensation under the Workers' Compensation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.1 et seq. (1979).


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while in the course of employment. The trial court awarded him medical expenses, attorney fees, and additional compensation under the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.1 et seq. (1979), and the employer sought review. Pursuant to the Act, either party was allowed to present a certified copy of the award of the arbitrator to the trial court to enter a judgment in accordance therewith. The court found that full payment or tender of full payment of a final award was a complete defense to an application for judgment under the Act. However, the court determined that, if anything was properly due the employee after the final award, the trial court was required to enter judgment as provided. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1303 (1987) allowed interest on judgments. The court determined that the Act was not in violation of the equal protection provision because the means were rationally related to the statute's purpose. The court affirmed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded a judgment of the trial court, which granted judgment in favor of the employee, held that the employer was liable for his damages, and awarded him medical expenses, attorney fees, and additional compensation under the Workers' Compensation Act.

Anderson v. Forest Park


No. 1--91--1884


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


238 Ill. App. 3d 83; 606 N.E.2d 205; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1730; 179 Ill. Dec. 373



October 28, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Odas Nicholson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which dismissed her amended complaint alleging civil rights and other violations by defendants, city and employees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an eight count complaint against defendants, city and employees, alleging that her rights were violated and she suffered injuries as a result of being forcibly taken from her home and hospitalized for psychological evaluation. The court reversed the dismissal of counts charging a violation of rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, as the state immunity act could not control a federal remedy. The decision to remove plaintiff from her bedroom and seek medical evaluation was discretionary, and fell within the Illinois Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1-101 et seq. (1991), except for allegations of wilful and wanton, or intentional, conducts. Qualified immunity was an affirmative defense, and was not an appropriate ground for a motion to dismiss. It was properly pled after the filing of an answer, and could then be the subject of a summary judgment motion. The allegations of intentional infliction of emotional distress were properly stricken, as there was no allegation of extreme and outrageous conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the counts relating to civil rights violations by defendant employees, as the state immunity statute could not control federal remedies, and affirmed the dismissal of the remaining counts.

Daley v. Zebra Zone Lounge, Inc.


Nos. 1-91-1084, 1-91-1086 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


236 Ill. App. 3d 511; 603 N.E.2d 785; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1676; 177 Ill. Dec. 715



October 16, 1992, Decided  
October 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Edward C. Hofert, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mayor and city, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed their action for judicial review of the decision of the License Appeal Commission to reverse the mayor's refusal, in his capacity as the local liquor control commissioner, of defendant bars' requests for retail liquor licenses.


OVERVIEW: The mayor and the city filed an action seeking judicial review of the commission's decision reversing the mayor's refusal, in his capacity as the local liquor control commissioner, of the bars' requests for retail liquor licenses. The trial court dismissed the action, holding that the mayor and city did not have standing to seek administrative review. The court reversed, finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 154a (1991), which amended the Illinois Liquor Control Act to give the mayor standing to seek judicial review, applied retroactively although the law was changed after the complaint was filed but before final judgment of the circuit court was entered. The amendment was a reaction to overturn an erroneous judicial decision and clarified the existing statute to state that appeals from the local appeal commission were to be considered procedurally equivalent to those from the state commission. Retroactive application of the amended statute was the just and equitable result because, prior to the erroneous judicial decision, local liquor commissioners had successfully brought similar actions. The court remanded with directions to proceed with judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of plaintiffs' action for judicial review of the commission's decision to reverse the mayor's refusal of the bars' requests for retail liquor licenses.

People v. Rush


No. 1--87--3184


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


238 Ill. App. 3d 806; 606 N.E.2d 132; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1678; 179 Ill. Dec. 300



October 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 8, 1993. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Thomas A. Hett, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping for attacking a woman outside a bar.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant beat and raped her. Defendant questioned whether the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute was unconstitutional, whether the jury was improperly instructed, and whether his sentence was excessive. The court rejected defendant's contention that the statute was unconstitutional because the mental state of intent, knowledge, or recklessness was implied. Moreover, defendant waived any objections to jury instructions because defendant neither objected to the jury instructions given nor tendered alternate instructions. Defendant's motion for a new trial did not address improprieties in the jury instructions. However, the instruction on aggravated kidnapping omitted an essential element of the crime, but such error was harmless. Further, a trial judge's decision on sentencing was entitled to great weight and would not be disturbed absent a showing of an abuse of judicial discretion. Considering the sentencing hearing as a whole, the court found no abuse of discretion in sentencing defendant to an extended term of 55 years. The court, therefore, affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping.

In re C.A.


No. 1-91-3091


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


236 Ill. App. 3d 594; 603 N.E.2d 1171; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1677; 177 Ill. Dec. 797



October 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied February 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Walter Williams, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted appellee guardian's petition for authority to consent to the entry of a "do not resuscitate" (DNR) order on a minor infant's medical charts. Appellant argued that the order was outside of the authority of the juvenile court, that an improper standard was applied, and that the evidence was insufficient to justify the DNR order.


OVERVIEW: A minor infant was born several weeks prematurely, suffering from severe cocaine withdrawal and infection with the human immunodeficiency virus. Due to the infant's condition, and her 19-year-old parents' inability to care for her, the Illinois Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) petitioned to make the infant a ward of the court. Appellee DCFS guardianship administrator was appointed guardian and appellant guardian ad litem was appointed. Upon the request of the parents, appellee guardian petitioned the juvenile court for authority to consent to the entry of a "do not resuscitate" (DNR) order on the infant's medical charts. After a hearing, the juvenile court granted the petition. The order was stayed pending appellant's review. In affirming the decision, the court held that the juvenile court had jurisdiction to hear the case and to grant appellee permission to enter the DNR order. The court ruled that, because the consent or desire of the infant could not be determined, the juvenile court properly applied a best interests of the minor standard of review. The court found that the medical evidence was clear, convincing, and supported the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision and held that the juvenile court had jurisdiction to hear and decide the petition, that the juvenile court properly applied a best interests of the minor standard of review, and that the medical evidence was clear, convincing, and sufficient to support the grant of authority to enter the "do not resuscitate" order.

 

935 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


DeCastris v. Gutta


No. 2--91--0624


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


237 Ill. App. 3d 168; 604 N.E.2d 359; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1636; 178 Ill. Dec. 103


February 21, 1992, Submitted  
October 8, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 29, 1992. Rehearing denied November 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert R. Thomas, Judge, presiding. No. 86-L-970.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied the doctor's motion to reduce a general jury verdict in a medical malpractice case, where a judgment was rendered in favor of plaintiff patient, by an amount equal to 50 percent of collateral source payments for medical expenses and lost wages as provided for by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-1205(2) (1983).


OVERVIEW: Under the circumstances presented by the record on appeal, the court held that the mere fact that the verdict was a general one, did not preclude its reduction. The court held that the itemization of a verdict so as to reflect the monetary distribution between economic loss and noneconomic loss was mandatory and the refusal of such a tendered instruction was reversible error. However, no such itemized verdict form was either tendered or refused by the parties. As a result, the court held that, inasmuch as it was the court's duty to review a trial court's judgment and not its reasons therefore, and, assuming arguendo that the jury's verdict did include recovery for the patient's medical expenses and lost wages, the court nonetheless affirmed the trial court's refusal to reduce the judgment on the basis that the doctor failed to prove the reduction to which he was entitled. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the trial court's judgment was not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying a motion by the doctor to reduce a general jury verdict.

Stat., ch. 110, par. 7-104(b), of the order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied the property owner's motion to set aside the order granting plaintiff development company the authority to exercise the right of eminent domain.


OVERVIEW: The development company filed complaints for condemnation of two parcels owned by the property owner. The circuit court's order gave the development company the authority to exercise the right of eminent domain, awarded compensation, and vested the fee simple titles and the temporary easements in the development company. The property owner appealed, alleging that the two parcels were not properly subject to the eminent domain proceedings, and that his constitutional rights were violated in that he had not been given proper notice. The court held that although the property owner perfected his appeal on the three statutory issues, his lack of argument on those issues constituted a waiver of those issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, the circuit court's denial of the property owner's motion to set aside, and dismissed, for want of jurisdiction, the property owner's appeal challenging the constitutionality of the Act's provisions.

McDunn v. Williams


No. 1-92-1109


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Michael J. Murphy, Judge Presiding

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant incumbent sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which enjoined the Chicago Board of Election Commissioners (CBEC) from preparing an abstract and announcing the winner of an election in appellee candidate's election contest.


OVERVIEW: The candidate's contest petition was dismissed on the ground that the candidate had not timely filed the petition. The appellate court reversed the order dismissing the case and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings. On another trial of the issues, the circuit court entered judgment enjoining the CBEC from announcing the winner of the election until further order. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the circuit court properly concluded that the candidate's petition was not moot because the incumbent was never unequivocally declared the winner. The court found that circuit court did not err in refusing to count the ballots that were not initialed because the court was unwilling to carve out an exception to the initialing requirement set out in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-44 (1989). The court implemented an equitable remedy by ordering the incumbent to remain in his office until resignation and ordered the candidate to be placed on the ballot to fill the vacancy of another judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order enjoining the CBEC from announcing a winner of the election in the candidate's election contest. The court ordered that the incumbent remain in office until resignation and that the candidate be added to the general ballot to fill the vacancy of another judge.

Herriott v. Powers


No. 1-91-1964


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


236 Ill. App. 3d 151; 603 N.E.2d 654; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1569; 177 Ill. Dec. 584



September 29, 1992, Decided  
September 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Loretta C. Douglas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Village of Tinley Park Director of Public Works (director) sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded damages to appellee motorist in her negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The director was driving a village-owned vehicle when he collided with the motorist. The motorist filed a negligence action outside of the one-year statute of limitations for commencement of civil injury actions against local governmental employees contained in the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 8-101 (1987). On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the circuit court for the motorist and remanded the case. The court held that the director raised a valid affirmative defense that the motorist failed to file her action within the time limits of § 8-101 and was entitled to a directed verdict. The court held that § 8-101 applied because the director was acting within the scope of his employment when the accident occurred and the motorist's action was subject to the limitations period under the Act. The director was on-call 24 hours a day, was driving a village vehicle, and was engaged in his usual routine of work duties when the collision happened. The court found that a directed verdict should have been granted because a contrary verdict, in light of the evidence, could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court in the motorist's negligence action against the director and remanded with instructions to grant judgment for the director on his affirmative defense.

People v. Page Books, Inc.


No. 2-91-0243


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


235 Ill. App. 3d 765; 601 N.E.2d 273; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1550; 175 Ill. Dec. 876


September 10, 1992, Submitted  
September 25, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied November 9, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed February 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Donald J. Hennessy, Judge, presiding. No. 89-CM-6929.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for two counts of obscenity pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(a)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a bookstore that sold adult magazines and videos, was convicted for two counts of obscenity after 26 magazines and 5 videotapes were seized during a search of defendant's premises. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the conviction. The court held that the state's decision to charge all the magazines as one count and all the videos as the second count, along with the trial court's decision to submit general, rather than special, verdict forms as to each count, created an impermissible prior restraint. The court found that defendant could not determine which of the magazines or videos were in fact obscene given that the jury was only required to find that at least one was obscene to convict defendant. This uncertainty rendered the procedures unconstitutional. Additionally, the court held that the trial court erred when it included a challenged portion of a pattern jury instruction regarding obscenity as viewed with reference to children without first making a finding that some evidence existed from which the jury might find that the material was specially designed for or directed to an audience of children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for obscenity and remanded the cause for a new trial.

McNulty v. Ill. State Toll Highway Auth.


No. 1-91-3490


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


235 Ill. App. 3d 569; 601 N.E.2d 1252; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1560; 176 Ill. Dec. 554



September 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 1992.As Corrected October 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE EDWARD C. HOFERT, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sought review after the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed counts I, II, and VI of their amended complaint against defendant authority, which arose under the Illinois Toll Highways Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 314a26 et seq. (1953) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The citizens' complaint alleged that the Authority had failed to fix and adjust tolls at the lowest possible rate, thereby unlawfully accumulating and withholding a surplus fund of $ 74 million (count I); that the Authority had wrongfully diverted and misappropriated the Northern Illinois Toll Highway surplus to pay construction costs on a new and separate tollway (count II); and had violated their civil rights under § 1983 (count VI). The trial court dismissed counts I, II, and VI of the amended complaint. The court affirmed. With respect to count I, the citizens had failed to demonstrate with particularity the method in which the surplus funds had been wrongfully diverted or misappropriated, or any unlawful action by the Authority. With respect to Count II, the legislature had intended that tolls and revenues collected from the existing highway system be applied to construction and land acquisition costs for the challenged toll highway. Given the court's affirmation of the trial court's dismissal of counts I and II, count VI, which was premised upon a right of property from which due process had been wrongfully denied, necessarily had to fall.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

941 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Terra-Nova Inv. v. Rosewell


No. 1-91-0281


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


235 Ill. App. 3d 330; 601 N.E.2d 1109; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1488; 176 Ill. Dec. 411



September 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action, plaintiffs, investment company and those similarly situated, appealed the dismissal of its complaint against defendants, county, treasurer, and clerk, by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming that the voluntary payment doctrine did not apply, that they had standing to challenge the state Revenue Act's constitutionality, and that the challenged statute violated their due process and equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court dismissed a complaint against defendants, county, treasurer, and clerk, that challenged the constitutionality of the state Revenue Act (Act), plaintiff investment company appealed. The court affirmed the judgment below, ruling that because plaintiff was not a party at the scavenger sale confirmation proceeding, the complaint was not an impermissible collateral attack. When the bidder-taxpayer became owner of a certificate of purchase after confirmation of a sale and petition for a tax deed, he became a party. Until then, defendant treasurer was the party in the proceedings. The court also held that because plaintiff paid a fee in the scavenger sale process, he had standing to challenge the statutory scheme related to the fee proceeds. The court ruled, however, that the Act was constitutional. A strong presumption of constitutionality accompanied a state's scheme of taxation which was overcome only by a clear showing that it was arbitrary and provided an unreasonable classification, and plaintiff did not overcome that presumption. The transfer of money accumulated in one fund into a general revenue fund was within the legislature's authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below that dismissed plaintiff investment company's complaint against defendants, county, treasurer, and clerk, although the complaint was not a collateral attack on a previous proceeding nor barred by the voluntary payment doctrine and plaintiff had standing, the Revenue Act was constitutional.

Woodard v. Krans


No. 2--91--1008


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient brought suit against defendants, doctor and hospital, alleging that as a result of their negligence she contracted tuberculosis from the doctor while he was performing electroshock therapy upon her. The Circuit Court of Winnebego County (Illinois), dismissed her complaint, stating that she had failed to submit a certificate of merit and medical report in compliance with state rules of civil procedure. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: A patient's complaint against a doctor and hospital for negligently causing her to contract tuberculosis was dismissed by the lower court. On appeal, the patient claimed that the medical report requirements of Ill. Code Civ. P., 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 2-622 were unconstitutional, and that the trial court erred in refusing to grant her discovery of certain medical records, in refusing leave to submit an amended medical report, and in holding that one of the counts sounded in malpractice rather than ordinary negligence. The court held further that (1) the patient failed to support her argument that the lower court erred in refusing to allow her to discover certain medical records with any authority, (2) where the patient failed to tender proposed amendments that might cure her failure to comply with the medical report requirements, the lower court did not abuse its discretion in refusing leave to amend the report, and (3) where the standard of care in preventing the spread of infectious diseases in a hospital was not simply a matter of lay knowledge, the patient's cause of action sounded in malpractice.

People v. Joyce


No. 2--90--0229


Appellate court of Illinois, Second District


234 Ill. App. 3d 394; 599 N.E.2d 547; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1426; 174 Ill. Dec. 763


July 8, 1992, Submitted  
September 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Philip L. DiMarzio and the Hon. Joseph McCarthy, Judges, presiding. No. 88-CF-58



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for child abduction under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted based on his attempts to lure a 14-year-old girl into his truck while she was walking home from school. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court rejected defendant's argument that the child abduction statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1987), created an unconstitutional mandatory presumption by presuming unlawful intent upon proof of the statute's other elements. The court held that para. 10-5(b)(10) instead created a permissive inference, because proof of the other elements merely constituted prima facie evidence of unlawful intent, and the statute placed no restraint on the trier of fact's ability to accept or reject that inference. The court held that the trial court properly found unlawful intent on defendant's part where the inference was supported by corroborating evidence of his guilt. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a continuance for defendant to obtain an evaluation of his sanity, because the case had been pending for a long time and defendant had been competently represented by counsel. The court also rejected defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Piat


No. 2--91--0755


Appellate court of Illinois, Second District


234 Ill. App. 3d 262; 599 N.E.2d 563; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1435; 174 Ill. Dec. 779


February 11, 1992, Submitted  
September 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. David M. Hall, Judge, presiding. No. 91-TR-26445



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Secretary of State challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County, Traffic Division (Illinois), that ordered the issuance of a judicial driving permit (JDP) to appellee driver following the secretary's discretionary suspension of his driving privileges.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was summarily suspended following a motor vehicle accident for which the driver was arrested and charged with driving under the influence of alcohol. On the same date, the secretary ordered a discretionary suspension of the driver's privileges. The circuit court ordered the secretary to issue a JDP. The court reversed, finding that the secretary's discretionary suspension under Ill. Rev. Stat. 1989, ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-206(a)(31) was not a suspension for which a JDP could be issued because it was not mandated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1 (1989). A JDP could have been granted only for statutory summary suspensions issued pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1 (1989). The suspension of the driver's privileges by the secretary, pursuant to his discretionary powers set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. 1989, ch. 95 1/2, para. 6-206(a)(31) was effective during the duration of the period of the JDP.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that required the secretary to issue a JDP to the driver.

 

945 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Haist v. Wei Wu


No. 1--90--0716


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


235 Ill. App. 3d 799; 601 N.E.2d 927; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1437; 176 Ill. Dec. 229



September 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Allen A. Freeman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband of decedent sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded a verdict in the husband's favor on his suit against appellee physician under the Wrongful Death Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 1-2 (1981), but awarded the husband no damages. The physician cross-appealed the trial court's denial of his motion for a directed verdict on the issue of causation.


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the physician negligently failed to inform the wife of her life-threatening condition, while the physician claimed that the wife refused to give a telephone number and insisted on contacting him for results from her medical tests. On appeal, the husband argued the trial court erred in its rulings regarding contributory negligence and by allowing evidence violating the Dead Man's Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 8-201 (1989). The court held that the trial court correctly refused to apply comparative negligence or grant a directed verdict on contributory negligence and noted that wrongful death claimants who contributed to the death of another were different than common law tort victims and not entitled to recover benefit for their wrongdoing. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to establish that the husband's negligence contributed to his wife's death. The court held that the Dead Man's Act was not violated because the husband had opened the door to the physician's testimony on his communications with the wife. The court also found sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict that the physician's conduct was a cause of the wife's death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which awarded the verdict to the husband and awarded him no damages due to his contributory negligence in his wife's death.

Pidgeon v. State Bd. of Elections


No. 4--91--0586


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


234 Ill. App. 3d 490; 600 N.E.2d 858; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1412; 175 Ill. Dec. 615



September 3, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Sue E. Myerscough, Judge, presiding. No. 91CH84



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voter appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted a motion to dismiss, filed by defendant board of elections, the voter's complaint alleging the that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 103-7 (1989), which governed the election of members of the board of trustees of a community college district that was contiguous to an experimental community college district, violated the Illinois Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The voter filed a complaint alleging that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 103-7 (1989) constituted special legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 and constituted an impermissible delegation of legislative authority to an administrative board in violation of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. The circuit court granted the state board of elections' motion to dismiss the voter's complaint. The voter appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that there was at least one rational basis for Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 103-7 (1989), that there was no reason why the legislature had to change every community college district at once as it sought to remedy the "evil" of at-large elections, and that the court was to defer to the discretion of the Illinois General Assembly where it saw fit to designate an administrative board as the appropriate body to determine electoral boundaries for the community college district's new single-member electoral districts. It was conceivable that the legislature sought to remedy the "evil" of at-large election districts in order to avoid requiring the district to litigate the appropriateness of such electoral districts in federal court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the voter's challenge on state constitutional grounds of a state statute governing the election of a community college board of trustees.

Robles v. Chicago Transit Authority


No. 1-90-3217


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


235 Ill. App. 3d 121; 601 N.E.2d 869; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1389; 176 Ill. Dec. 171



September 1, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE STEPHEN A. SCHILLER, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, found in favor of plaintiff decedent's representative on her wrongful death and survival claims against defendant transit authority. The transit authority appealed the verdict, and the decedent's representative appealed the interest awarded on the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the decedent was 65 percent negligent. The court allowed the transit authority to supplement the record on appeal because the decedent's representative would not have been prejudiced. The court noted that there was testimony that the bus accelerated while the rear doors were open, which would not have occurred if the interlock system had been functioning properly, and the jury was free to find in favor of either side. The court held that the decedent's contributory negligence did not preclude the representative from prevailing on res ipsa loquitur claims. While the finding of 65 percent contributory negligence appeared to be inconsistent with the rationale behind the element of control, the analysis focused on whether the transit authority's inferred negligence was, more probably than not, a cause of the injury, though the decedent's negligent acts might also have contributed to his death. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the representative's expert to testify. The court held that the trial court was correct in declining to award prejudgment interest under the Illinois Wrongful Death Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 1 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Johnson v. Owens-Corning Fiberglas Corp.


No. 4--92--0175


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


233 Ill. App. 3d 425; 599 N.E.2d 129; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1347; 174 Ill. Dec. 583



August 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 15, 1992. Released for Publication October 2, 1992. Second Correction November 20, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 89L187. Honorable William T. Caisley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff representative filed an action against defendant company for the wrongful death of her husband as a result of an absestos related disease. The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) entered a default judgment against the company for its noncompliance with a court order to produce two of its employees as witnesses at trial. The company appealed the judgment entered against it and the order denying its motion for post-trial relief.


OVERVIEW: The company was ordered to produce two of its employees who lived outside of the jurisdiction of the court to be witnesses at trial. The court affirmed the trial court, holding that although it did not have personal jurisdiction of the two witnesses, the order was directed to the company over which the trial court did have jurisdiction. The court held that as long as the order was directed at the corporate defendant rather than the individual employees, the principles of due process were not violated, and the court could sanction the company for its failure to produce its employees. The court held that the imposition of sanctions under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 219(c), 134 Ill. 2d R. 219(c), was a matter within the discretion of the trial court, and a reviewing court would uphold the trial court's decision, absent an abuse of discretion. The court held that pleadings could be stricken only when the stricken pleadings bore some reasonable relationship to the information withheld. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in entering sanctions. The court held that the jury instruction given was within the discretion of the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jusgment of the trial court.

 

950 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rasmussen


No. 2--91--0117


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


233 Ill. App. 3d 352; 598 N.E.2d 1368; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1343; 174 Ill. Dec. 431


July 8, 1992, Submitted  
August 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. Nos. 90-CF-666, 667, 668. Honorable Daniel D. Doyle, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), whose jury convicted defendant of criminal fortification of a residence, unlawful use of a weapon by a felon, possession of a firearm without an owner's identification card, possession of cocaine, possession of cannabis, and possession of a hypodermic needle or syringe. He was sentenced accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first challenged the criminal fortification of a residence conviction under 38 Ill. Comp. Stat. 19/5 (1989). He argued that the statute was vague and that it should not apply to small habitual drug users. Under a search warrant, the police broke down the door to defendant's residence. The door was barricaded by a board and had four deadlocks. The court held that defendant did not meet his burden of clearly establishing the statute's constitutional infirmity. The criminal fortification statute was reasonably designed to promote entry of police into areas used for illegal drug activity, which was a threat to public welfare. The statute was a reasonable exercise of the state's police power, and thus defendant suffered no deprivation of due process. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to find that defendant intended to prevent the officers from entering his residence because of the illegal drugs use. Defendant clearly maintained his residence in a fortified condition. Defendant also challenged his conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon under 38 Ill. Comp. Stat. 24/1.1 (1989). The evidence established that defendant constructively possessed a pistol.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences. The court held that any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crimes of criminal fortification of a residence and of unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon beyond a reasonable doubt.

Square D Co. v. Johnson


No. 1--91--2381


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


233 Ill. App. 3d 1070; 599 N.E.2d 1235; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1338; 175 Ill. Dec. 221



August 25, 1992, Decided  
August 25, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Randye A. Kogan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant Illinois Department of Revenue's cross-motion for summary judgment, finding that state and regional transportation authority (RTA) use taxes were correctly assessed under the Illinois Use Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.1 et seq. The department cross-appealed the trial court's refusal to impose a municipal use tax.


OVERVIEW: The department assessed use taxes on the Michigan corporation's jet, which it bought in Georgia, registered in Michigan, and kept in a hangar in Illinois. The corporation's headquarters were located in an Illinois village, and it had manufacturing and distribution facilities in numerous states and foreign countries. The court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the trial court properly applied the Complete Auto four-part test to determine that the jet should be taxed because current Commerce Clause principles applied where the Act was neither ambiguous nor unclear; (2) the Act's exemption for interstate carriers for hire met the requirements of uniformity because real and substantial differences existed between those who were taxed and those who were not and the classification was reasonably related to a legislative purpose; (3) the jet had to be registered in Illinois because the corporation was an Illinois resident for the purposes of the Illinois Aeronautic Act and the jet did not qualify for the commercial flying exemption; and (4) the jet was not subject to the village's municipal use tax because the jet was used where passengers boarded it, not at the corporate offices.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that state and regional transportation authority use taxes were properly imposed on the taxpayer's corporate jet and that the jet was not subject to the municipal use tax.

People v. Jones


No. 4--91--0610


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


233 Ill. App. 3d 411; 599 N.E.2d 48; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1322; 174 Ill. Dec. 502



August 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 1992. As Corrected November 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 87F950. Honorable James A. Hendrian, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff People of the State of Illinois sought review of an order of withholding entered in the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) against defendant father that did not include a delinquency amount as requested by the state.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition for entry of a child support order against the father. The trial court entered an order requiring the father to pay $ 30 in current support and directing any payor of the defendant to withhold $ 30 per week for current child support, but refused the state's request to include an amount to be withheld toward a potential delinquency because no delinquency existed at the time of the order. On appeal, the court reversed and ruled that § 20 of the Illinois Parentage Act of 1984, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2501 et seq. (1989), imposed a mandatory requirement that all orders of support designate a specific additional amount to be withheld in the event of a delinquency. The court also ruled that this statutory requirement was not an unconstitutional legislative encroachment upon the judiciary. The court noted that, in enacting the statute, the legislature complied with a federal mandate and that 45 C.F.R. §§ 303.100(a)(4), (b)(1) (1986) required that the procedure for income withholding be triggered when the absent parent failed to make payment for one month's support and that the withholding must occur without the need for any further action by the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order of withholding against the father that did not include a delinquency amount as requested by the state. The court remanded the case with instructions to enter an additional dollar amount for any potential delinquency in the order of withholding.

Grigoleit, Inc. v. Board of Trustees of Sanitary Dist.


No. 4--91--0744


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


233 Ill. App. 3d 606; 599 N.E.2d 51; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1323; 174 Ill. Dec. 505



August 24, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 1992. As Corrected November 20, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 88MR23. Honorable Warren A. Sappington, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sanitary district board of trustees challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which reversed its order that revoked appellee company's permit to discharge industrial wastewater into the publicly owed treatment works (POTW).


OVERVIEW: The company applied for a permit to discharge its industrial wastewater. During the application process, the company advised the board that a warrant was required for on-site inspections beyond the manhole designated for checking compliance. A permit was issued and the board attempted to conduct on-site inspections of the property. The company refused the board access and the board responded by revoking the company's permit. The circuit court reversed and found that the permit application allowed the board access to the manhole and the board was not denied access thereto. On appeal, the board argued that the inspections were a condition of the permit. The court agreed and reversed. The board was given statutory authority to condition or prohibit the discharge of industrial wastewater. The court found nothing in the law that granted the company a vested right to continuous discharge in the POTW on its own terms and conditions. Thus, while the company was free to refuse the board access to its facilities, it did so at the risk of having the board revoke its permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and reinstated the board's order.

People v. Horton

Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit for Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a)(2) (1989), and sentenced him to 28 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his girlfriend hosted a small party in his apartment. The guests included an individual later involved in an altercation with defendant, the victim, and three others. DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to 12 years imprisonment for allegedly raping his wife at knife point while the couple was separated. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault.

Nicholson v. The Chicago Bar Ass'n


No. 1--90--2043


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District Second Division


233 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 599 N.E.2d 1132; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1266; 175 Ill. Dec. 118



August 11, 1992, Decided  
August 11, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES M. WEXSTTEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff circuit judge sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the circuit judge's motion for leave to file an amended complaint in the her action against defendant Chicago Bar Association alleging that she was denied due process of the law when the association rated her as "not recommended" for a vacancy on the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The circuit judge sought appointment to a vacancy on the appellate court. As part of the application process, the association evaluated the circuit judge's qualifications and rated her as "not recommended" for the office. The circuit judge brought an action alleging that she was denied due process. The trial court dismissed her complaint. More than 10 months after it was due, the circuit judge filed a motion for leave to file an amended complaint. The trial court denied the circuit judge's motion as untimely. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion because the authority of the trial court to dismiss the action due to failure to abide by orders was necessary to prevent undue delays in the disposition of pending cases. In order to state a cause of action under the Fourteenth Amendment, the association's actions had to be those of a state actor, not merely those of a private association. The circuit judge had no protected liberty interest in obtaining a single position as an appellate judge where other opportunities existed, and the "not recommended" rating did not significantly injure her professional standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which denied the circuit judge's motion for leave to file an amended complaint as untimely, in the circuit judge's action against the association alleging that she was denied due process of the law when the association rated her as "not recommended" for a vacancy on the appellate court.

 

957 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


South Holland v. Chernick


Nos. 1--89--2879, 1--89--2909, 1--90--0134 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


233 Ill. App. 3d 860; 600 N.E.2d 30; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1252; 175 Ill. Dec. 407



August 7, 1992, Decided  
August 7, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LAWRENCE CARROLL, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing complaints against defendant car wash that charged the car wash with violating the village's Sunday closing ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The village filed complaints charging the car wash with violating the village's Sunday closing ordinance. The trial court entered an order granting the car wash's motion to dismiss the complaints on the basis that the ordinance by its express language exempted the washing of motor vehicles from its proscriptions. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the ordinance did not create an exemption. It was apparent that there was a typographical error in the printing of the ordinance. To accept the typographical error required the court to assume that the village, in enacting the ordinance and its amendments, abandoned any effort to maintain internal cohesion and grammatical integrity. The court thus construed the ordinance in accord with the clear intent of the village. However, the court was unable to say with certainty that the car wash had prior knowledge that the village did not intend to provide an exemption for the washing of motor vehicles. Therefore, the trial court on remand could have considered the issue of notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the village's complaints against the car wash for violations of an ordinance. The court remanded the case, with directions that the trial court could on remand consider the issue of whether the car wash had notice that the village did not intend to provide an exemption in the ordinance for the washing of motor vehicles.

 

958 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Lappin v. Costello


NO. 4-92-0009


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


232 Ill. App. 3d 1033; 598 N.E.2d 311; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1239; 174 Ill. Dec. 114



August 6, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 18, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 89L205. Honorable George S. Miller, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a merchant and a corporation, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois). The circuit court dismissed two counts of the second amended complaint filed against defendants, the city and the city attorney, and granted summary judgment in favor of the city and defendant charging police officer on the counts alleging false arrest and violation of civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988.


OVERVIEW: After they received complaints, the police went to a gun show and arrested a merchant for running the show without posting a bond as required under a local ordinance. The merchant and the corporation running the show filed a complaint alleging that the city, the city attorney, and the charging police officer violated their civil rights. They did not name a second city attorney until they filed their second amended complaint, which was more than two years after the arrest. The circuit court dismissed two counts of the complaint because the statute of limitations had run. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the action against the city attorney under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was not timely commenced within two years of the alleged civil rights violation. The court held that the circuit court properly entered summary judgment on the remaining counts because the officers had probable cause to make an arrest and to shut down the show. The court concluded that the merchant and the corporation did not have a cause of action as a matter of law because the arrest was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court dismissing two counts of the second amended complaint against the city attorney and the city and granting summary judgment in favor of the city and the charging police officer.

People v. Gant


No. 1--89--0669


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District Second Division


233 Ill. App. 3d 936; 599 N.E.2d 1086; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1246; 175 Ill. Dec. 72



August 4, 1992, Decided  
August 4, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 12, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WASILEWSKI, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder, armed violence, home invasion, aggravated unlawful restraint, and possession of a stolen motor vehicle. Defendant also appealed from his extended-term sentence for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to all of the crimes except murder, which defendant admitted was committed by his accomplice. The court rejected defendant's contention that his right to effective assistance of counsel was violated because both prongs of the Strickland test were satisfied. First, defense counsel's overall performance was competent and defendant consented to his attorney's legitimate, although impracticable independent crime theory as a defense for murder. Moreover, defense counsel did not concede any fact to which defendant did not admit to the police. Second, defendant was not prejudiced by counsel's performance because the evidence of guilt was overwhelming. The court rejected defendant's contention that the record did not show that he intelligently and knowingly agreed to plead guilty because the recorded proved that he pleaded not guilty. As for defendant's extended term sentence, the court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (1985) was not unconstitutionally vague because it specifically described the conduct that qualified for an extended-term sentence. The court held that the evidence established wanton cruelty.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and extended-term sentence for murder, armed violence, home invasion, aggravated unlawful restraint, and possession of a stolen motor vehicle were affirmed.

National Marine v. EPA


No. 3-90-0814


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


232 Ill. App. 3d 847; 597 N.E.2d 911; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1234; 173 Ill. Dec. 937


September 5, 1991, Submitted  
August 3, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed December 2, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Grundy County (Illinois), which dismissed its complaint for a declaratory judgment and other relief against defendant state Environmental Protection Agency's (EPA) issuance of a notice pursuant to § 4(q) of the Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1004(q) (1991).


OVERVIEW: The state EPA notice stated that it found the release or threat of release of hazardous substances on the corporation's property and determined that action was necessary to prevent any risk to the environment. The corporation alleged that § 4(q) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1004(q) (1991), was unconstitutional, and that the state EPA had acted beyond its statutory authority because contamination was found on only 12 acres of the corporation's approximately 64-acre parcel and the notice related to the entire parcel. The trial court dismissed the action because the corporation failed to exhaust its administrative remedies and refused to review the action by writ of certiorari. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the lack of a preenforcement proceeding did not offend due process, and that preenforcement judicial review was not available under the Act. However, the court held that the gross disparity between the area of alleged actual contamination and the area included in the notice presented a case appropriate for review under common law certiorari and that the trial court's failure to grant such review was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the corporation's action for declaratory judgment and other relief against the state EPA for issuing a notice of contamination.

People v. Johnson

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


231 Ill. App. 3d 412; 595 N.E.2d 1381; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1116; 172 Ill. Dec. 711

July 10, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Released for Publication August 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 89-CF-1091. Honorable Harry D. Hartel, Jr., Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted her of abuse of a long-term care resident in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-19(a) (1987).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of abuse of several long-term care residents as a result of her behavior towards elderly residents of a nursing home during the period that she was employed as a nurse aide. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) pursuant to Ill. Rev. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-19 was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant could reasonably have been expected to understand that the statute proscribed the conduct in which she engaged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

People v. Watters


No. 5-90-0719


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


231 Ill. App. 3d 370; 595 N.E.2d 1369; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1113; 172 Ill. Dec. 699



July 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court, of St. Clair County. No. 88-CF-787. Honorable Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which sentenced him to imprisonment under the sentencing provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(C) (1989), from a judgment of guilty but mentally ill on a charge of aggravated criminal sexual assault, a Class X felony.


OVERVIEW: A mentally retarded defendant was found guilty but mentally ill of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The trial court held that he was eligible for probation but that the mandatory sentencing provisions precluded probation. Defendant was sentenced to prison for six years after a determination that he did not fit the criteria for civil commitment. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing. The court held that the offense's mandatory prison provisions could yield to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 104-26(c)(1) (1989), because the legislature intended that special provisions be made for unfit defendants and gave the trial court sentencing discretion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3(c)(2)(C) (1989). Because punishment should be directly related to the personal culpability of defendant and because the legislature adopted a "least restrictive alternative" approach to sentencing in which probation was the preferred disposition of all offenses for which it was authorized, the court concluded that the trial court erred in ruling that it had no discretion to sentence defendant to probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault but vacated the sentence of imprisonment and remanded the cause for a new sentencing hearing.

City Nat'l Bank v. Vancloostere


NO. 5-90-0668


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


230 Ill. App. 3d 723; 596 N.E.2d 208; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1115; 172 Ill. Dec. 929



July 9, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 89-CH-12. Honorable Richard E. Richman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagors challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which denied their motion to have the circuit court's prior order that confirmed the foreclosure sale set aside on the grounds that the terms of the sale were not fair and that justice was not done by the sale. Plaintiff mortgagee had instituted the action to foreclose on two mortgages it had issued to the mortgagors.


OVERVIEW: On November 17, 1989, the circuit court entered a judgment of foreclosure that specified that the redemption period was governed by § 15-1603(b)(1) of the Illinois Mortgage Foreclosure Law, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 15-1603(b)(1) (1989). The circuit court made an express written finding pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(a), codified at 134 Ill. 2d R. 304(a), that there was no just reason for delaying enforcement or appeal. The court found that the redemption period was set by the November 17, 1989 judgment, which expressly indicated that the redemption period was based on § 15-1603(b)(1). The circuit court's judgment contained the express finding required by Rule 304(a) and, thus, it was a final and appealable order.If the mortgagors believed that the use of § 15-1603(b)(1) was improper, that was when the issue should have been raised. Yet, they did not file a timely notice of appeal from that judgment. The mortgagors were foreclosed from directly attacking the circuit court's decision regarding the applicable redemption period. The court dismissed the appeal because the mortgagors advanced no cognizable basis for a collateral attack on the circuit court's ruling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision, which denied the mortgagors' motion to have the circuit court's prior order that confirmed the foreclosure sale set aside on the grounds that the terms of the sale were not fair and that justice was not done by the sale.

Leask v. Hinrichs


No. 2-91-0671


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


232 Ill. App. 3d 332; 595 N.E.2d 1343; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1085; 172 Ill. Dec. 673


April 24, 1992, Submitted  
July 7, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:   [***1] Released for Publication August 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: DOYLE, INGLIS, McLAREN



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient's representative challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice the patient's representative's negligence suit against appellee doctor for failure to comply with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989) and denied the patient's representative leave to amend her complaint.


OVERVIEW: The patient died from cardiac arrest while hospitalized from injuries received in an accident while alighting from a bus. During discovery, the patient's representative learned that the patient may have been the victim of malpractice and amended her complaint to add claims against the doctor and others. The trial court found that the patient's representative had failed to comply with the requirement of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1989) and dismissed the case against the doctor with prejudice. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the patient's representative waived certain arguments about the sufficiency of the medical reports she filed but, under the circumstances, the trial court abused its discretion because involuntary dismissal with prejudice did not serve the purpose of the statute, which was to deter frivolous medical malpractice suits at an early stage. In so holding, the court noted that nothing in the record indicated that this was a frivolous claim or that the doctor would be unduly prejudiced by allowing the patient's representative to amend her complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the patient's representative's cause of action against the doctor and remanded for further proceedings.

OVERVIEW: Defendant appropriated a car from a parking lot of a corporate center. The vehicle's owner had left the running car unattended while he returned to the building to help his wife. People v. M.D.


No. 2-90-0878


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


231 Ill. App. 3d 176; 595 N.E.2d 702; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1046; 172 Ill. Dec. 341


June 11, 1992, Submitted  
June 30, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 29, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. Nos. 90-CF-54, 90-CF-55. Honorable David L. Smith, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) convicted him for aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted his wife and was convicted of aggravated, criminal sexual assault. On appeal, defendant claimed that the criminal sexual assault statute, which contained a marital exception, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 12-18(c), violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions; that his conviction was reversible error; that the trial court erred in refusing to admit evidence of his wife's prior sexual acts; and that the prosecutor committed reversible error during voir dire. The court held that (1) the statute violated the equal protection and due process clauses; (2) the invalidity of the marital exemption did not affect the validity of the criminal sexual assault, aggravated criminal sexual assault, criminal sexual abuse, or aggravated criminal sexual abuse statutes; (3) the trial court did not err by ruling that the proffered evidence was inadmissible because the determinative issue was whether defendant's conduct was deliberate or accidental; and (4) any error resulting from the prosecutor's questioning during voir dire was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's aggravated criminal sexual assault conviction.

People v. Chandler


No. 1-88-2667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


231 Ill. App. 3d 110; 596 N.E.2d 153; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1007; 172 Ill. Dec. 874



June 26, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed violence and aggravated battery and sentenced him to two concurrent 12-year terms for armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed violence and aggravated battery and sentenced to two concurrent 12-year terms for armed violence. On review, defendant argued that the trial court erred when it allowed the admission of prior consistent statements. The court found that the victims had made consistent statements after their inconsistent ones and that they had the same motive to fabricate their statements when making the prior consistent statements as they did at the trial. Therefore, the court found that the prior consistent statements were not admissible. But the court also found that the admission of the prior consistent statements was harmless error because the victims' testimony was corroborated by other evidence, including the testimony of two witnesses. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred when it failed to consider the mitigating factor that he acted under a strong provocation. But the court found that it was presumed that the trial court considered all mitigating factors. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that convicted defendant of armed violence and aggravated battery was affirmed.
