Haben v. Anderson


No. 3-91-0707


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


232 Ill. App. 3d 260; 597 N.E.2d 655; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 1027; 173 Ill. Dec. 681


April 14, 1992, Submitted  
June 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied and Released for Publication September 3, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied December 2, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, McDonough County, Illinois. No. 90-L-38. Honorable William D. Henderson, Judge, Presiding



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's estate appealed an order of the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, McDonough County, Illinois, dismissing its wrongful death action. Plaintiff alleged that defendants, members of a university club, were involved in "hazing" decedent, pressuring him to drink, and causing his intoxication, from which he died. Plaintiff also alleged that one defendant negligently breached a voluntarily assumed duty to care for decedent.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff decedent's estate alleged that defendants, members of a university club, were involved in "hazing" decedent, causing his intoxication and eventual death. Plaintiff also alleged that one defendant, in whose dormitory room decedent died, breached a voluntarily assumed duty to care for him. Decedent was a "rookie" in a club in which membership was a valued status. The complaint alleged that the initiation violated the Hazing Act (Act), Ill. Comp. Stat., ch. 144, para. 220.9 et seq. (Supp. 1990). The trial court dismissed for failure to plead that drinking was required for initiation, and failure to adequately allege that one defendant assumed a duty. The court reversed, holding it was sufficient to have pled that the club had a de facto drinking requirement. Under the Act, defendants owed decedent a duty to act reasonably to protect him, and it was reasonably foreseeable that injury could have resulted. The court rejected arguments that the Act was unconstitutional and that the cause of action did not apply to individual club members. The court also held that the complaint adequately stated a claim that one defendant negligently breached an assumed duty of care.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal and remanded the cause of action for further proceedings. The court held that the complaint adequately stated a cause of action against defendants, members of a university club, for wrongful death and against one defendant for breach of an assumed duty to care for decedent. The court held that the allegation of a de facto drinking requirement was sufficient to plead a cause of action under the circumstances.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of robbery and sentenced him to seven years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another individual entered a woman's car and robbed her. Defendant filed a motion for a mistrial on the basis that the prosecution improperly used peremptory challenges to exclude three blacks from the jury. The prosecution stated that one venireperson was a lawyer for a public interest group, another had overly strong reaction to alleged racist comments, and another was too sympathetic given her disabled husband. The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed, holding that it would defer to the trial court's findings regarding the credibility of the prosecution's explanations. One juror, a non-black learning disabled teacher, who was accepted by the prosecution, was also a crime victim and therefore, there was a legitimate reason for differentiating this juror from the excluded venireperson. The court vacated defendant's sentence because there was evidence that defendant could be an addict and because the trial court failed to inform him of the option of treatment under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 6360-2 (1989). The court remanded for defendant to be examined by a treatment program and a determination of whether he was an addict or alcoholic.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery. The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for a determination of whether defendant was an addict or alcoholic and eligible for a treatment program.

Waste Management of Illinois, Inc. v. Pollution Control Bd.


Nos. 1-90-2702, 1-90-2818 Cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


231 Ill. App. 3d 278; 595 N.E.2d 1171; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 924; 172 Ill. Dec. 501



June 11, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review of Orders of the Illinois Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Illinois Pollution Control Board (board), adopted new regulations regarding nonhazardous waste landfills. Petitioner landfill challenged those regulations as arbitrary and capricious, in excess of the board's authority, and not in compliance with the applicable law.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the potential for methane explosions was such that the board's action in adopting the monitoring requirement of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 811.310(b)(8)(D)(2), was not arbitrary and capricious. The court held that by incorporating a not yet promulgated list of contaminants into Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 811.310(d)(1)(F), the board rendered that section invalid because there was no opportunity for public hearing on the list. Although the regulation could impact adversely on the development of the gas processing industry, the court held that Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 811.317 - 811.320, related to groundwater monitoring. The court held that the self-insurance test for landfills, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 811.715(d), was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. The court held that Ill. Admin. Code tit. 35, § 813.106(b), which delayed the finality of board decisions, was invalid because it was in excess of the board's statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's order promulgating new regulations for nonhazardous landfills in part, and reversed in part.

People v. DeBusk


Nos. 1-87-3699 and 1-88-0312


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


231 Ill. App. 3d 229; 595 N.E.2d 1156; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 915; 172 Ill. Dec. 486



June 10, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Matthew J. Moran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Co-defendants challenged the judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting the defendants of home invasion, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-11 (1985), armed robbery, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2 (1985), and their consequent sentences. The co-defendants argued that they were denied their right to representation by conflict-free counsel and the armed robbery jury instructions were erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Co-defendants sought review of the lower court judgment convicting them of home invasion and armed robbery. The court held that the trial court erred in denying the second co-defendant's attorney's motion that another attorney be appointed to represent the second co-defendant and that, therefore, the second co-defendant was denied his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to conflict-free counsel. The second co-defendant suffered from the joint representation because he did not have his attorney's exclusive loyalty and was represented by an attorney who was hostile to his own interests. The lower court's failure to appoint separate counsel or take adequate steps to determine whether the risk was too remote to warrant separate counsel constituted reversible error. However, the court held that the first co-defendant was property represented by his own conflict-free attorney. The court held that the jury instructions for armed robbery, which did not include a mental state as an essential element of the crime, were not erroneous. The court affirmed the first co-defendant's convictions and reversed the convictions of the second co-defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the first co-defendant's convictions for home invasion and armed robbery but reversed the second co-defendant's convictions for the identical offenses.

Worth v. Watson


No. 1--90--3095


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


233 Ill. App. 3d 974; 599 N.E.2d 967; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 920; 174 Ill. Dec. 883



June 10, 1992, Decided  
June 10, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 13, 1992. Rehearing Denied September 25, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James F. Stack, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipal corporation appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment in favor of defendant property owners in a municipal ordinance violation case.


OVERVIEW: The municipal corporation charged the property owners with zoning ordinance violations, including an allegation that "junk" had accumulated. In reversing an order granting the property owners summary judgment, the court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. A personal of ordinary intelligence had a reasonable opportunity to know what conduct was lawful or unlawful. In affirming the denial of a preliminary injunction sought by the municipal corporation to remedy allegedly new conditions, the court held that there was no emergency presented by the addition of materials on the property. The denial was not an abuse of discretion. When the municipal corporation sought to amend its complaint prior to the grant of summary judgment, it should have been allowed, since the allegations were similar to those contained in the original complaint, the amendment was timely, and it would have been more efficient to resolve the new allegations in the current litigation rather than to require a new lawsuit. It was not error to allow the property owner to withdraw the defense of estoppel without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The entry of summary judgment in favor of the property owner on the alleged ordinance violation was reversed, and the cause remanded for a determination of whether a violation occurred. The court directed that the municipal corporation be allowed to file an amended complaint adding additional violations on remand. The denial of a preliminary injunction sought by the municipal corporation was affirmed.

People v. Patten


1-91-1593


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


230 Ill. App. 3d 922; 595 N.E.2d 1141; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 898; 172 Ill. Dec. 471



June 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for two counts of child abduction in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-5(b)(10) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached two 10-year-old children, coming close to them while holding his car door open, and asked them to come to him and give him a kiss. On a previous occasion, defendant had approached two 11-year-old children in the same red car and asked them to come here. The 10-year-old children correctly identified defendant in a lineup. At trial, the jury was instructed that if they found that defendant attempted to lure the children into his car without parental consent the jury could infer that it was done for an unlawful purpose. Defendant was convicted of two counts of child abduction, and the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence of the previous crime was admissible because it tended to show modus operandi and identity. The court ruled that the instruction did correctly inform the jury that the presumption of unlawful purpose was rebuttable because the court prefaced the presumption with the word "may." The court held that because the legislature could reasonably find that attempted child abduction was a very serious offense, punishing attempted abduction to the same extent as abduction did not violate defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for two counts of child abduction.

McCarthy v. La Salle Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


NO. 1-90-0696


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

June 5, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ARTHUR DUNNE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, proposed class action representative (representative), appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed her complaint against defendant landlords without prejudice for failing to allege sufficient facts to maintain a class action.


OVERVIEW: The representative contended that the class allegations of her complaint were sufficient to survive a motion to dismiss. The court held that the representative adequately alleged that there was a common question of law or fact that predominated over questions affecting only individual members of the class. The court also held that the representative's alleged common question of law or fact was controverted. According to the court, the class action was properly predicated upon allegations that the proposed class members were aggrieved by the same or similar conduct based on a long series of transactions based on similar acts or documents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

 

976 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Boughton Trucking & Materials, Inc. v. County of Will


NO. 3-91-0738


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


229 Ill. App. 3d 576; 593 N.E.2d 1119; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 885; 171 Ill. Dec. 299


April 16, 1992, Submitted  
May 29, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 30, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County, Illinois. Nos. 91-CH-7278 and 91-L-8057. Honorable William Penn, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Will County, Illinois, which dismissed their actions against defendants, county and town, alleging that they deprived the taxpayers of their civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985(3) for failure to allege exhaustion of administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers owned real estate in the county. They alleged that the county and town unlawfully conspired to increase the assessed valuation of their land and other parcels of real estate that was used for mining and quarrying. They claimed that similar properties used for mining and quarrying in other townships within the county were not reassessed. The taxpayers argued that the county and town deprived them of their civil rights and their right to equal protection. The trial court dismissed the actions. The court affirmed and held that the trial court properly dismissed the complaints for failure to allege exhaustion of the plain, speedy, and efficient remedy available to them. The taxpayers were barred by the principle of comity from asserting 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 actions in federal courts. Because § 1983 actions based on alleged unconstitutional reassessments could not be maintained in federal courts, there was even more reason for requiring and applying the court's own principles of administrative and judicial review, which was a plain, speedy, and efficient remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the taxpayers' actions against the county and town for failure to allege exhaustion of administrative remedies.

Anagnost v. Layhe


1-92-0581


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


230 Ill. App. 3d 540; 595 N.E.2d 109; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 798; 172 Ill. Dec. 46



May 27, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael Murphy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed a decision of the Cook County Officer's Electoral Board sustaining respondent's objections by reason of the Compulsory Retirement of Judges Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 23.71 (1989), to nomination papers filed by petitioner in the Republican primary for the office of Supreme Court Judge.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a licensed attorney over the age of 75 years. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 23.71 (1989) required automatic retirement at the expiration of the term in which a judge attained the age of 75. Respondent argued that the court should treat candidates for a judgeship in the same manner as sitting judges under the Act. The court found that the Act applied only to sitting judges. Impairment of a citizen's right to run for elective office should only have been by specific language barring access to the ballot and authorized in the Illinois Constitution, and the Illinois General Assembly had not enacted legislation that specifically barred a person over the age of 75 from running in a judicial election.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

Hyatt Corp. v. Sweet


No. 1-91-0957


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


230 Ill. App. 3d 423; 594 N.E.2d 1243; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 812; 171 Ill. Dec. 723



May 22, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Mary M. Conrad, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted summary judgment to defendant state department of revenue (department) in the taxpayer's action that challenged the deficiencies of the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act (ROT), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 441 (1989), and interest that were charged by the department in connection with the service charges imposed by the taxpayer for its banquets.


OVERVIEW: The department previously charged the taxpayer with deficiencies of ROT and interest in connection with the service charges it imposed on its banquet customers. For the audit period in question, although the taxpayer collected and remitted the proper amount of ROT on its charges for banquet food and beverages, it did not remit such tax on the service charges imposed in connection with the banquets. The taxpayer paid the amounts at issue under protest and filed an action in the circuit court for a review of the proposed deficiencies. The circuit court granted summary to the department. The court reversed and remanded the order that granted summary judgment to the department. The court held that a service charge was exempt under § 2(e) of ROT if it was mandatory and separately stated on customers' bills. Furthermore, only that portion of the service charge that was turned over to the employees who would have received tips, absent the service charge, was not taxable. The court stated that the taxpayer's use of the monies collected from the service charge to cover the employer's expenses, such as shift pay, did not render those services charges exempt from the tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order that granted summary judgment to the department in the taxpayer's action that challenged the deficiencies and interest charged by the department in connection with the service charges imposed by the taxpayer for its banquets. The court remanded the case, holding that the portion of the service charges that was returned by the taxpayer to its servers, as shift pay, was not exempt from the ROT tax.

People v. Hopkins


NO. 4-91-0711


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


229 Ill. App. 3d 665; 593 N.E.2d 1028; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 782; 171 Ill. Dec. 208



May 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 6, 1992. As Corrected September 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 90CF564. Honorable Wayne C. Townley, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling from the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of burglary pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1(a) (1989) and sentenced defendant to seven years in prison.


OVERVIEW: A black man and a black woman entered the owner's store and conversed with the owner, who was working the cash register. The couple then drew the owner away from the cash register, asking questions about the merchandise. Defendant entered the store wearing a red baseball cap and removed money from the cash register. The owner yelled at defendant, who quickly left the store. The man and woman also left; the owner ran out, flagged down a police car, and reported the crime. Defendant, the man and woman, and another person were apprehended riding together in a car; defendant had changed to a blue baseball cap. The trial court convicted defendant of burglary, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the jury could easily have concluded that none of the three people entered the store for any reason other than for defendant to steal money from the cash register. Defendant went immediately to the cash register upon entering the store. Defendant and the first people to enter the store rode in the same car immediately after the burglary. Police found defendant's red baseball cap under the seat in which defendant rode. Defendant gave a false name to police.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary and remanded the cause to adjust defendant's sentence to give credit for time served while awaiting trial.

Schickler v. Santa Fe Southern Pacific Corp.


No. 1-90-0320


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


229 Ill. App. 3d 291; 593 N.E.2d 961; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 751; 171 Ill. Dec. 141



May 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE HAROLD A. SIEGAN, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway company bondholders sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting appellee railway company and trust company's motion to dismiss the bond holders' action for breach of contract due the railway company's failure to pay the semi-annual interest due on the bond in gold coin or its equivalent as required by the terms of the bond and breach of fiduciary duty by the trust company.


OVERVIEW: Bondholders filed suit against a railway and a trust company as successor trustee under the indenture created at the time of the issuance of the bonds. The bondholders contended that the railway had breached its contract by failing to pay the semi-annual interest due on the bond in gold coin or its equivalent as required under the terms of the bond and alleged the trust company had breached its fiduciary duty in allowing others to make interest payments in cash rather than in gold. The bondholders sought to permanently enjoin defendants from making interest or principal payments on the bonds in any other form other than gold coin or its equivalent, and sought compensatory damages for defendant's failure to make such payments. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting the railway and trust companies' motion to dismiss the suit and concluded that the Joint Resolution of 1933, or Abrogation Act, declared void the gold clauses in these bonds. The court held that the Act was a legitimate exercise of Congress's constitutional power over the monetary of the system and the exercise of such power did not depend upon the economic circumstances which precipitated its passage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting a railway company and a trust company's motion to dismiss the bondholders' suit for breach of contract due the railway company's failure to pay the semi-annual interest due on the bond in gold coin or its equivalent as required by the terms of the bond and breach of fiduciary duty by the trust company.

In re Estate of Sutherland


No. 1-91-0588


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


229 Ill. App. 3d 281; 593 N.E.2d 955; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 759; 171 Ill. Dec. 135



May 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Frank M. Siracusa, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition to file a claim against an estate because the claim period had expired. Administrator appellee did not notify him by mail of the statutory deadline for filing claims. The creditor argued that the notice provisions of § 18-3(a) of the Probate Act, which required only notice by publication, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The creditor argued that he did not receive sufficient notice under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Ill. Const. art. 1, § 2 of the proceedings in the estate to afford him an opportunity to file his claim before the running of the claims limitation period. The creditor helped the decedent manage certain real estate and provided services after the decedent's death. The administrator sent the creditor a notice of a petition to sell estate securities. On appeal, the court found that the creditor received actual notice of the probate proceeding that might affect his rights as a creditor in time for him to take appropriate steps to protect them. The creditor made no effort to file his claim until 10 months after the Letters of Office had issued to the administrator and 4 months after the claim period expired. The court held that his failure to timely file was not the result of the insufficiency of the actual notice, but the result of his failure to timely act. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which found that his failure to timely file was not the result of insufficiency of actual notice, but the result of his failure to timely act on the notice received.

People v. Hammer


No. 2-91-0500


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


228 Ill. App. 3d 318; 591 N.E.2d 554; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 737; 169 Ill. Dec. 381


April 14, 1992, Submitted  
May 13, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1992. Released for Publication May 29, 1992


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 90-CF-2190. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful possession of weapons by a felon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1.1(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: While responding to a domestic disturbance, the police found guns in the marital bedroom. Defendant contended that his conviction for unlawful possession of weapons by a felon based on constructive possession violated his due process rights because it was lawful for his wife to own the guns in that she had a firearm owners' identification card (FOID). The court affirmed the conviction because defendant was the actual owner of the guns, the wife never used them, she applied for a FOID at her husband's suggestion as a subterfuge to avoid the fact that defendant could not be issued a permit due to his prior conviction, and defendant admitted to a police officer that the weapons were "his guns." Thus defendant did much more than merely sleep in the house where his wife kept the guns. Accordingly, findings that defendant knew of the guns and that they were under his dominion and control did not offend due process. Defendant waived his argument against the admission of his son's testimony regarding prior conversations concerning the guns and, in any event, the evidence was relevant to show that defendant knew of the guns' existence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of weapons by a felon.

People v. Mitchell


1-89-2232


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 917; 593 N.E.2d 882; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 730; 171 Ill. Dec. 62



May 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Allowed October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Will E. Gierach, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(b)(1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault for sexually assaulting his nine-year-old niece. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial, holding that the trial court erred by allowing an assistant state's attorney to testify regarding out-of-court statements made by defendant's niece and her mother. The trial court erred by failing to hold an Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10(b)(1) hearing to determine the reliability of the niece's out-of-court statement. The trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury about the weight and credibility of the niece's statement as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10(c). The trial court also erred by allowing the attorney to describe the mother's out-of-court statements about the niece's remarks as the attorney did not hear the niece's remarks personally as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-10(a)(2). Finally, the trial court erred by refusing to hold a hearing concerning plaintiff's use of peremptory challenges where it used its first five challenges to excuse males.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded because the trial court erred by allowing an assistant state's attorney to testify regarding out-of-court statements made by defendant's niece and her mother as it failed to hold a reliability hearing, failed to instruct the jury, and the attorney had not personally heard the niece's statements.

People v. Carpenter


No. 1-90-3120


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 899; 593 N.E.2d 817; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 696; 170 Ill. Dec. 928



May 6, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Daniel J. Lynch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of reckless homicide, driving under the influence of alcohol, and driving on a suspended driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in an automobile accident that killed a child and injured two others. Defendant was convicted of reckless homicide, driving under the influence of alcohol, and driving on a suspended driver's license. Defendant asserted that his first blood test was inadmissible because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.4 unconstitutionally conflicted with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 236, 134 Ill. 2d R. 236, testimony regarding his second blood test was improper, and his blood tests were improperly admitted as expert opinion. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and held that Ill. Rev. The court ruled that defendant waived the issue of chain of custody of his second blood sample because he did not object at trial to the sufficiency of the chain of custody. The court also held that defendant waived the issue of expert testimony because he did not argue or support his claim by citation to relevant authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of reckless homicide, driving under the influence of alcohol, and driving on a suspended driver's license.

People v. Lauderdale


No. 1-91-0667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 830; 593 N.E.2d 757; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 678; 170 Ill. Dec. 868



April 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Paul T. Foxgrover, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the count of the indictment charging defendant with aggravated criminal sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was indicted on one count of aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14-(a)(2) (1989) and one count of criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14-(a)(1) (1989), filed a motion to dismiss the aggravated criminal sexual assault count on the ground that the injuries alleged, bruising and abrasion to the victim's vaginal wall and destruction of her hymen, did not warrant enhancement of the charge. On appeal of the trial court's order granting the motion, the court reversed. The court ruled that the definition of "bodily harm" under the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute included injuries to the victim's sexual organs, that the legislature intended that the term "bodily injury" be given a broad interpretation, and that the injuries alleged were adequate to charge defendant with aggravated criminal sexual assault. The court concluded that the vaginal injuries suffered by the victim were not the normal incident of a criminal sexual assault, as claimed by defendant, and thus could have served to enhance the offense charged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to dismiss the count of the indictment charging defendant with aggravated criminal sexual assault and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Sesmas


No. 3-91-0623, Consolidated with No. 3-91-0627


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County. No. 91 CF 5. Honorable James J. Wimbiscus, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, passenger and driver, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois), which denied their motion to suppress the evidence found in a false compartment in the gas tank of their car, entered a judgment of conviction for drug trafficking, and imposed sentence.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court denied defendants' motions to suppress the evidence found in a car they were driving cross-country. After trial the circuit court entered a judgment of conviction for drug trafficking and imposed sentence. Defendants appealed. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence because it found that: 1) the passenger did not have standing to challenge the search of the car because he had no reasonable expectation of privacy in the car; 2) there was no evidence that the driver was coerced into giving her consent to the search because it was clear that she adequately understood the situation and she was not pressured to consent; 3) the continued detention after the issuance of the warning citation was not an illegal seizure because the continued detention was consensual and of reasonable duration; 4) the scope of the search was reasonable; 5) use of the officer's prior testimony to assess his credibility was harmless error because it did not affect the outcome; 6) there was sufficient evidence to support a finding that defendants knowingly possessed the drugs; and 7) the punishment provided for in the statute was proportionate to the offense and was constitutional.

People v. Goodey


NO. 4-91-0605


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


227 Ill. App. 3d 232; 591 N.E.2d 102; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 603; 169 Ill. Dec. 222



April 15, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 22, 1992. Released for Publication April 15, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 91CF94. Honorable Jerry L. Patton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) convicting him of delivery of a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(7)(ii) (1989) and criminal drug conspiracy in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1405.1(a) (1989) and sentencing him seven and one half years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of delivery of a controlled substance, 10 or more segregated parts of an object containing in them any amount of lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD), and of criminal drug conspiracy, in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act. The trial court sentenced defendant, and on appeal, the court affirmed in part and remanded. The court held that § 1401(a)(7)(ii) was not unconstitutionally vague because it was drafted in consideration of the means by which LSD was packaged and sold. LSD was commonly packaged in sheets, which were objects, that contained perforated units, which were segregated parts. Thus, § 1401(a)(7)(ii) sufficiently gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice of the prohibited conduct. The court also found that the state submitted sufficient evidence to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the court determined that defendant was entitled to have his street-value fine reduced by a credit for every day he spent in custody prior to his sentencing pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-14 (1989) and remanded to the trial court for amendment of his sentencing order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for delivery of a controlled substance and remanded with directions to enter an amended sentencing order.

Carbondale Liquor Control Comm'n v. Illinois Liquor Control Comm'n


Consolidated No. 5-90-0779


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


227 Ill. App. 3d 71; 590 N.E.2d 1044; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 590; 169 Ill. Dec. 125



April 14, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 90-MR-44. Honorable J. Phil Gilbert, Judge Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 90-MR-46. Honorable J. Phil Gilbert, Judge Presiding.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 90-MR-45. Honorable J. Phil Gilbert, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three consolidated cases, appellant, a local liquor control commission, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which ruled that the local commission had no standing to appeal the final orders of the appellee, the Illinois Liquor Control Commission (State Commission), in favor of three local applicants for liquor licenses.


OVERVIEW: The State Commission had reversed the local commission's decision to deny liquor licenses to the applicants. The local commission filed complaints for administrative review. The circuit court struck the complaints on the basis that the local commission lacked standing to seek administrative review. The court affirmed the decision. The court reasoned holding that the local commission was not a party aggrieved by reversal of its own administrative decision because it was a quasi-judicial body, and it had not been given a statutory grant of authority to seek administrative review. The court disagreed with the local commission's contention that it did not act in a quasi-judicial capacity and that the case relied upon by the circuit court did not apply. The argument lacked merit because it failed to consider the local commission's primary role. By statute, the local commission exercised quasi-judicial powers and had the authority to conduct hearings on complaints. The court concluded that the local commission's responsibility to protect the public interest did not authorize it to act as a representative of the public for the purpose of vindicating its own decision on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order striking the local commission's appeal of the State Commission's decisions to grant liquor licenses to the three applicants.

Gabriel v. Columbia Nat'l Bank


No. 1-91-0282


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 240; 592 N.E.2d 556; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 563; 170 Ill. Dec. 120



April 10, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Arthur Dunne, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant joint tenant sought review of a judgment on the pleadings from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was granted to plaintiff excluded sister in her action for fraud and reformation of a land trust. Defendant invoked her privilege against self-incrimination as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. V and Ill. Const. art. I, § 10 in her verified answer to plaintiff's allegations of forgery.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff excluded sister brought an action against defendant joint tenant for fraud and reformation of a land trust, alleging that defendant forged a land trust document assigning plaintiff's share of certain real estate to defendant and plaintiff's mother as joint tenants. Defendant invoked her privilege against self-incrimination as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. V and Ill. Const. art. I, § 10 in her verified answer to plaintiff's complaint. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to plaintiff and defendant appealed. The court reversed the judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that judgment on the pleadings based upon defendant's invocation of the state constitutional privilege against self-incrimination in her answer to allegations of forgery was a violation of the privilege. The court concluded that the pleading requirements for answers in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-610 (1989) yielded to the constitutional right to avoid self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the pleadings in favor of plaintiff excluded sister and remanded the case for further proceedings. Judgment on the pleadings based upon defendant joint tenant's invocation of the state constitutional privilege against self-incrimination in her answer to plaintiff's allegations of forgery was a violation the privilege.

 

991 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mays


No. 1-90-0243


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


230 Ill. App. 3d 748; 595 N.E.2d 1088; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 546; 172 Ill. Dec. 418



April 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992. As Corrected July 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FORM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MICHAEL B. GETTY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for the offenses of attempted murder, aggravated battery, and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed and beat a tow truck driver. Defendant contended on appeal that his statement to the police was involuntary because prompted by physical coercion, that he had not been proved guilty of attempted murder, and that his sentences were improper. The court affirmed the judgment. The court stated that there was no evidence establishing that defendant suffered any injury while in police custody, and that ample evidence supported the finding that defendant made the statement voluntarily. The court found that the prosecutor's failure to investigate defendant's allegation that the police hit him, in light of the other contradictory evidence, did not constitute a denial of due process. The court stated that the question of intent was for the trier of fact, and that it was unable to say that the trial court's express finding that defendant specifically intended to kill the victim was error. The court rejected defendant's claims that his conduct supported only one conviction, and that the trial court's failure to state in the record its opinion that a consecutive term was necessary to protect the public rendered the consecutive sentences improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant.

 

992 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collier


No. 1-89-1350


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 159; 592 N.E.2d 444; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 481; 170 Ill. Dec. 8



March 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE JAMES M. BAILEY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him, after a bench trial, of attempted first degree murder and armed violence, contending that the statute creating the offense of first degree murder violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment. Defendant also alleged that the sentence imposed was excessive and should be vacated or reduced.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial of attempted first degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 8-4, 9-1 (1985) and armed violence , in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 33A-2 (1985). He appealed, contending that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9-1, 9-2 (1985), which created the offense of first-degree murder, were unconstitutional. Defendant also contended that the sentence imposed by the court of 16 years imprisonment was excessive and should be vacated or reduced. The court affirmed the convictions, finding that ch. 38, paras. 9-1, 9-2 did not violate the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court concluded that the sentence imposed was not excessive because it was not manifestly disproportionate to the nature of the offense and the record reflected that the trial court took into consideration defendant's age, education, background, employment status, family status, and lack of a significant criminal history when determining the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant for attempted first degree murder and armed violence and concluded that the sentence was not manifestly disproportionate to the nature of the offense.

 

993 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carter


No. 1-89-1015


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 526; 592 N.E.2d 491; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 483; 170 Ill. Dec. 55



March 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992. As Corrected August 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable James Heyda, Judge Presiding



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment entered after he was found guilty by a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for aggravated battery and robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the verdict for aggravated battery, premised upon use of a deadly weapon, was inconsistent with the jury's implicit rejection of the use of a dangerous weapon in the commission of the robbery, that the statute that permitted the sentencing court to impose a more severe sentence upon a defendant who committed an offense in a place of worship violated the Establishment Clause of U.S. Const. amend. I, that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was subject to Class X sentencing, and that the court erred in permitting the state to present certain rebuttal evidence. In affirming the circuit court's judgment, the court found that 1) the verdicts were not inconsistent, 2) Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(a)(10) (1989) did not violate the Establishment Clause of U.S. Const. amend. I, 3) Class X sentencing was proper, and 4) testimony was proper rebuttal and thus its admission was not abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

994 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 1-91-0074


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


228 Ill. App. 3d 163; 592 N.E.2d 514; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 531; 170 Ill. Dec. 78



March 31, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MARY JANE THEIS, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated arson and sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him and that the arson statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20-1.1 (1987), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated arson, a violation of ch. 38, par. 20-1.1. The trial court sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment and defendant appealed, contending that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him and that ch. 38, para. 20-1.1 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, finding that the statute, as amended, was constitutional because it incorporated the elements of arson, which necessarily included the mental state of knowledge. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant, even though at the time of sentencing he was 65 years old. The evidence established that defendant had lived in the subject premises, an apartment building, and knew that children and a severely retarded person resided there. The evidence indicated that defendant set the fire at night, when most of the residents were asleep, which resulted in many of them awakening when the building was already engulfed in flames and required them to jump out windows to save themselves. The court concluded that the crime was shocking and horrifying and that the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence imposed against defendant following his conviction for aggravated arson and found the arson statute constitutional.

 

995 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 1-88-0700


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 917; 592 N.E.2d 389; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 459; 169 Ill. Dec. 902



March 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE WILL E. GIERACH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for possession of an automobile certificate of title without complete assignment pursuant to the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-104(a)(2) (1985). Defendant alleged that the statute violated due process because it failed to require a culpable intent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after he produced the title to a car that had been reported stolen. The signature on the title was a forgery and the owner denied selling the car. However, the owner's nephew allegedly sold the car and forged the owner's signature, telling defendant that he was the true owner. The court reversed defendant's conviction, finding that he did not have the requisite criminal intent needed for a violation of § 4-104(a)(2). The court found that the statute was constitutional because it had been interpreted as requiring such criminal knowledge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of an automobile certificate of title without complete assignment.

 

996 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Witt


No. 1-89-0516


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 936; 592 N.E.2d 402; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 529; 169 Ill. Dec. 915



March 30, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE GINO L. DIVITO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of first degree murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1987), following a jury trial. Defendant claimed that an amended murder statute was unconstitutionally applied to him as an ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his conviction was invalid as first degree murder, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1 (1987), because the statute was not in effect at the time of the offense. The court determined that the statute was not invalid as being an ex post facto law and affirmed the conviction. Prior to July 1, 1987, the state had the burden to prove, beyond a reasonable doubt, the elements of murder. The defendant then had the opportunity to present evidence of a factor in mitigation, serious provocation or unreasonable belief, either of which must have been present to reduce an offense of murder to voluntary manslaughter. The amended statute did not change the elements of the crime, but it defined the offenses of first and second degree murder, and shifted the burden of proof to a defendant, to prove by a preponderance of the evidence, one of the factors in mitigation to reduce an offense of first degree murder to second degree murder. However, in this case defendant did not attempt to prove a mitigating factor, he relied instead on an alibi defense so the change had no effect on the defense and the new statute did not criminalize behavior that was previously lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction.

 

997 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Mazur v. Hunt


No. 1-89-2473


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 785; 592 N.E.2d 335; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 454; 169 Ill. Dec. 848



March 27, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ODAS NICHOLSON, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured filed an action against defendants, insurer and agents, asserting fraud in obtaining proof of loss for stolen jewelry. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion to dismiss filed by the insurer and the agents. The insured appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured argued that he was induced into signing the proof of loss that failed to include all of the pieces of stolen jewelry. The insured asserted that the lower court erred when it ruled that § 155 of the Illinois Insurance Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, par. 767 (1987), preempted his claim of fraud. The court found that the insured failed to plead any additional damages from the alleged fraud, and thus the conduct was preempted by § 155 of the Insurance Code. The statute preempted the insured's claims for compensatory and punitive damages because the damages were recoverable under the policy.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the claim of fraud was affirmed.

 

998 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People v. Johnson


No. 1-89-3361


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


227 Ill. App. 3d 800; 592 N.E.2d 345; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 448; 169 Ill. Dec. 858



March 27, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE WILL E. GIERACH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for first degree murder and sentence of 28 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 28 years' imprisonment for first degree murder. The court found that, in viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, the trial court could have found the essential elements of first degree murder beyond a reasonable doubt. Sufficient evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant did not believe the victim was threatening him with imminent death or great bodily harm when he shot the victim, given that the shot entered the back of the victim's head, no weapons were found on the victim, and testimony revealed the victim was running away when shot. The court ruled that defendant's Sixth Amendment right to conflict-free counsel was not violated by the trial court's refusal of defendant's last minute request to appoint counsel other than his private counsel because the trial court made sufficient inquiry into defendant's claims and was not obliged to honor the request. The court ruled that the trial court erred in its belief in sentencing defendant that the crime was drug related because no one testified that defendant or the victim was involved in drug dealings, or that the argument between them was drug related.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for a new sentencing hearing.

 

999 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


Midland Enters. v. City of Elmhurst


No. 2-91-0300


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


226 Ill. App. 3d 494; 589 N.E.2d 1019; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 417; 168 Ill. Dec. 619


March 3, 1992, Submitted  
March 20, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 23, 1992. Petition for Leave to Appeal Denied October 7, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 88-CH-150. Honorable Carl F.J. Henninger, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City of Elmhurst Building Department and the Illinois Department of Transportation, Division of Water Resources (DWR), sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied the DWR injunctive relief under § 18f of the Rivers Act. The DWR sought a mandatory injunction against appellee company to remove two berms and a lift station that it constructed adjacent to its properties on the Salt Creek.


OVERVIEW: The company built a shopping center and a berm to control flood waters. It also constructed a hotel directly to the north. Before the hotel was complete, the DWR granted the company a permit that excluded the construction of a berm and did not include a lift station. The DWR was not aware that the lift had been built or that a berm was later built. The DWR sought a mandatory injunction for the removal of the shopping center berm and amended the claim for the removal of the hotel berm and lift station. On appeal, the court held that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to review the permit conditions because the company failed to seek administrative review of the permit conditions within the required 35-day period. The court reversed the portion of the circuit court's order denying the DWR injunctive relief as to the hotel berm. The court also reversed the decision of the circuit court, holding that it erred in applying general equitable principles when it refused to issue a statutory injunction as to the construction of the lift station. It affirmed the circuit court as regards to the shopping center berm because the DWR was not diligent in requiring the company to remove it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying a mandatory injunction as to the remaining shopping center berm. The court reversed the trial court's order denying the DWR injunctive relief as to the hotel berm and reversed the trial court's decision not to enjoin the construction of the lift station.

 

1000 of 1262 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Wray v. Brassard


NO. 4-91-0281


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


226 Ill. App. 3d 1007; 589 N.E.2d 1012; 1992 Ill. App. LEXIS 380; 168 Ill. Dec. 612



March 19, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 24, 1992. As Corrected May 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Douglas County. No. 75D57. Honorable Dan L. Flannell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Illinois Department of Public Aid (department), filed a petition for adjudication of contempt on behalf of the wife, asking that defendant husband be held in contempt of court for failure to pay child support and seeking child support arrearage. The Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois) ordered that the statute of limitations barred the collection of a large portion of the payments. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the entry of the divorce decree wherein the husband was ordered to pay weekly child support, he made no child support payments. The husband argued that the appeal was untimely filed as it was based on the prior order addressing the barring of arrearage pursuant to the five-year statute of limitations in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-205 (1987). The department claimed that the 20-year statute of limitations applicable to judgments contained in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 13-218 (1987) applied to the divorce decree. The court reversed the trial court's decision, holding that: (1) the appeal was timely because the there was no Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304 finding as to the prior order and thus it was not appealable as it did not dispose of all of the department's claims against the husband; and (2) the trial court erred as a matter of law in applying the five-year statute of limitations to the arrearage because the 20-year limitation on enforcement of judgments was applicable. The court noted that the department's pleadings seeking the payments originally ordered by the divorce decree were sufficient to effect revival of the decree.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment finding that collection of certain arrearage of child support owed by the husband was barred by the five-year statute of limitations.
